801 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Mohave Disposal v. City of Kingman


1 CA-CV 93-0428


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


184 Ariz. 368; 909 P.2d 435; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 167; 195 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



July 27, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County. Cause No. 92-CV-947. The Honorable Leonard C. Langford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona), which denied its motion for summary judgment and granted appellee city's motion to dismiss its action for compensation for lost business in an annexed area of the city. The trial court ruled that the refuse collection service provided by the corporation was not a public utility service within the meaning of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-516.A.


OVERVIEW: The city annexed a previously unincorporated area where the corporation had been providing refuse disposal services. The city's trash collection fee was imposed on the area's residents, and the corporation lost customers. It filed an action against the city seeking compensation for its lost business on the ground that refuse disposal was protected by § 9-516.A as a public utility service. The trial court denied the corporation's motion for summary judgment and granted the city's motion to dismiss. The corporation appealed. The corporation was not a public service corporation within the meaning of Ariz. Const. art. 15, § 2 because refuse disposal was not among the services or products described in that section. The corporation was not a public utility service pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-516.A. That term did not include all business affected with the public interest. The corporation was not a political subdivision of the state. It did not offer the type of service or product provided by public service corporations, nor would competition lead to abuses detrimental to the public interest. The city was not required to purchase or condemn the corporation's property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment which denied the corporation's motion for summary judgment and granted the city's motion to dismiss its complaint seeking compensation for lost business in an annexed area of the city.

 

802 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Chadwick v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 95-0100


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


184 Ariz. 190; 908 P.2d 4; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 159; 195 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



July 25, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on December 19, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-95-0415-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 95-04370. The Honorable Jeffrey S. Cates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teacher sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied his petition for special action that his dismissal hearing pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-549 (1991) be stayed pending resolution of a criminal case against him alleging sexual conduct with a former student.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was indicted on several counts of sexual conduct with a minor, one count of sexual abuse, and one count of child molestation. Real party in interest governing board of the school district sent the teacher a notice of their intention to dismiss him. It then denied the teacher's request that the dismissal hearing be stayed pending resolution of the criminal charges. Upon filing his petition for special action, the trial court held that the was no abuse of discretion on part of the board and that the teacher had no enforceable right, warranting injunctive relief. On appeal, the court found no error and denied the teacher's relief. The board argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-549 vested it with the discretion to place a teacher on paid leave pending resolution of a criminal case but did not require that it did so. The teacher argued that his Fifth Amendment privilege entitled him to a stay of the dismissal hearing pending resolution of the criminal case. The court held here there was no penalty if the teacher invoked the Fifth Amendment because of the board's assurances that his silence during the administrative investigation or hearing was not going to be held against him.


OUTCOME: The court denied the teacher's request that his dismissal hearing be stayed pending resolution of the criminal case against him.

 

803 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


City of Tucson v. Wolfe


2 CA-CR 94-0229, 2 CA-CR 94-0230 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


185 Ariz. 563; 917 P.2d 706; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 163; 195 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 54



July 25, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected Per Order Dated August 7, 1995. Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by the Arizona Supreme Court May 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause Nos. CR-43858 and CR-43856 (Consolidated). Honorable Gilbert Veliz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgments from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted them of indecent exposure under Tucson, Ariz., Ordinance § 11-25.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were employed as dancers in a nightclub that featured exotic entertainment when they each received a "clothing requirement violation" citation from the city after they removed opaque material covering the nipple and areola portions of their breasts. On review, the court held that Tucson, Ariz., Ordinance § 11-25.1 did not violate the state and federal guarantees of equal protection under the law because it prohibited females, but not males, from exposing the nipple and areola regions of their breasts. As both courts below held, given the community standard for "decency" expressed by the community's legislatures both local and statewide, the ordinance was substantially related to an important governmental interest in regulating the public decency and order. As applied to female nightclub entertainers and servers, the additional clothing requirement of § 11-25.1 was narrowly drawn and not unduly burdensome that mandated only that females cover the nipple and areola portions of their breasts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions of indecent exposure.

 

804 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Colonial Life & Accident Ins. v. State


1 CA-CV 93-0580


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


184 Ariz. 533; 911 P.2d 539; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 152; 194 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



July 11, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on February 21, 1996 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-95-0424-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 93-22020. The Honorable Michael O. Wilkinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED and REMANDED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County, (Arizona) that granted appellee insurer declaratory and injunctive relief in an action seeking to prevent the state from requiring the insurer to competitively bid for group insurance contracts for state employees.


OVERVIEW: For a period of approximately seven years, an insurer sold insurance to state employees via pre-tax payroll deduction without having to compete for a contract from the state, as required of other insurance companies. The state sought to terminate this privilege, and the insurer filed a special action in superior court seeking a judgment declaring that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 38-612(B) (1994) exempted it from the competitive bidding requirements. The trial court granted the insurer declaratory and injunctive relief agreeing with an attorney general opinion that § 38-612(B) conferred a special privilege on the insurer. The court reversed, holding that § 38-612(B) protected the right of state employees to pay premiums on existing insurance policies with pre-tax payroll deductions and that it did not confer a special privilege on the insurer regarding the sale of new insurance to state employees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the declaratory and injunctive relief granted to the insurer.

 

805 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Weinstein


1 CA-CR 94-0093


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


182 Ariz. 564; 898 P.2d 513; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 135; 193 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



June 20, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 93-92406. The Honorable David L. Roberts, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed a theft by extortion charge against defendant on the ground that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-1804(A)(6), under which defendant was indicted, was unconstitutionally overbroad because it encompassed a substantial amount of protected speech. The state argued that § 13-1804(A)(6) was a valid enactment that prohibited "blackmail."


OVERVIEW: After defendant wrote a letter to his landlord threatening that defendant was going to take certain action, such as sending press releases to the media regarding the landlord's alleged criminal activities, unless the landlord refunded defendant's security deposit, defendant was indicted for theft by extortion. The trial court dismissed the charge on the ground that § 13-1804(A)(6) was unconstitutionally overbroad. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that § 13-1804(A)(6), which made criminal not only protected political threats, but also threats common in everyday business and personal interactions, was unconstitutionally overbroad because it criminalized expression protected by the First Amendment. The court refused to encroach upon the legislature's power to determine what acts constituted crimes. The court held that reading a requirement of a "wrongful" threat into § 13-1804(A)(6) would not have saved the statute because adding the term "wrongful," which would not have informed the public what conduct was prohibited, would have made the statute void for vagueness. Thus, the court held that § 13-1804(A)(6) encompassed a substantial amount of protected speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that dismissed a theft by extortion charge against defendant.

 

806 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Zamora v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 94-0324


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


183 Ariz. 470; 904 P.2d 1294; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 131; 192 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 67



June 15, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 94-04807. The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED ORDER VACATED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, individual charged with two counts of aggravated driving while under the influence (individual), filed an application to review the decision of respondent Superior Court of Maricopa County (superior court) (Arizona), which denied the individual's motion to strike the allegation of historical prior felony convictions. The superior court granted a stay of the individual's trial to pursue special action review with the court.


OVERVIEW: The individual argued that his prior felony convictions could not have been used to enhance his sentence because neither conviction fit within the plain meaning of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604(U) (Supp. 1994), the statute was unconstitutionally vague on its face, and the prior convictions were invalid because they resulted from an illegal plea agreement and sentence. The court accepted jurisdiction and granted the relief requested. The court held that § 13-604(U)(1)(a) applied to prior felony convictions that mandated a term of imprisonment and that fell within one of the listed categories. Because the individual's previous felony convictions did not fall within any of the statutory categories, the convictions could not have been used for enhancement. The court also held that the individual's prior convictions were erroneously held to have been repetitive offenses with one prior felony conviction. Therefore, the superior court's denial of the individual's motion to strike was vacated.


OUTCOME: The court granted the individual's requested relief and vacated the superior court's order that had denied the individual's motion to strike the allegation of historical prior felony convictions.

Araiza v. U.S. West Business Resources


1 CA-CV 93-0393


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


183 Ariz. 448; 904 P.2d 1272; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 121; 191 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



May 30, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 91-04037. The Honorable Sherry Hutt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) granted appellee special employer's motion for summary judgment, finding that appellant employee was an employee of the special employer and that the actual employment relationship was controlling regardless of the contract terms used between the special employer and the temporary services employer. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employers operated under a contract by which the temporary services employer furnished employees to work at the special employer's premises. The employee knew that he was an employee of the temporary services employer rather than the special employer. The employee suffered permanent injury while working at a cable stripping machine on the special employer's premises. The employee filed an action in tort against the manufacturer and distributor of the machine and added the special employer as a defendant, alleging that the special employer was negligent in making changes or modifications to the cable stripping machine, in failing to properly train the employee on the operation of the machine, and in failing to warn of the dangers of the machine. The court held that the true nature of the relationship of the parties was that of employer and employee; therefore, the special employer enjoyed the immunity from tort liability afforded to employers under Arizona law. Further, the court held that the employee was not entitled to bring a third-party claim under the contract, and that certain provisions of the workers' compensation act as applied to him were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment in favor of the special employer was affirmed.

 

808 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Frazer, Ryan, Goldberg, Keyt & Lawless v. Smith


1 CA-CV 93-0225


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


184 Ariz. 181; 907 P.2d 1384; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 111; 190 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 6



May 11, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on December 19, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-95-0279-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 91-04203. The Honorable Elizabeth P. Arriola, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff creditor, a law firm, brought a successful collections suit against defendant debtor, a former client. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) entered a judgment granting the creditor the right to garnish assets of the debtor and permitted a writ of garnishment against a checking account at garnishee bank. The debtor appealed the judgment allowing the writ.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the judgment was correct under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 33-1131, 12-1598.10. Although § 33-1131 limited the percentage of earnings that could be garnished and § 12-1598.10 lowered that percentage more in cases of hardship, monies deposited in a bank ceased to be "earnings" when they were paid by the employer pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-15098.01(A), 12-1570(6). These monies were subject to garnishment under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1570.01(A)2. Although the debtor argued that this interpretation of earnings eviscerated the earnings protection of §§ 33-1131, 12-1598.10, the court held the clear language of the statutes, the legislative history, and analogous federal law all illustrated that the earnings protections did not extend to earned monies disbursed to the debtor's bank account.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the garnishment judgment, granting a writ of garnishment against the debtor's checking account to the creditor.

Lathrop v. Arizona Bd. of Chiropractic Examiners


1 CA-CV 93-0310


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


182 Ariz. 172; 894 P.2d 715; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 99; 189 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



April 25, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Memorandum Decision Redesignated Opinion and Ordered Published April 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 92-13301. The Honorable Stanley Z. Goodfarb, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff chiropractor appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which affirmed the revocation of his chiropractic license by defendant Arizona State Board of Chiropractic Examiners (Board). The Board found that the chiropractor had engaged in unprofessional conduct and conduct which constituted a danger to the health, welfare, or safety of a patient, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 32-924(A)(5), (15).


OVERVIEW: Patients went to the clinic after seeing a weight loss advertisement but were given unnecessary x-rays and inadequate examinations by the chiropractor's. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court found, inter alia, that (1) the record supported the Board's findings of fact and conclusions of law as to the chiropractor's conduct because it was replete with evidence of misconduct, such as unnecessary x-rays and insufficient examinations; (2) the Chiropractic Act was not unconstitutionally vague, because it contained standards by which the Board could assess professional conduct; (3) the license revocation was not an excessive penalty because it was not so disproportionate to the offense as to shock one's sense of fairness where revocation was a permissible sanction for even a single statutory violation; (4) it was not an abuse of discretion to allow one of the state's experts to offer expert testimony where the witness was a licensed chiropractor who had been in practice for more than six years, and (5) the chiropractor was not denied due process where a witness was not compelled to give expert testimony because the witness had been designated as a fact witness only.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and the Board's revocation of the chiropractor's license.

R.L. Augustine Constr. Co. v. Peoria Unified Sch. Dist. No. 11


1 CA-CV 93-0107


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


183 Ariz. 393; 904 P.2d 462; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 98; 189 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



April 25, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 91-17068. The Honorable William P. Sargeant, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant construction company challenged a summary judgment granted appellee school board by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona). The construction company asserted that the Procurement Code as set forth in Ariz. Admin. Code R7-2-1155 to -1184 was unconstitutional and denied the construction company due process in a hearing procedure.


OVERVIEW: A construction company entered into a contract with a school board for a project. When the project was not completed on time, the school board assessed liquidated damages. The construction company objected and submitted its claims to the school board pursuant to the Procurement Code, Ariz. Admin. Code R7-2-1155 to -1184. The school board found in its own favor; the construction company appealed and was granted a hearing before a hearing officer appointed by the school board. The school board prevailed again and the construction company filed suit. The trial court granted summary judgment to the school board, finding that the construction company had not exhausted its remedies under the Administrative Review Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 12-904 to -914. The trial court rejected the contention that the Procurement Code was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found that the Procurement Code was unconstitutional as violative of due process because the school board had an interest in the outcome and was able to dictate the outcome in its unilateral selection of the hearing officer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the cause, finding the Procurement Code unconstitutional, and remanded the action to the trial court.

State v. Smith


1 CA-CR 94-0283-PR


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


183 Ariz. 424; 904 P.2d 1248; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 90; 188 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 39



April 11, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review from the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Rule 32.9(c), Arizona Rules of Criminal Procedure). Cause No. CR 92-0727. The Honorable James B. Sult, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVIEW GRANTED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a pro per petition for review of a decision from the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief in which he asserted that his sentence of 10 years imprisonment imposed for his conviction for theft was cruel and unusual punishment. The superior court granted defendant's attorney permission to withdraw prior to the disposition of defendant's petition for review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of theft and was sentenced to an aggravated term of 10 years in prison. Defendant sought post-conviction relief under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 32, contending that the sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The trial court denied defendant's petition finding that no material issue of fact or law existed to grant relief. Defendant then filed a motion for appeal of the sentence, which the trial court treated as a petition for review. In addition, defendant's attorney filed and was granted a petition for withdrawal form the case. Subsequently, defendant filed a pro per petition for review. On review, the court ruled that defendant's sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment because he had 19 prior convictions, which justified the aggravated 10 year term. However, the court concluded that defendant's case had to be remanded to the trial court because he was denied the constitutional and fundamental right to counsel during his appeal as the result of his attorney being permitted to withdraw prior to a final disposition.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant's sentence of 10 years in prison for a theft conviction was not cruel and unusual punishment. Nevertheless, the court was compelled to remand the defendant's claim that the sentence was cruel and unusual punishment because his fundamental right to counsel during the appeal was denied.

 

812 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanderson


1 CA-CR 92-1715


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


182 Ariz. 534; 898 P.2d 483; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 82; 187 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



April 4, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on June 29, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-95-0230-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Apache County. Cause No. 2790, The Honorable Michael C. Nelson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for one count of child molestation under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-604.01 from the Superior Court of Apache County (Arizona), arguing, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying his challenges to the composition of the jury pool and jury panel on the basis that they violated the U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for child molestation, concluding that he failed to establish a prima facie violation of his right to a jury representing a fair cross-section of the community as required by the Sixth Amendment. The conclusion that Native Americans were a distinctive group within the county and were underrepresented on the jury panel was not dispositive because the underrepresentation was not the product of systematic exclusion. Defendant failed to support his argument that Native Americans were underrepresented on the master jury list because they registered to vote at a lower rate than other county residents do. Further, the trial court's conclusion that granting excuses based on an inability to understand English was easily supported because, although it was an inappropriate basis for qualification for jury service, it was an appropriate ground to be excused from service. Further, the excusing of reservation residents on the basis of transportation difficulties was not systematic. The criterion was implicitly authorized by statute as an excuse for hardship, was facially neutral, and, was applied sparingly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for child molestation.

 

813 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Young ex rel. Young v. DFW Corp.


2 CA-CV 94-0103


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


184 Ariz. 187; 908 P.2d 1; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 84; 187 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 58



April 4, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellees' Petition for Review DENIED. Justice Martone voted to grant the Petition for Review.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY. Cause No. CV 91-03738. Honorable Jonathan H. Schwartz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents on behalf of their injured child, sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which rendered judgment in favor of appellee taproom in the parents' action for injuries that their child suffered when she was struck by an automobile.


OVERVIEW: The accident in which the child was injured occurred when her parents' car was struck head-on by an intoxicated driver. The driver had a blood alcohol of .20, and she had been served alcohol at the taproom on the night of the accident. The court reversed the judgment, holding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-312, upon which the trial court had instructed the jury, was unconstitutional. Section 4-312 restricted the jury's consideration of the evidence to a determination of whether the driver was so impaired by alcohol as to visibly affect her ability to function, such that a reasonable person would infer that she was intoxicated. The court held that under Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 6, legislation could not abrogate a right of action for injuries. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-312 abrogated such a right by preventing the jury from considering other evidence from which intoxication could have been inferred under common law as it existed prior to the enactment of § 4-312. The driver did not appear intoxicated, but evidence showed that she consumed many drinks and the taproom was not crowded. A jury could have inferred from that evidence that the driver was intoxicated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the verdict and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

814 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Hyatt Regency Phoenix Hotel Co. v. Winston & Strawn


1 CA-CV 92-0133


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


184 Ariz. 120; 907 P.2d 506; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 58; 185 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



March 7, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on December 19, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-95-0281-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. CV 87-39216 and CV 89-10586 (Consolidated). The Honorable Susan R. Bolton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL: AFFIRMED, CROSS APPEAL: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, partnership, corporation, and others, filed an action against defendant law partnership, alleging that an attorney with the law partnership acted negligently and breached its contractual and fiduciary duties to them in an unrelated litigation. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) rendered judgment in favor of the partnership, and both the law partnership and the partnership appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the law partnership argued, inter alia, that it could not have been liable for punitive damages because it was a wholly passive employer. The court held that § 13 of the Uniform Partnership Act, codified at Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 29-213 (1989), imposed vicarious liability on partners for damages that were punitive in nature. Thus, the law partnership was vicariously liable in punitive damages for acts of the attorney that were performed in the ordinary course of the partnership's business. The court further held that there was substantial evidence that the law partnership proximately caused the partnership to sustain actual damages in the unrelated litigation and that the jury could have reasonably concluded that but for the law partnership's legal malpractice, the partnership could have could have significantly reduced its liability in the litigation. Moreover, the award satisfied the predicate requirement for an award of punitive damages because the jury's finding that the attorney acted with an evil mind was reasonably supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for compensatory and punitive damages against the law partnership but reversed part of the trial court's award of credit for partial satisfaction against the judgment. The court remanded the matter to the trial court for entry of judgment in accordance with its opinion.

 

815 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


WIDGER v. ARIZONA DEP'T OF REVENUE


No. 1 CA-TX 93-0005


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


183 Ariz. 296; 903 P.2d 604; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 269; 188 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 60



February 23, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 15, 1995. Redesignated as Opinion April 13, 1995. Redesignated as Opinion Reaffirmed May 12, 1995. Review Denied September 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court, Cause No. TX 90-00080, The Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged an order from the Arizona Tax Court, which dismissed their action for a partial refund of property taxes and denied their motion for new trial. Appellees, Arizona Department of Revenue, county, and county tax officials, filed a cross-appeal from a portion of the tax court's opinion that found the amending act of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-506 was unconstitutional to the extent it retroactively amended the statute.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers owned a portion of agricultural land as to which a subdivision plat had been recorded splitting the property into small parcels. The land was never developed and was continually farmed. The tax assessor assessed the taxpayers' land as vacant residential subdivision lots, following the policy that a parcel could not quality as agricultural land unless it contained a minimum of 20 acres. The taxpayers sought a declaration that their parcels had been erroneously assessed as nonagricultural property and a refund of overpayments of taxes made on the nonagricultural assessments. The tax court held that the taxpayers had no claim for relief under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-506, and that amendments to the statute could not be retroactively applied. On appeal, the court affirmed. The valuation decision that resulted in individual nonagricultural valuation for all the taxpayers' lots despite their combined use as a farming operation was not an erroneous assessment for which relief could be granted under the statute. Relief was available under the statute only for assessment errors that were clear and indisputable without the need for resolution of contested issues of fact or law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the taxpayer's action for a partial refund of taxes and did not reach the issue of whether the retroactive amendment of the tax law was unconstitutional.

 

816 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Home Builders Ass'n v. City of Scottsdale


1 CA-CV 92-0210


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


183 Ariz. 243; 902 P.2d 1347; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 35; 184 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



February 16, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV-87-31929. The Honorable William P. Sargeant, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee developers petitioned the Arizona Supreme Court to grant review the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), and the state supreme court remanded to the court to review the claims in light of a United States Supreme Court decision. The underlying cause regarded the charge of development fees by defendant city.


OVERVIEW: The court was required to consider whether the newly decided case had any effect on its prior opinion. In analyzing the effect of that case the court first considered whether the fees charged by the city implicated the power of eminent domain. If the fees constituted a land-use regulation, eminent domain would have been implicated. If the fees were a tax, however, they would not have been subject to the Takings Clause. The court found that the payment of the fee was a condition to the city's issuance of a building permit and the fee was for the express purpose of providing future water to the subject property. Thus, the fee was to be used to benefit the property on which the fee was imposed, rather than for general revenue and was a regulatory fee rather than a tax. Because the development fee ordinance was more akin to a land-use regulation than a tax, it was subject to the Takings Clause. Because the city's development fees involved a legislative, rather than adjudicative, determination, the court concluded that the new case did not control the outcome of the case and did not affect its prior opinion.


OUTCOME: The court upheld its prior decision.

 

817 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Olea


1 CA-CR 93-0069


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


182 Ariz. 485; 897 P.2d 1371; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 19; 183 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



February 2, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED on July 11, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-95-0180-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County Cause No. CR-92-01861 The Honorable Gregory H. Martin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted defendant for use of a narcotic drug in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408(A)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a county employee, took his county car to the county maintenance facility to be repaired and cleaned. While it was being cleaned, a prisoner on a work program found a bag of cocaine in the car. Defendant, in an effort to prove his innocence, submitted to drug testing. The drug test was positive and was confirmed by an independent lab. Defendant had his own urine test performed several days later and a hair test performed several months later and both were negative. Defendant was convicted for use of a narcotic drug in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408(A)(1). On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that: (1) a conviction under § 13-3408(A)(1) did not require an independent showing that the defendant used a "usable" amount of a narcotic drug; (2) the trial court correctly concluded that its amendment of the indictment by removing the reference to a specific amount of cocaine was technical in nature and did not prejudice defendant; (3) the language in § 13-3408(A)(1) is sufficiently clear to apprise ordinary citizens of the prohibited conduct; and (4) it was a harmless error to reject the results of defendant's drug test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for illegal use of a narcotic drug.

 

818 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sigro


1 CA-CR 93-0681


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 8; 182 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



January 17, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Redesignated a Memorandum Decision by Order of July 3, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 196.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-93-05236. The Honorable Frank T. Galati, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) of solicitation to possess narcotic drugs. Defendant appealed form his conviction and sentence, contending that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence of two lumps of "crack" cocaine found as a result of a pat-down search and in failing to consider his inability to pay a probation services fee pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901(A).


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err. Defendant testified that he approached the officer. The officer testified defendant was free to leave. The voluntary, consensual encounter with the officer did not implicate Fourth Amendment safeguards. The first prong of the plain feel test was satisfied because a pat down search of defendant was justified, as the officer was aware that many people in the high crime area carried small knifes in their pockets. Thus, the officer was lawfully positioned to feel the crack cocaine. The second prong was satisfied because due to his experience and training, the two asymmetrical lumps were immediately recognizable by the officer as crack cocaine. The third prong was satisfied because the pat-down search ended as soon as the officer recognized the crack cocaine. At that point defendant was arrested and the subsequent search of defendant's pocket was a search incident to a lawful arrest. Thus, suppression of the crack cocaine was not warranted. Defendant's failure to object to the imposition of the probation fee at trial was fatal to that claim on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and defendant's sentence were affirmed.

State v. DePiano


1 CA-CR 92-1855


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


187 Ariz. 41; 926 P.2d 508; 1995 Ariz. App. LEXIS 3; 181 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 16

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) convicted defendant of two counts of child abuse in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-3623(B)(1) (1989) and imposed consecutive sentences of 17 years each. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police found defendant and her children in defendant's car with the engine running in the garage, which was filled with smoke and exhaust fumes. Defendant was convicted for child abuse. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) there was substantial evidence in the form of expert testimony and documentary evidence that defendant's children were likely to die or to be seriously injured as a result of the carbon monoxide levels and concomitant oxygen depletion in the garage; (2) the failure to object to evidence of prior bad acts at the time of trial waived the assertion and failed to preserve the claim for appellate review; (3) defendant's objection to the introduction of lay opinion testimony was foreclosed when defendant had first introduced the lay opinion testimony; and (4) defendant's failure to object to the prosecutor's closing argument waived the assertion on appeal. The court held that the imposition of two consecutive 17-year sentences was not unconstitutionally cruel and unusual. The sentences were not grossly disproportionate in light of the fact that defendant intentionally attempted to murder her children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for child abuse and the sentence of two consecutive 17-year sentences.

State v. Moerman


1 CA-CR 93-0674, 1 CA-SA 93-0276, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


182 Ariz. 255; 895 P.2d 1018; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 256; 179 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



December 13, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on May 23, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-95-0058-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal/Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. LC 93-00368 and LC 93-00366. The Honorable Norman D. Hall, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a special action and appealed from their convictions and sentences, $ 100 fines each, for violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(A)(1) (Supp. 1992), misconduct involving weapons, a class one misdemeanor. Respondent Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) affirmed the convictions and sentences entered by respondent municipal court. Defendants argued that the statute was unconstitutional and was misapplied to their situations.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were carrying guns inside fanny packs that were designed specially to carry concealed weapons. The court found that Ariz. Const. art. II, § 26 provided not an absolute right, but instead a qualified one in which the right of the individual citizen to bear arms in defense of himself or the state should not be impaired. The court found that although Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102 might limit the right to bear arms, it neither frustrated nor impaired it. The court concluded that § 13-3102 was constitutional. The court found that the legislature intended to prohibit a person from carrying a concealed weapon on his or her person in a manner readily accessible for immediate use unless the conveyance utilized to carry the weapon reasonably would place others on notice that such person was armed. The court found that fanny packs did not give such notice, such as a conspicuously carried holster or scabbard. The court affirmed and concluded that a "fanny pack" was not a "case" for purposes of § 13-3102(F), which exempted application of § 13-3102(A)(1).


OUTCOME: The court denied relief to defendants and affirmed their convictions and sentences.

Soos v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 94-0068


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


182 Ariz. 470; 897 P.2d 1356; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 254; 179 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 22



December 8, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on July 11, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-95-0049-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. DR 93-07297 and DR 93-14461 (Consolidated). The Honorable Pamela J. Franks, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father filed a petition for special action from the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which declared the surrogate parentage contracts statute unconstitutional and ordered an evidentiary hearing to determine which person would be the better mother of triplets bore by a surrogate.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother contracted with a surrogate to carry their offspring. During the pregnancy, the mother filed to dissolve the marriage. The father responded that he was the biological father and that, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-218 (1991), the surrogate was the legal mother. The children were born and an order was entered naming the father the natural father; he took custody. The mother attacked the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-218(B) (1991), and the trial court agreed. The father filed a petition for special action. The court accepted jurisdiction and denied the father's requested relief, finding that the statute violated the Equal Protection Clause of the United States and Arizona Constitutions. A parent's right to the custody of a child was a fundamental interest; therefore, although a gender-based distinction was at issue, the statute was tested against a strict scrutiny analysis. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-218(C) allowed a man to rebut the presumption of legal paternity but did not provide the same opportunity for a woman. By providing dissimilar treatment, the statute violated the Equal Protection Clause. The state did not show any compelling interest.


OUTCOME: The court accepted jurisdiction and denied the father the relief he sought.

State v. Gates


1 CA-CR 91-1637


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


182 Ariz. 459; 897 P.2d 1345; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 211; 174 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



September 27, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied May 8, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-94-0405-PR. Reported at: 1995 Ariz. LEXIS 44.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 91-03691. The Honorable Gregory H. Martin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), for sexual exploitation of a minor and for a dangerous crime against children in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-3553(A)(1) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction on a charge of the sexual exploitation of a minor in violation of § 13-3553(A)(1). The charge, which was based on three home videotapes, required proof that appellant made a film in which minors were engaged in sexual conduct. The relevant statutory definition of sexual conduct under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §13-3553(2)(f) meant the lewd exhibition of the genitals, pubic, or rectal areas of any person. The court reversed and remanded with directions to enter a judgment of acquittal. The court concluded that none of the minors in appellant's videotapes were engaged in sexaul conduct within the meaning of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-3553. Two of the tapes showed the normal, nonsexual conduct of children changing clothes or taking a shower in what they thought was a private setting. The third tape frequently focused on the genitals and pubic areas of minors, but the photographic images used as material for the third tape depicted children engaged in normal, nonsexual conduct that was appropriate for the age and activity being photographed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for the sexual exploitation of a minor was reversed and the matter was remanded with directions to enter a judgment of acquittal.

Davis v. Cessna Aircraft Corp.


1 CA-CV 91-0216


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


182 Ariz. 26; 893 P.2d 26; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 208; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,038; 174 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



September 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on April 25, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-94-0502-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. CV-87-38359 and CV-87-38360. The Honorable Philip W. Marquardt, Judge. The Honorable Sherry Hutt, Judge. The Honorable Albert M. Goldberg, Judge, Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff surviving parents appealed an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant power company on the negligence claims in the wrongful death action, dismissed the strict liability claim against defendant aircraft corporation, and entered judgments on the jury verdicts in favor of aircraft corporation and defendant manufacturer on negligence and products liability claims.


OVERVIEW: As an initial matter, the court held that power company was entitled to summary judgment, finding that although it owed a duty of care to the decedents, its failure to marks its power lines did not create an unreasonable risk of harm to normally operating aircraft and thus its conduct was not actionable negligence. The court further found that because surviving parents failed to produce evidence from which reasonable people could have concluded that manufacturer's engine was defective, the trial judge should have granted a directed verdict for manufacturer on the duty to warn claim. In addition, the court then held that the trial judge committed reversible error in admitting the National Transportation Safety Board's probable cause conclusion. The court concluded by finding that because of recent developments in caselaw that held Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-551 unconstitutional, the trial judge had erred by dismissing the strict liability claim against aircraft corporation and such a claim was thus still viable against that party.


OUTCOME: Although the court affirmed the judgment in favor of manufacturer, as well as the summary judgment in favor of power company, it reversed the judgments in favor of aircraft corporation and remanded those matters for a new trial on surviving parents' strict liability, negligence, and products liability claims.

Kerr v. Waddell


1 CA-TX 92-0010


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


183 Ariz. 1; 899 P.2d 162; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 205; 173 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 50



September 13, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Arizona Tax Court Cause No. TX 89-01153. The Honorable Kenneth W. Reeves III, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; VACATED IN PART; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), granted appellant taxpayers partial relief on their challenge to Arizona's scheme of taxation of governmental retirement plan contributions, denied their claims for refunds and for injunctive relief, and granted summary judgment to appellee director and assistant director of appellee Arizona Department of Revenue on the taxpayers' claim for 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 damages. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers claimed that the state's scheme for income taxation of mandatory contributions to federal, state, and local governmental retirement plans violated the doctrine of intergovernmental tax immunity codified in 4 U.S.C.S. § 111. The trial court granted the taxpayers partial declaratory relief, denied their claims for refunds and injunctive relief, and held that the Arizona Department of Revenue's director and assistant director enjoyed qualified immunity on the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim for damages. On appeal, the court held that the taxpayers, who were subjected to discriminatory taxation, had an enforceable right under § 1983; that their failure to exhaust administrative remedies barred their refund claims, but not their § 1983 claims for damages and injunctive relief; that Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 43-1001(2) and 43-1022(2) were unconstitutional; and that the director and the assistant director were entitled to qualified immunity. The court also held that, in light of its holding that § 43-1001(2) was unconstitutional, the request for injunctive relief required further consideration, including consideration of legislative compliance with the mandate of equal treatment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, vacated in part, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Oakley


1 CA-CV 92-0420


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


180 Ariz. 34; 881 P.2d 366; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 187; 172 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 55



August 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County. Cause No. CV 92-0344. The Honorable Michael Irwin, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee board member sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which ruled that the board member vacated office by moving out of the district from which the board member was elected. Appellee state had filed an action to require the board member to vacate office.


OVERVIEW: When elected, the board member lived in the district from which he was elected to serve on the Board of Governors of the Yavapai Community College. In the interim, new election districts were approved and the board member moved to a house that was located in the new district; however, the house was not within the old district. The trial court found that the new boundaries were not in effect when the board member moved; thus, he ceased to reside in his election district and, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 38-291(5), he could not continue to serve on the board. The board member argued that the statute that created the new election districts was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court concluded that (1) the adoption of the boundaries of an election district was a legislative act, and the authority to establish community college election districts was delegated to the board of supervisors by statute; (2) the board largely was free to fashion districts as it saw fit; (3) the legislature was free to set qualifications for members of the board of governors of a community college district; and (4) Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15-1441(A) was not inconsistent with Ariz. Const. art. 7, § 15.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling that the board member vacated his office.

DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, employer and worker's compensation carrier (carrier), sought review of a decision of the Arizona Industrial Commission (commission) that awarded worker's compensation benefits to a claimant and denied their request for apportionment of the permanent partial disability compensation award under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23-1065(C) (Supp. 1993).


OVERVIEW: The administrative law judge (ALJ) awarded the worker's compensation benefits to the claimant and denied petitioners' request for apportionment of the permanent partial disability compensation award. This determination was rested on the fact that although the claimant's cervical arthritis and either bilateral hand arthritis or occipital neuralgia were preexisting nonindustrial physical impairments rating 10 percent or more under the guidelines, the written record requirement was not satisfied as to the bilateral hand arthritis. Further, the court determined that the written records requirement applied to the claimant's impairment from bilateral hand arthritis, but the employer failed to satisfy the requirement. Thus, the court affirmed the decision that denied apportionment.


OUTCOME: The commission's award of worker's compensation benefits was affirmed.

Third & Catalina Assocs. v. City of Phoenix


1 CA-CV 93-0337


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


182 Ariz. 203; 895 P.2d 115; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 176; 63 A.L.R.5th 879; 171 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 63



August 18, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on May 23, 1995, by Arizona Supreme Court CV-94-0503-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 92-12347. The Honorable Edward C. Rapp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commercial building owner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment to appellees, city, city council, and fire department (city), and affirmed the city's denial of the owner's requested exemption or major variance from a city ordinance requiring that all buildings over 75 feet tall be retrofitted with sprinkler systems.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued on appeal that the sprinkler retrofit ordinance was an unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation because of the great expense and difficulty in retrofitting a building that contained asbestos. The owner also argued that the ordinance violated constitutional equal protection clauses because it exempted residential buildings and that its enforcement violated due process. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the city. The court also held that, given the extensive administrative procedures that addressed the owner's complaint, the owner had not been subjected to a violation of procedural due process. The court found no equal protection violation in exempting residential buildings and held that the exemption was supported by the differences in use and occupancy between commercial and residential buildings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the city and held that the sprinkler retrofit ordinance as applied to the owner was not unconstitutional.

In re Appeal in Maricopa County, Juvenile Action No. JT9065297


1 CA-JV 93-0053


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


181 Ariz. 69; 887 P.2d 599; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 172; 171 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 50



August 17, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 23, 1994. Petition for Review Denied on January 24, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-94-0403-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Superior Court Cause No. JT 9065297. The Honorable John L. Popilek, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) found that appellant juvenile violated the city's curfew for juveniles under the age of 16, which was set out at Phoenix, Ariz., City Code § 22-1 (1993). Therefore, the trial court held that the juvenile was an incorrigible child. The juvenile sought review.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile had her father's permission to go out with friends. She and her friends went to a park. The police took her in to custody when they responded to a report of a disturbance in the park. The juvenile court adjudicated her as an incorrigible child and imposed a penalty. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 22-1 was constitutional, and that it was neither overbroad nor vague. The court found that the juvenile did not meet her burden of proving that the parental permission exception exempted her from the curfew. While the juvenile enjoyed fundamental rights, including First Amendment freedoms and the right to move freely, those rights were not automatically coextensive with the rights of adults. The court found that curfew restrictions served a significant State interest that was not present in the case of adults. In making its determination that the State's significant interest justified infringing upon the juvenile's fundamental rights, the court examined three factors: (1) the peculiar vulnerability of children; (2) their inability to make critical decisions in an informed, mature manner; and (3) the importance of the parental role in child rearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the juvenile's conviction.

Conyers v. City of Prescott


1 CA-CV 92-0273


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


182 Ariz. 336; 897 P.2d 638; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 166; 171 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



August 11, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED on June 29, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-95-0034-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County. Cause No. 53797. The Honorable James B. Sult, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff landowner in an action challenging the legality of a sewer system assessment.


OVERVIEW: The landowner contested the legality of the city's assessment for a new sewer installation. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the landowner, concluding that although the city's method of apportioning was not inherently discriminatory or arbitrary, the method used in the instant case was unconstitutional as applied. On review, the court reversed. Although Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 48-589 required a city to apportion an assessment according to the benefits each landowner received, it did not define a method to accomplish this mandate. All that was required by the city under constitutional law was that the city apportion the burden of assessments with approximate equality, upon a reasonable basis of classification, and with due regard to the benefits to the individual property owners. The city reasonably concluded that the landowner's share of the assessment was proportional to the benefits he received from the project.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting summary judgment in the landowner's favor and remanded the matter with directions to enter judgment for the city.

OVERVIEW: The issue before the court was whether the aggrieved parties were barred by the doctrine of res judicata from maintaining an action challenging the constitutionality of Arizona's forfeiture statutes. The court concluded the aggrieved parties were not parties in the prior forfeiture actions, and thus, the doctrine of res judicata did not bar their action involved in this appeal.

State v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 94-0128


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


179 Ariz. 343; 878 P.2d 1381; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 167; 171 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 9



August 9, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action. Yavapai County Superior Court Cause No. CR 994-0102. The Honorable Richard Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the decision by the Yavapai County Superior Court (Arizona), which overturned defendant's convictions for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by an officer after running a red light. The officer noticed defendant's unsteady stance and administered a field sobriety test. Defendant stated he was unable to perform more tests and agreed that he drank excessively. The officer arrested defendant, read him the Miranda warnings, and asked him to submit to a intoxilyzer test. Defendant agreed to the tests that resulted in excessive blood alcohol concentration readings. Defendant was not informed of his right to have an independent test performed. The lower court ruled that the failure of the arresting officer to inform defendant of his right to an independent blood alcohol test constituted a due process violation warranting the reversal of defendant's convictions. The court found that the lower court was incorrect in finding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(B) shifted the burden of proof to defendants. Furthermore, the court found no requirement that defendant be informed of his right to an independent test in order to satisfy due process. Rather, § 28-692(H) required only that defendant have a reasonable opportunity to obtain the test.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the lower court that overturned defendant's convictions.

 

833 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Stramka v. Salt River Recreation


1 CA-CV 92-0100


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


179 Ariz. 283; 877 P.2d 1339; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 143; 169 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



July 21, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV-90-20032. The Honorable Barbara A. Rodriguez, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff river recreation patron appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted defendant river recreation company summary judgment on grounds that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-1551 relived it of any duty to the patron on his claim alleging various theories of negligence when he was injured in a river rafting incident.


OVERVIEW: When the river recreation patron fell out of a rafting tube and cut his hand on something sharp under the water, he sued the river recreational company, alleging various theories of negligence. The recreational company motioned for summary judgment on grounds that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-1551 relieved it of any duty to the patron. Upon review, the reversed the summary judgment for the recreational company, holding that the recreational company did not qualify for the immunity of the recreational use statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-1551. The court stated that the recreational company's permit to occupy a three-acre site of forest land for the purpose of doing business with recreational users of the river made it a commercial user of the premises, not an "occupant" of the premises within the meaning of the recreational use statute. The court held that permission to do business on recreational land did not confer recreational-use-statute immunity on that land.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the river recreation company and remanded the matter for further proceedings, holding that the recreation company's permit did not confer immunity to the injured patron under the recreational use statute.

 

834 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re Appeal in Maricopa County Juvenile Action No. JS-501904


1 CA-JV 94-0001


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


180 Ariz. 348; 884 P.2d 234; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 141; 169 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 34



July 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on November 29, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. JS-501904. The Honorable Barbara A. Rodriguez, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) terminating her parental rights with respect to her three youngest children.


OVERVIEW: The trial court terminated the mother's parental rights with respect to her three youngest children after the children had been in out-of-home placement for more than two years. The mother appealed, but the court affirmed. The evidence produced at the hearing supported the conclusion that the children were adoptable. The evidence also supported the trial court's determination that severance was in the children's best interests. Appellee Department of Economic Security (DES) had made diligent efforts to provide services to the mother, and the mother's failure to participate in the services DES offered did not foreclose termination of her parental rights. The trial court did not err in admitting a social study report into evidence under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-537.B. DES redacted the portions of the report to which the mother had objected, and the trial court did not rely on the unedited version of the report. The trial court did not violate the mother's due process rights by allowing DES to amend its petition to include a new ground for termination because the mother had adequate notice of the new ground.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that had terminated the mother's parental rights with respect to her three youngest children.

 

835 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Midland Risk Management Co. v. Watford


2 CA-CV 94-0037


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


179 Ariz. 168; 876 P.2d 1203; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 134; 168 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 56



June 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY. Cause No. CV 92-09315. Honorable Sherry Hutt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted appellee accident victim's motion for summary judgment and denied appellant's cross-motion for summary judgment, finding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1170(F) mandated automobile liability insurance coverage after an injury occurred regardless of whether the policy was fraudulently procured.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer denied liability to appellee accident victims on the ground that its insured failed to disclose the existence of her husband, who was driving her car at the time of the accident. The husband had previously been convicted of driving under the influence and appellant would have excluded him from the policy's coverage if the insured had disclosed him. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1170(F) mandated automobile liability insurance after an injury had occurred regardless of whether the policy was fraudulently obtained. The court determined that the provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 20-1109, regarding misrepresentations in insurance applications, did not override the more specific provisions of § 28-1170(F). The court concluded that appellant's liability to appellee became absolute upon the occurrence of the accident. The court rejected appellees' claim for attorney fees that they incurred prior to judgment because appellees failed to timely raise their claim in the trial court and failed to file a cross-appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment entered in favor of appellee accident victims and against appellant insurer because the Financial Responsibility Law mandated coverage after an injury occurred, notwithstanding the fact that the policy had been fraudulently obtained. The court denied appellees' claim for attorney fees because they failed to timely raise their claim in the trial court.

Knoell v. Cerkvenik-Anderson Travel


1 CA-CV 91-0577


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


181 Ariz. 394; 891 P.2d 861; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 133; 168 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 45



June 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 90-15460. The Honorable Michael O. Wilkinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted a motion to dismiss, pursuant to Ariz. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6), in the parents' wrongful death action brought under misrepresentation, dram shop, negligence, and outrage theories of liability against appellee travel agency.


OVERVIEW: The travel agency hosted parties in Mexico for recent high school graduates and allegedly furnished alcoholic beverages. The parents' 18 year old son was killed when he fell or jumped from his hotel room after abusing alcohol. The parents brought a wrongful death action against the travel agency. The lower court granted the travel agency's motion to dismiss pursuant to Ariz. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6). The court remanded the parents' misrepresentation claim because it was not necessary to recite the magic language of an intentional misrepresentation claim and the parents adequately pled the cause of action. Further, the parents' unsafe facility claim was remanded because the negligence claim did not mention alcohol consumption; thus, it was not barred by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-301. The court affirmed all other aspects of the lower court's decision because Arizona's dram shop laws only imposed liability on liquor licensees. Moreover, under Arizona tort law and the Mexican legal drinking age, the travel agency benefited from liability immunity under § 4-301. Finally, the travel agency's conduct did not support a claim for intentional infliction of emotional distress.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the lower court's decision dismissing the dram shop and outrage claims. The court remanded the misrepresentation and unsafe facilities claims for further proceedings.

State v. Buhman


1 CA-CR 92-0135


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


181 Ariz. 52; 887 P.2d 582; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 114; 166 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 6



May 26, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED on January 24, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-94-0291-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-91-04862. The Honorable Colin F. Campbell, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed the indictment against defendant for one count of failure to provide for his minor child in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-2458 (1988).


OVERVIEW: The state charged defendant with one count of failure to provide for his minor child and alleged that for three years, defendant gave no financial support to his child, although he had the means to do so. The trial court dismissed the state's indictment on the basis that § 12-2458 was unconstitutionally vague because it neither internally defined, nor provided a reasonably ascertainable external basis for defining, the standard of "reasonable support." On appeal, the court reversed and held that § 12-2458 was susceptible to constitutional construction and was not unconstitutionally vague. The court remanded for proceedings consistent with its opinion. The court interpreted the term "reasonable support" in § 12-2458 by reference to the definition of "support" in Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-2451(E). Through that interpretation, the court found that § 12-2458 criminalized a parent's failure to provide sufficient support to maintain a child at a reasonable subsistence level with food, shelter, clothing, medical care, and the like. Therefore, § 12-2458 was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the indictment against defendant for failure to provide for his minor child, and it remanded for further proceedings.

Malone v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 94-0004


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


181 Ariz. 223; 889 P.2d 16; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 110; 165 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 39



May 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED on February 22, 1995 by Arizona Supreme Court CV 94-0340-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 93-08192. The Honorable Richard Aubuchon, Judge Pro Tempore The Honorable Robert A. Hertzberg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a criminal defendant, sought a special action to review a judgment of respondents, the Superior Court of the State of Arizona, in and for the County of Maricopa and its judge, which denied the defendant's motion to reduce his bond. The defendant was charged with conspiracy to commit murder and first degree murder, and his bond was set at $ 100,00 plus $ 40,000 in surcharges under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-2403.A.


OVERVIEW: A juvenile court judge transferred the defendant for adult prosecution and set the bail. The defendant argued that the surcharge constituted excessive bail in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. XIII and Ariz. Const. art. 2, §§ 15, 22. Former Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-2403.A provided for the imposition of a 40 percent surcharge on any fine, penalty, or forfeiture imposed and collected for criminal offenses. Section 41-2403.B required the bond to include the assessment. On appeal, the court found that the record was too limited to determine whether the bond was reasonable or unreasonable. To avoid an unconstitutionally excessive bail, the assessment had to be a part of the amount of bail that was sufficient to secure the defendant's attendance in court. Adding the assessment to a sufficient bail amount violated the constitutions. Section 41-2403.B was not unconstitutional as it was written when the statute intended to allocate as a surcharge a certain percentage of the bail. However, the court could not determine whether the trial court concluded that $ 140,000 was a reasonable bail or whether that conclusion was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the action to permit the trial court to determine whether the judge regarded $ 140,000 as reasonable bail, independent of the surcharge.

Callender v. MCO Properties


1 CA-CV 92-0002


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


180 Ariz. 435; 885 P.2d 123; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 95; 164 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 55



May 10, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on December 20, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-94-0279-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 90-07697. The Honorable Brian R. Hauser, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, victim and mother (victim), appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted defendant sublessee's motion for summary judgment on the victim's dram shop claims, on the ground that the sublessee was neither a licensee as defined in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-101(19) nor subject to liability under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 4-311 and 4-301, and granted defendant campground operators' summary judgment motion.


OVERVIEW: The victim, who was intoxicated, purchased alcoholic beverages from an inn. He later was injured in a diving accident in a lake near land subleased to the sublessee under a subconcession arrangement. The operators operated the campground under subconcession arrangements with the sublessee. The victim contended that the operators and sublessee negligently furnished or failed to prevent service of alcoholic beverages to him when he was already intoxicated, and failed to adequately warn that it was unsafe to dive in the water near the campground. On appeal, the court affirmed the summary judgments in favor of the sublessee and the operators. The court concluded that dram shop liability did not apply to the sublessee, as it did not actually perform or control the service, sale, or supply of liquor to an underage or obviously intoxicated person. The court noted that the victim was a public invitee with respect to the lake, but was seeking recovery from the sublessee of the land adjacent to the lake, not the lake owner. There was simply no relationship between the victim and the operators that would have imposed a duty of care on the sublessee and operators for the victim's benefit.


OUTCOME: The judgment below granting summary judgment to the sublessee and the campground operators was affirmed.
