State v. Phillips


1 CA-CR 93-0417


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


178 Ariz. 368; 873 P.2d 706; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 79; 163 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 36



April 26, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 13, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. LC-93-00189. The Honorable John H. Seidel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which found defendant guilty of violating Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(A)(3) for driving or being in actual physical control of a vehicle while having a nonprescription drug or its metabolite in one's body, and revoked her driver's license for one year and ordered that she pay a fine and enter a driver's education program.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed her conviction and sentence under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 28-692(A)(3) for driving or being in actual physical control of a vehicle while having a nonprescription drug or its metabolite in one's body, claiming that the statute was unconstitutional. Defendant's primary argument was that § 28-692(A)(3) was vague and overbroad. She argued that it lacked specific guidelines for its application and permitted arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. The court rejected her argument and affirmed the conviction and sentence, and held that the statute was constitutional. The court found that § 28-692(A)(3) defined, in unequivocal terms, the type of behavior prohibited, and that it gave fair and objective guidelines to both potential offenders and law enforcement personnel that any driver who had ingested a proscribed drug was to be subjected to prosecution. The court concluded that she did not have standing to argue that § 28-692(A)(3) was overbroad because she alleged neither a substantial infringement upon a protected First Amendment right nor that she was an innocent defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for driving or being in actual physical control of a vehicle while having a nonprescription drug or its metabolite in one's body and the revocation of her driver's license for one year and order that she pay a fine and enter a driver's education program.

WATAHOMIGIE v. ARIZONA BD. OF WATER QUALITY APPEALS


1 CA-CV 93-0142


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


181 Ariz. 20; 887 P.2d 550; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 73; 163 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



April 21, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 92-06872. The Honorable Joseph D. Howe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a federally recognized Indian tribe and tribe members (tribe), sought judicial review of administrative decisions and administrative appeals regarding the issuance of an aquifer protection permit. The Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, Arizona Board of Water Quality Appeals (board), hearing officer, Arizona Department of Environmental Quality (department), and a corporation.


OVERVIEW: The tribe filed a notice of appeal with the board challenging the department's issuance of an aquifer protection permit to the corporation. The permit authorized the operation of uranium mine. The board dismissed the administrative appeal. The tribe sought judicial review of the order of dismissal and of an order in limine. The trial court granted summary judgment against the tribe. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that the regulations promulgated by the board, which required detailed disclosure in the notice of appeal, were reasonable and adequately related to the legislature's intent to provide for expedient appeals. Thus, the regulations were valid and enforceable, and the board did not err in dismissing the tribe's appeal. The court also found that the board did not abuse its discretion when it granted the motion in limine and denied the tribe leave to supplement its notice of appeal. Finally, the court concluded that the board did not err in dismissing the appeal on the ground that the evidentiary hearing did not begin within the 60-day period required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 49-323(B) (1988).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that granted summary judgment against the tribe. The court held that the board properly dismissed the notice of appeal that the tribe filed after the department granted the corporation an aquifer protection permit.

State v. Ott


1 CA-CR 89-1488, 1 CA-CR 91-0612-PR, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 71; 162 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 66



April 14, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Petition for Review DENIED. Cross Petition for Review DENIED. Chief Justice Feldman voted to grant review on the confrontation issue presented in the Cross Petition for Review. Redesignated as a Memorandum Decision November 9, 1994.
The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Published to Uunpublished November 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal/Petition for Review from the Superior Court of Coconino County. (Rule 32.9(c), Arizona Rules of Criminal Procedure). Cause No. CR 13713-88. The Honorable William F. Garbarino, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Coconino County (Arizona), which convicted him of conspiracy to sell a narcotic drug, sale of a narcotic drug, possession of a narcotic drug for sale, and possession of drug paraphernalia. The trial court found him to be a "serious drug offender" under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3410 (1987) and sentenced him to life imprisonment without possibility of parole for 25 years.


OVERVIEW: Four witnesses testified at trial to more than 20 incidences of prior uncharged crimes, and defendant was denied a jury trial on the issue of whether he was a "serious drug offender." The court found that the defense at trial was not the state of mind of defendant, but whether he committed the crime alleged. The court found that the evidence of prior misconduct was excessive to the point that a jury had to believe that so many sales in the past indicated a disposition to sell cocaine on the occasion. The court found that giving a Ariz. R. Evid. 105 limited admissibility instruction did not cure the defect. The court concluded that the admission of the evidence of prior uncharged crimes was reversible error. The court found that at the time of a second deposition, defendant had the opportunity to cross-examine an unavailable declarant with regard to her first deposition and had the motive to do so in a manner that would discredit her in the jury's eyes. The court found that admitting the first deposition did not violate the Confrontation Clause. The court concluded that a jury trial was required concerning whether defendant was a serious drug offender.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Alvarado


1 CA-CR 91-0537, 1 CA-CR 92-1168 PR (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


178 Ariz. 539; 875 P.2d 198; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 41; 160 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



March 8, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on June 21, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-94-0144-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal/Petition for Review from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona Rule of Criminal Procedure 32.9(c)). Cause No. CR 90-02937. The Honorable Michael D. Ryan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED; REVIEW DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) convicting him of offering to sell marijuana in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3405(A)(4).


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his conviction of offering to sell marijuana, defendant contended that reversal was necessary because he conviction was based on an improper proposition of law on the part of the state regarding the mens rea element of the crime of offering to sell marijuana under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3405(A)(4). The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial. To commit the crime of offering to sell marijuana under § 13-3405(A)(4), one had to be aware of believe that he had made an offer to sell the substance, not that he had told a lie or made a joke. However, the state's main legal theory was based upon its proposition that § 13-3405(A)(4) constituted a strict liability crime. Also, the trial court did not specifically reject the state's main legal theory and the trial court's general verdict did not indicate on which legal theory it was based. Remand for a new trial was appropriate on these facts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of offering to sell marijuana and remanded the case for a new trial.

State v. Averyt


1 CA-CR 92-0557, 1 CA-CR 92-0558 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


179 Ariz. 123; 876 P.2d 1158; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 39; 160 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



March 8, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review is Granted July 11, 1994. Petition for Review Denied on November 4, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-94-0181-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 91-07655. The Honorable Michael D. Ryan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the verdict from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which found defendants guilty of three counts of failing to file an income tax return in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42-137(B)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that § 42-137(B)(4) was susceptible of more than one interpretation. Defendants asserted that § 42-137(B)(4) was unconstitutionally vague regarding the point in time at which criminal liability attached and regarding the element of intent. The court disagreed with that contention because the statute was not vague or ambiguous with regard to the mental state required for its violation. Nevertheless, the court reversed and remanded defendants' convictions. The court concluded that the jury instruction given was incomplete and hence incorrect because the jury was not told that the element of knowledge applied to both the element of the failure to file and the element of the duty to file. Without the proper instruction, the state was relieved of the burden of proving defendants' knowledge of their duty to file state tax returns.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions for failing to file a tax return and reversed the sentences imposed. The court remanded for a new trial.

Hart v. Industrial Comm'n


1 CA-IC 92-0189


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


180 Ariz. 307; 884 P.2d 193; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 35; 159 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



March 1, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on November 29, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action--Industrial Commission. ICA CLAIM NO. 91348-039251. CARRIER NO. None. Administrative Law Judge Russell G. Sheley



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer challenged the judgment of respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona, which dismissed as untimely the request for a hearing filed by the employer. At issue on appeal was whether Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-947(A), which limited an uninsured employer's protest period, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent claimant filed a workers' compensation claim against the employer alleging that he had sustained an industrial back injury. The Commission could not locate workers' compensation coverage for the employer, so it forwarded the claim to the No Insurance Section/Special Fund Division, which issued a notice of determination. The employer filed an untimely protest letter. An administrative law judge dismissed the protest as untimely and the Commission affirmed the award. The court affirmed, holding that the 30-day protest period for uninsured employers under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-947(A) was constitutional because the statute treated all uninsured employers alike, and there was a reasonable basis for giving uninsured employers a shorter protest period than insured employers, which had 90 days to file a protest letter. One basis for disparate treatment was that Arizona law required employers to carry workers' compensation insurance, so uninsured employers were in violation of the law. Another reasonable basis for the disparate treatment was that claimants face added administrative delay in obtaining workers' compensation benefits when their employer was uninsured.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's award.

 

846 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Madrid v. Indus. Comm'n


1 CA-IC 92-0174


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


178 Ariz. 606; 875 P.2d 839; 1994 Ariz. App. LEXIS 8; 156 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 71



January 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED on June 28, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-94-0110-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Special Action--Industrial Commission. ICA CLAIM NO. 91192081664, 91259109905. CARRIER NO. XX00241, 520C636429-2. Administrative Law Judge Karen G. Calderon



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner worker brought a special action to review an award from respondent Industrial Commission (Arizona), which was approved by an administrative law judge for the apportionment of total temporary disability compensation between respondent carriers, awarding each one credit for overpayment. The issue was whether the worker was entitled to collect total temporary disability from two carriers for two separate and distinct injuries.


OVERVIEW: The worker injured his right knee and his right arm in two work-related accidents. Different carriers handled the claims. The arm was reinjured while the claim was open. The worker received temporary total disability. The knee claim was reopened and compensation paid until that carrier discovered that another carrier was making payments on the arm claim. The claims manager then apportioned the payments. The knee claim reopened a second time and the worker received payments from both carriers after he told the first that he no longer received anything from the second. The court agreed that the worker could not recover twice for the same loss of earning capacity. The court rejected the worker's argument that temporary total disability was not based on loss of earning capacity, but was based strictly on a medical assessment in which the fact and severity of the injury justified compensation. The court explained that the statutory language was mandatory and unqualified because an industrial injury at the total temporary stage caused a total loss of earning capacity. The court concluded that the worker had no standing to question how compensation was apportioned between the carriers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Industrial Commission's award to the worker, apportioned between the carriers, as approved by the administrative law judge.

Phoenix Newspapers v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 93-0234


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


180 Ariz. 159; 882 P.2d 1285; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 287; 22 Media L. Rep. 1531; 155 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



December 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied November 1, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. SW 93-00184, 93-00185, 93-00188, 93-00189. The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner newspaper filed a special action that challenged a decision of respondent judge, who was a judge of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), and real party in interest state that sealed search warrants and supporting affidavits in a high profile case after they were served and returned but before a criminal case was filed, claiming that the judge's decision violated Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3918(A).


OVERVIEW: Search warrants were executed in a high profile murder investigation. The judge ordered the warrants and affidavits sealed after they were returned but before a criminal case was filed. The newspaper, which received redacted copies, brought a special action for release of the documents. The newspaper claimed that the phrase "if the warrant is served, such documents and records shall be open to the public as a judicial record" that was contained in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3918(A) mandated release of the warrants once they were returned. Although it acknowledged the presumption that information received by a court was open to the public, the court denied relief. The court ruled that adopting a mandatory interpretation of § 13-3918(A) meant that the statute violated the separation of powers because only the state supreme court had the constitutional right to make procedural rules. The court adopted a permissive interpretation of § 13-3918(A) and held that the issuing court, in its discretion, had the right to balance the presumption of openness against the state's need to keep confidential any information which had the potential to jeopardize ongoing criminal investigations.


OUTCOME: The court denied the relief requested by the newspaper.

 

848 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Wilderness World v. Arizona Dep't of Revenue


1 CA-TX 92-0016


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


180 Ariz. 155; 882 P.2d 1281; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 281; 154 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 75



December 23, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause No. TX 92-00109. The Honorable William J. Schafer III, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision of the Arizona Tax Court, which granted a motion for summary judgment filed by appellee Arizona Department of Revenue (ADOR) in an action brought by the taxpayer alleging that its guided river trips did not fall within the scope of an amusement tax and that the amusement tax was improperly assessed against it.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was engaged in the business of conducting guided river rafting tours through the Grand Canyon National Park. The taxpayer charged a single fee for the trip, which included the guide service, food, beverages, transportation, and necessary equipment. ADOR audited the taxpayer for October 1982 through July 1985 and assessed an amusement tax under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-1314(A)(1). After exhausting its administrative remedies, the taxpayer filed a complaint in the tax court. The tax court granted ADOR's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the taxpayer's guided river rafting trips did not come within the reach of the amusement tax statute as the statute applied to businesses charging admission fees, and the taxpayer was prohibited from charging an admission fee to the park and the fee charged was for the skill, direction, and service provided by the guide; and (2) where the statute listed 21 specific business classifications, none of which included an activity similar to guided river rafting trips, the amusement tax could not be extended to such services.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the tax court's decision and ordered it to enter judgment in favor of the taxpayer for an amount consistent with the court's opinion.

Perez v. Southern Pac. Transp. Co.


2 CA-CV 93-0008


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


180 Ariz. 187; 883 P.2d 424; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 282; 154 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 63; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,806



December 21, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied November 1, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 274149. Honorable Gilbert Veliz, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad and appellee personal representative both sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which entered a verdict in favor of the personal representative in his wrongful death action on a strict liability theory but found that his products liability cause of action was barred by the statute of repose.


OVERVIEW: The railroad argued that the trial court erred as a matter of law in eliminating a foreseeability requirement before imposing strict liability for abnormally dangerous activity. The personal representative argued that the trial court erred in applying Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-551, the statute of repose, to bar his wrongful death claim for products liability when there was no evidence that the product was older than 12 years and that § 12-551 was unconstitutional. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case. It held that the trial court erred as a matter of law in applying a hindsight test to impose strict liability for abnormally dangerous activity upon the railroad. The court observed that the determination of whether an activity was abnormally dangerous had to be related to the time at which the railroad engaged in the activity being analyzed. It concluded that the personal representative's product liability claim was no longer barred by the statute of repose because § 12-551 had been held unconstitutional. The court observed that the trial court entered no factual findings on the products liability issue and reversed and remanded on that issue as well.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which entered judgment for the personal representative on his cause of action against the railroad for strict liability for engaging in an abnormally dangerous activity and found that his strict products liability cause of action was barred by the statute of repose, and remanded the case.

State v. Jones


1 CA-CR 92-1758


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


177 Ariz. 94; 865 P.2d 138; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 273; 154 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



December 14, 1993, Filed

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which reversed appellee business owners' convictions for violating Maricopa, Ariz., Ordinance art. XIX, § 1902(8), and finding that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The business owners were charged with six zoning violations. The state alleged that the business owners operated a nude-dancing establishment in violation § 1902(8) of the local zoning ordinance. The trial court fined them $ 725 and placed them on probation. The superior court reversed the convictions and held that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. On appeal, the court affirmed the reversal of the convictions, ruling that the state failed to articulate any government interest for the ordinance. The court ruled that the ordinance was imprecise, subjective, and undefined. The court held that on vagueness alone, the ordinance was unconstitutional. There was insufficient evidence to establish that the activity covered by the ordinance was incompatible with enterprises in the business owners' area that did not require a special-use permit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the reversal of the business owners' convictions for violating the county zoning ordinance and the finding that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.

State v. Verdugo


2 CA-CR 93-0524


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


180 Ariz. 180; 883 P.2d 417; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 268; 153 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 16



November 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review by the Supreme Court Denied November 1, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY. Cause No. CR 91-08868. Honorable E. G. Noyes, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of one count of conspiracy; two counts of offer, sale, or transportation of cocaine; and one count of offer, sale, or transportation of heroin--all class two felonies. Defendant claimed that the trial court abused its discretion by admitting into evidence tapes of calls intercepted as a result of wiretaps.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was one of 31 people indicted on 81 drug-related counts, and the state's case arose from the wiretapping of four telephones and its interception of some 500 calls, 17 of which were the basis of the case against defendant. He appealed his convictions on the basis of the wiretaps and the admission of the resulting evidence. The court affirmed the convictions and found that the Arizona wiretapping statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3010(A), was not unconstitutionally broader than the federal statute, 18 U.S.C.S. § 2516(2). The court held that the affidavits filed in support of the wiretap application were adequate and that disclosure of the English translations of the transcripts of the intercepted conversations was sufficient to protect defendant's rights to timely disclosure. The court also found that permitting the transcripts of the English translations to go to the jury was proper because although the initial translations were made by police officers, a court interpreter later corrected the translations. The court further found that the officer who testified as an expert on the narcotics codes used by those whose conversations were intercepted was qualified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and the sentences imposed upon him but modified the imposition of the mandatory fine. The court found that the Arizona wiretapping statute was constitutional and that the procedures followed in obtaining the wiretap provided sufficient safeguards of defendant's rights and constituted substantial compliance with both the federal and state statutes.

E.C. Garcia & Co. v. Ariz. State Dep't of Revenue


1 CA-TX 90-0024, 2 CA-CV 89-0250 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


178 Ariz. 510; 875 P.2d 169; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 251; 152 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 39



November 12, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review denied on June 23, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-94-0048-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Arizona Tax Court and from the Superior Court of Pima County. Cause Nos. TX 90-00031 and 246360. The Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge. The Honorable Michael J. Brown, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers challenged the Superior Court of Pima County's (Arizona) dismissal of their 1987 property tax appeal because of their failure to serve defendant county. The taxpayers also challenged the Arizona Tax Court's refusal to accept jurisdiction of their subsequent special action seeking a refund of the same 1987 property taxes. The appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Taxpayers challenged a tax assessment that deemed their property to be non-agricultural. The superior court's dismissal of the taxpayer's cause of action was affirmed because the court found that the taxpayers failed to serve an indispensable party, the county. The taxpayers also challenged the assessment in the tax court. The court reversed the tax court's refusal to accept jurisdiction of this special action seeking a refund from the 1987 property taxes because the assessment of the land as non-agricultural was erroneous within the meaning of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-506. Furthermore, the court found that the amendments to § 11-506 did not apply retroactively as to disallow the refund. The court found that the taxpayers had a substantial present property interest, which qualified for protection under due process clauses of the United States and Arizona Constitutions. The court held that because the amendment was more than a mere clarification of the law and the right embodied in the statute was a substantive right, due process would have been violated with the amendment's retroactive application.


OUTCOME: The court's previous opinion was vacated upon the granting of a motion to reconsider. The superior court's judgment dismissing the tax appeal was affirmed because the court found that the taxpayers had failed to serve an indispensable party. The tax court's judgment was reversed, however, because the court found an erroneous assessment within the meaning of the applicable statute and amendments to the statute did not apply retroactively.

State v. Strong


2 CA-CR 92-0894


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


178 Ariz. 507; 875 P.2d 166; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 250



November 9, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied June 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-37161. Honorable Leslie B. Miller, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which entered a jury verdict convicting him of making an unlawful offer to sell a narcotic drug in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408(A)(7). The jury was instructed that defendant had to act "knowingly," and it was given the statutory definition of the term under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-105(6)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that intent was an element of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408(A)(7). The court on appeal disagreed, finding that only "knowledge" was required. The court also found that the statute was constitutional even when read in this manner. Prosecutions could not be had for "offers made in jest" because defendant would have to know that his conduct was that described as a criminal offense. Thus, the element of intent did not have to be read into the statute or proved by the State. On other issues, the court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction because preliminary negotiations constituted a completed offense. Money did not have to change hands. Defendant's actions in arranging for a later meeting to sell the drug were sufficient. The court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment below.

 

854 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Precision Components v. Harrison, Harper, Christian & Dichter, P.C.


2 CA-CV 93-0239


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


179 Ariz. 552; 880 P.2d 1098; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 247



November 4, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied October 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY. Cause No. CV 90-28051 and CV 90-25516 (Consolidated). Honorable Robert D. Myers, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defense attorneys sought review of the order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) ordering both the defense attorneys and the plaintiffs' counsel not to charge their clients for time spent in the preparation and filing of a motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: In a motion for summary judgment, the two parties submitted over 3,500 pages of exhibits, many of which appeared unnecessary. The trial court held a conference in which it sanctioned all the attorneys by ordering them not to charge their clients for time spent in the preparation and filing of the motion. The defense attorneys appealed. The court affirmed the trial court's order. The court found that it could not grant relief for the defense attorneys' alleged deprivation of due process because the defense attorneys had not requested a hearing on the specifications or for reconsideration of the sanctions imposed. Because they had not raised the due process issue in the trial court, the court could not review the issue on appeal. The trial court had the inherent power to sanction the defense attorneys for their actions, and Ariz. R. Civ. P. 11 did not deprive the trial court of this inherent power. Although the defense attorneys had written the trial court a letter asking the court to vacate its order, the letter was an inadequate substitute for a motion for reconsideration. Moreover, the imposition of sanctions had been within the sound judicial discretion of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order requiring the defense attorneys not to charge their clients for time spent in the preparation and filing of a motion for summary judgment.

Home Builders Ass'n v. City of Scottsdale


1 CA-CV 92-0210


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


179 Ariz. 5; 875 P.2d 1310; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 239; 150 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 47



October 26, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review GRANTED July 6, 1994. FURTHER ORDERED: Pursuant to Rule 23(i) (2), Rules of Civil Appellate Procedure, this matter is remanded to the Court of Appeals for reconsideration in light of the United States Supreme Court opinion in Dolan v. City of Tigard, No. 93-518. FURTHER ORDERED: Request for Attorneys' Fees shall abide the final determination of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 87-31929. The Honorable William P. Sargeant, III, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Scottsdale (city) sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which found that Scottsdale Ordinance 1940, imposing a water resource development fee upon new developments, violated Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-463.05 (amended 1991).


OVERVIEW: Appellee developers filed a complaint against the city claiming that Scottsdale Ordinance No. 1940 was invalid. The trial court held that the ordinance failed to meet the statutory requirements of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-463.05 (amended 1991). The city amended the ordinance and sought a new trial, which was denied. On appeal, the court held that because the less restrictive standards approach applied to § 9-463.05, the statutory requirements imposed on the city were to be construed broadly. Specific plans and direct benefits were not required. The city only needed to show some rational basis for setting the amount of the fee in order to avoid it being clearly erroneous, arbitrary, and wholly unwarranted. Given the minimal burden of proof, the court held that the city's development fee would result in a beneficial use and it was imposed in a non-discriminatory manner. The court remanded the case to the trial court for a determination of whether the fee bore a reasonable relationship to the burden placed on the city.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in part because the court concluded that the city's determination that its development fee would result in a beneficial use was not clearly erroneous, arbitrary, and wholly unwarranted and that the fee was assessed in a non-discriminatory manner. The court remanded the case for a determination of whether the fee bore a reasonable relationship to the burden placed on the city.

State v. Sasak


1 CA-CR 90-1265, 1 CA-CR 92-0173-PR, 1 CA-CR 92-0335-PR (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


178 Ariz. 182; 871 P.2d 729; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 248



October 19, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on May 3, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-93-0545-PR.
Redesignated as Opinion November 9, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal/Petitions for Review from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. (Rule 32.9(c), Arizona Rules of Criminal Procedure). Cause No. CR 89-03800. The Honorable Kenneth L. Fields, Judge. The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REVIEW GRANTED; RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences imposed by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) for theft and illegally conducting an enterprise.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea agreement, defendant plead guilty to two felony counts and in return the state agreed to recommend that he not receive consecutive sentences. He was sentenced to 10 years on each count. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the finding that the state did not violate the plea agreement was not error because defendant failed to show that his plea rested on the state's promise and because he failed to offer an objection at sentencing. There was no abuse of discretion because the judge considered the relevant factors offered by defendant in mitigation. The proceedings were not defective due to a conflict of interest because the trial judge's previous position in the same office as two of the attorneys was prior to defendant's case. The court also determined that defendant's plea was voluntarily and intelligently made because there was no factual support that he was not aware of the consequences of his guilty plea on his probationary status. Finally, the court held that the imposed sentences did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment because they were not disproportionate to the extensive monetary loss to the victims and the lack of remorse by defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's felony convictions, finding no abuse of discretion or clearly erroneous findings of fact.

In re One Rolex Brand Man's Watch


No. 1 CA-CV 91-0254


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


176 Ariz. 294; 860 P.2d 1347; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 227; 149 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



October 7, 1993

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state filed an in rem complaint for forfeiture of appellee claimant's property, alleging that the claimant had used the property in conspiring or attempting to purchase cocaine in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-3408(A)(1), 13-1001(A), and 13-1003(A) (1989). The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) granted the claimant's motion and dismissed the state's action for lack of probable cause proof. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state had called a police officer as a witness, who testified as to what another witness told him regarding transactions with the claimant. That other witness invoked the Fifth Amendment right not to incriminate himself and refused to answer any questions about the any transactions with the claimant. The trial court found that the state had not proved its case of probable cause. The state argued that the trial court erred in excluding the hearsay testimony; that despite the exclusion, the state established probable cause to forfeit certain items; and that the state was entitled to attorney fees pursuant to Ariz. The court further held that the state failed in its burden of establishing that the trial court committed any reversible error regarding the finding of probable cause, especially because it did not request a finding of fact or conclusions of law. The court chose to defer to the trial court's decision and found that neither of the parties was entitled to attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that dismissed the state's in rem action for forfeiture against the claimant.

 

858 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Smalley v. Detrick


Nos. 2 CA-CV 93-0161, 2 CA-CV 93-0169


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


176 Ariz. 208; 859 P.2d 1341; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 204; 148 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



September 21, 1993 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause Nos. 293031 and 293633 (Consolidated). Honorable J. Richard Hannah, Judge and William H. Tinney, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city and a city clerk, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, which found that a term in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 16-322(A)(8) referred to the number of party members voting in an election. The judgment was in favor of appellees, two candidates and their political party, in two consolidated actions.


OVERVIEW: Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 16-322(A)(8) provided that nominating petitions for city offices for districts within a city were to have been signed by registered members of the same party equal to a certain percentage of the designated party vote in the ward, precinct, or other district. Under § 16-322(B), the basis of percentage was to have been the vote of the party for mayor at the last mayoral election. The court agreed with the trial court that the term "designated party vote" in § 16-322(A)(8) referred to the number of party members voting in an election rather than the number of votes cast for a party's candidate. The city, as it had historically done, calculated the "designated party vote" by using the vote for the mayoral candidate within the ward. While historical interpretation was entitled to some weight, it could not have been taken as resolving an issue never raised. The court reasoned that the price of electoral success through appeal to voters outside the party ought not to have been an increase in the burden of running within the party.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Cactus Wren Partners v. Arizona Dep't of Bldg. & Fire Safety


1 CA-CV 91-0263


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


177 Ariz. 559; 869 P.2d 1212; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 197; 147 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 73



September 14, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on April 5, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-93-0377-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 90-08384. The Honorable Silvia R. Arellano, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A hearing officer of appellee state agency found that appellant mobile home park operator erroneously charged appellee tenants certain fees. The operator claimed that the power exercised by the agency hearing officer violated the separation of powers provision of Ariz. Const. art. III. The operator sought review of the agency decision in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which affirmed the decision. The operator appealed.


OVERVIEW: Tenants of a mobile home park brought an action before a state agency against the park operator, alleging that the operator erroneously charged certain fees. The state agency hearing officer found for the tenants and ordered the operator to reimburse the tenants. The operator sought review in the lower court, alleging that the hearing officer exercised power in violation of the separation of powers provision of Ariz. Const. art. III. The lower court rejected the operator's argument and affirmed the decision of the hearing officer. The operator sought further review. On review, the court examined the authority of the hearing officer to conduct proceedings, as codified in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-2198.01 et seq. The court concluded that the role of the hearing officer did not usurp that of the judiciary, nor did it exert a coercive influence on the judiciary. The court found no merit in the operator's claim that the agency proceedings and the decision of the hearing officer deprived him of his constitutionally-guaranteed right to a jury trial. The proceedings before the state agency were restitutive in nature, and the right to a jury trial did not preclude such proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court.

Neil v. Kavena


No. 1 CA-CV 91-326


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


176 Ariz. 93; 859 P.2d 203; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 183; 146 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 69



August 31, 1993 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV-89-23848. The Honorable Susan R. Bolton, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which determined that defendant hospital was entitled to a credit of $ 175,000 and that, because the parties had stipulated that $ 175,000 was the amount of damages, plaintiff was not entitled to additional damages from defendant in her medical malpractice action against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient filed a medical malpractice action against defendant hospital for injuries resulting from her gallbladder surgery. The parties submitted the matter to the trial court, stipulating that a jury would award plaintiff $ 175,000 as full damages sustained by plaintiff. Plaintiff appealed the trial court's determination that defendant was entitled to a credit of $ 175,000 and that because of the stipulation, plaintiff was not entitled to additional damages from defendant. The court reversed the trial court's decision because defendant had no constitutional right to invoke the law of joint and several liability. The court held that the legislature clearly intended Ariz. R. Civ. P. § 12-2506 to apply to cases filed after December 31, 1987, the statute's effective date, even if the cause of action accrued previously. The court concluded defendant was not entitled to a credit of $ 175,000 paid in settlement by the insurance company and doctor because plaintiff's lawsuit was commenced after the abrogation of joint and several liability, so Ariz. R. Civ. P. § 12-2506 was the proper measure of defendant's liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, holding that defendant hospital was not entitled to a credit for the $ 175,000 paid in settlement by the insurance company and doctor. The court determined that because plaintiff patient's lawsuit against defendant was commenced after the abrogation of joint and several liability, a different statute was the proper measure of defendant's liability.

Waddell v. Arizona State Land Dep't


1 CA-CV 91-0452, 1 CA-CV 91-0460 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


178 Ariz. 308; 873 P.2d 646; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 173; 146 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 36



August 26, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied. Opinion Ordered Depublished by Amended Order December 19, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ariz. LEXIS 136.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 90-20689/CV 90-31231. The Honorable Susan R. Bolton, Judge



DISPOSITION: CV 90-20689: REVERSED AND REMANDED. CV 90-31231: DISMISSAL AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, successful bidder on public property, and appellee, State of Arizona, each sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) which granted summary judgment for appellant in his administrative review action but dismissed his concurrent declaratory judgment action. Appellant contended that the sale was void under Ariz. Const. art. 10, § 11, and Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 37-240, 37-234 and sought reimbursement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, successful bidder on public property, sought to void the purchase and sale of land held in statutory "school trust" at auction, contending that the sale was void under Ariz. Const. art. 10, § 11, and Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 37-240, 37-234. Appellee, State of Arizona, denied his request. Appellant requested judicial review of the administrative decision. Appellee challenged the trial court's jurisdiction. Appellant then filed a declaratory judgment action. The trial court consolidated the actions and granted summary judgment for appellant in the administrative action but dismissed the declaratory action. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the administrative judgment voiding the sale, and affirmed the dismissal of the declaratory judgment. The court held that sale was only voidable, not void, because it was in substantial compliance with the law, and that the equities favored upholding the sale because both parties relied on the classification of the property as commercial under the statutes, the purpose of the statutes was to benefit the statutory school trust, not the purchaser, and that appellant had not tendered full performance of his own obligations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant's, successful bidder on public property, declaratory judgment action, and reversed and remanded the administrative review judgment against appellee, State of Arizona which voided the sale. The court held that the sale was only voidable, not void, because it was in substantial compliance with the law, and that the equities favored upholding the sale.

Burris v. City of Phoenix


1 CA-CV 90-0545


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


179 Ariz. 35; 875 P.2d 1340; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 170; 2 Am. Disabilities Cas. (BNA) 1251; 146 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19; 63 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P42,761



August 24, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Leave to File Reply in Support of Cross-Petition for Review GRANTED July 6, 1994.
Petition for Review DENIED on July 6, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-93-0364-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 88-23062. The Honorable Michael J. O'Melia, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the City of Phoenix, appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which required the city to hire plaintiff applicant as a fire fighter. The applicant appealed the trial court's order, which denied his request for an injunction against the city's further use of discriminatory physical examination standards in its hiring of fire fighters and which denied his claims for seniority, back pay, and front pay.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sued the city for employment discrimination under the Arizona Civil Rights Act for its failure to hire him as a fire fighter. The trial court ruled that the city had discriminated against the applicant on the basis of a handicap, the applicant's history of cancer, and ordered the city to hire him. The applicant appealed from other rulings of the trial court, and the city cross-appealed from the hiring order. The court affirmed the trial court's rulings in all respects but two. The court affirmed the findings that the applicant's history of cancer constituted a handicap under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1436(B)(1). The court reversed the denial of back pay and seniority, and the amount of the attorney's fees awards and remanded for the trial court to reconsider those rulings in light of the court's holding that evidence of the conditional settlement offer made by the city was inappropriately considered. The court also reversed and remanded the trial court's denial of the applicant's request for an order enjoining the city from applying physical examination standards that discriminated against the applicants for fire fighter positions on the basis of handicap.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of back pay and seniority, and the amount of the attorney's fees awards and remanded the case. The court also reversed and remanded the denial of the applicant's request for an order enjoining the city from using discriminatory physical examination standards. On all other issues, the court affirmed the trial court.


 

865 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Ward v. State


1 CA-CV 91-0494


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


178 Ariz. 164; 871 P.2d 711; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 166; 145 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 57



August 19, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 89-21930. The Honorable Susan R. Bolton, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, injured individuals, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee state. The injured individuals had alleged that the state was negligent in failing to mark a peninsula of land with which their boat collided. The trial court held that the state was immune under the recreational use statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33-1551.


OVERVIEW: The individuals were injured in a boating accident on a lake in a national forest. The state had a federal contract to provide aids to navigation such as buoys on the lake. The injured individuals alleged that the state was negligent and the state asserted § 33-1551 as an absolute defense. The trial court found that the state was immune. On appeal, the injured individuals contended that § 33-1551 did not apply to public lands, that the state was not an "occupant," and that § 33-1551 violated Ariz. Const. art. 18 § 6 by abrogating their common law negligence cause of action. The court disagreed and affirmed. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-1551 applied to public, as well as private lands and to bodies of water located on the "premises." Also, the state occupied the lake under its aids to navigation program with a degree of permanence. In addition, the court rejected the injured individuals' claim that they were invitees and at common law the landowner had an affirmative duty to use reasonable care to make the premises safe. Section 33-1551 did not abrogate a cause of action against the state because it could not have been liable under common law at the time the constitution was written.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the state and against the injured individuals.

 

866 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Evenstad v. State


1 CA-CV 91-0311


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


178 Ariz. 578; 875 P.2d 811; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 152; 144 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 55



August 5, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review DENIED on June 28, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-93-0433-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 89-06401. The Honorable Michael A. Yarnell, Judge Pro Tem



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) granted summary judgment in favor of appellee state based on governmental immunity under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.01 and dismissed the wrongful death claim of appellants, surviving parents, arising out of the state's negligent issuance of a driver's license to an unfit driver. The parents sought review.


OVERVIEW: The parents filed a wrongful death action against the state, alleging that the negligently issued a driver's license to an unfit driver who caused the death of their children. The trial court concluded that the state was protected from the action by immunity. On appeal, the parents claimed that the state failed to promulgate rules to identify unfit drivers as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-413 (1989) and that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.01 (1992) was unconstitutional. The court held that: (1) the qualified immunity provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.01 (1992) did not apply to the duty of the state to prescribe rules but that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.02 (1992) shielded the activity as an administrative function involving a fundamental governmental policy; (2) the state's mandatory policy combined with the statutes were rules identifying unfit drivers; and (3) that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.01 (1992) was not unconstitutional because it codified recognized immunities, furthered the state's legitimate interest in avoiding the hampering of a governmental function, and did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the state, which dismissed the parents' wrongful death action based on governmental immunity.

 

867 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sandoval


No. 1 CA-CR 92-1302


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


175 Ariz. 343; 857 P.2d 395; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 141; 144 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 37



July 29, 1993 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-92-03627. The Honorable Lawrence O. Anderson, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted defendant's motion and dismissed the charges against defendant of indecent exposure in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1402.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed urinating in a public park by two young girls. Defendant chased the girls with his penis exposed until they hid from him and notified the police. Defendant entered a plea agreement to plead no contest to one count of indecent exposure. The trial court found there was not enough evidence to substantiate the charge and granted defendant's motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court interpreted the statute from the clear and unambiguous meaning of its language. The court found that § 13-1402 only required that a person engage in public nudity in the presence of another person and have a reckless disregard whether the other person would be offended or alarmed. The court found that the facts of defendant's case amounted to a violation of § 13-1402. The court concluded that the trial court abused its discretion for untenable reasons because it used an incorrect legal interpretation of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charges against him for indecent exposure. The court remanded the matter for further consistent proceedings.

In re Appeal in Pima County Juvenile Severance Action No. S-114487


2 CA-JV 93-0008


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


180 Ariz. 29; 881 P.2d 361; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 147; 144 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 48



July 27, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. S-114487. Honorable Karen S. Adam, Judge Pro Tempore



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant infant child challenged an order from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) denying her petition to terminate the parental rights of defendant father. The child argued that the father had abandoned her and that her adoption by others would be in her best interests.


OVERVIEW: Based on his conversations with the mother, the teenage father believed that after the baby's birth in Arizona, the mother and child would move back to Texas, where the father and mother would be married. Instead, the mother surrendered her parental rights and put the child up for adoption. When the father learned of this, he contacted a Texas attorney who told him to contact an Arizona attorney. He ignored a consent to adoption form he received from the mother's attorney. The father spoke with the attorney over the phone and with the attorney for the adoptive parents. He decided to contest the severance and wrote a letter to the court in time for the initial severance hearing. The trial court denied the severance petition. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not apply the wrong standard in determining that the father did not abandon the child. The court took into account the father's age and circumstances. The court noted that the father had bought baby supplies and clothes in anticipation of the mother and child's return. The court emphasized fundamental rights of parents and held that the best interests of the child alone were not always grounds for severance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the severance petition opposed by the father.

State v. Bews


2 CA-CR 92-0203


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


177 Ariz. 334; 868 P.2d 347; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 129; 143 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 15



July 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied February 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY. Cause No. CR 90-03488.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed without prejudice the indictment charging defendant with unsworn falsification in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2704(A)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant testified in murder trials against her boyfriend, which both ended in new trials being ordered. Thereafter, she and her boyfriend were indicted on drug charges and defendant agreed to testify in her boyfriend's drug trial in exchange for dismissal of the charges against her. During her pretrial interview, defendant said she lied during the boyfriend's previous murder trials, that she wanted to tell the truth at his third trial, and gave a recorded statement. At the homicide trial, she testified consistently with her testimony in the previous trials and stated that she lied in her recorded statement because she was facing a lot of time in the penitentiary. She was then indicted for her false statement in the pretrial interview. The trial court dismissed the indictment and the court reversed. It found that defendant's statement was a statement made in connection with an official proceeding, as the pretrial interview was conducted in preparation for and in anticipation of trial, an official proceeding under the definition of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2801, and bore a sufficient relationship to the trial itself to constitute having been performed in connection with the trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the indictment for unsworn falsification and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

870 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Kadish v. Ariz. State Land Dep't


1 CA-CV 91-0110


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


177 Ariz. 322; 868 P.2d 335; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 156; 143 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



July 13, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. C-433745. The Honorable Michael J. O'Melia, Judge. The Honorable Mark W. Armstrong, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association and members appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) denying their request for an award of attorney's fees in a taxpayer action challenging the validity of the fixed royalty provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 27-234(B). The association and members argued that they were entitled to fees pursuant to the private attorney general doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff association and members filed a taxpayer action challenging the validity of the fixed royalty provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 27-234(B). The trial court dismissed the complaint, but the association and members subsequently prevailed in the state Supreme Court and the federal Supreme Court. Upon remand to the trial court, the association and members requested an award of attorney's fees. When the trial court denied the request, the association and members again appealed. The appeals court concluded that this case met the criteria for an award under the private attorney general doctrine. The court reasoned that the resolution of the litigation benefitted a large number of people in the state, including taxpayers, students and personnel. Also, the vindication of the right asserted was of societal importance. Lastly, vindication of the right asserted by the association and members required a legal challenge to a statute adopted by the state legislature and thus could only have been privately enforced. The court rejected defendant land department's argument that it was a nominal party, precluding an award of attorney's fees, because it had a proprietary stake in the outcome.


OUTCOME: The appeals court held that the trial court abused its discretion in denying the association and members' request for attorney's fees because there was no reasonable basis for the denial. Hence, the court reversed the judgment and remanded for entry of an award of attorney's fees.

 

871 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Turner


No. 1 CA-CR 92-0378


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


175 Ariz. 256; 855 P.2d 442; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 127; 142 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



June 29, 1993 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County. No. CR-13552. The Honorable Steven F. Conn, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona), which affirmed a judgment that convicted defendants for violating Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 5-331(C), which required that children 12 years of age or under wear life jackets whenever the watercraft was underway.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, who were ferryboat pilots, were convicted of violating Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 5-331(C), which required that children 12 years of age or under wear life jackets on watercraft that were underway. The court affirmed the convictions and held that § 5-331(C) was constitutional. The court did not find clear and manifest congressional intent to preempt state law in the area of boat safety. On the contrary, the court found that 46 U.S.C.S. § 4306 of the Federal Boat Safety Act authorized each state to regulate boat safety. The court noted that the United States Coast Guard believed that the federal legislation in the area of boat safety had not preempted the state's power to similarly legislate regarding the use of floatation devices by young children. The court concluded that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 5-331(C) neither conflicted with federal law nor frustrated the federal objectives. The court found that the state requirement that the life jackets had to be worn merely enhanced the minimum standards established by U.S. Coast Guard Reg. § 180.25-5 that life preservers for children be stowed. The court held that the state statute did not violate the Supremacy or Commerce Clauses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision that affirmed a judgment that convicted defendants of failing to require children 12 years of age or under to wear life jackets whenever the watercraft was underway.

In re Ten Thousand Ninety-Eight Dollars in United States Currency


No. 1 CA-CV 91-0307


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department E


175 Ariz. 237; 854 P.2d 1223; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 121; 141 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 39



June 22, 1993 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Rodriguez v. Arizona (In re Rodriguez), 2008 Bankr. LEXIS 176 (Bankr. D. Ariz., Jan. 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CV 90-29069. The Honorable Marilyn A. Riddel, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant drug dealer challenged the decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which ordered $ 10,098 formerly in the drug dealer's possession forfeited in a civil in rem action brought by appellee city. The drug dealer contended that the money could not validly be forfeited where he was charged with a preparatory crime, and that the forfeiture hearing was improperly set more than 60 days after the filing of the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The police seized $ 10,098 from the drug dealer in an operation in which an undercover officer agreed to sell marijuana to the drug dealer. The trial court ordered the money forfeited in a civil in rem action. The drug dealer contended that the money could not validly be forfeited where he was charged with a preparatory crime, the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss where the forfeiture hearing was set more than 60 days after the filing of the complaint, and there was no probable cause to justify the forfeiture of $ 98 found in the drug dealer's pants pocket. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that: (1) the clear and unambiguous language of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3413(A) authorized the forfeiture of the $ 10,098.00 even though the drug dealer was never charged with a substantive drug offense; (2) the city prosecuted the action in a timely manner where there were valid reasons for the delay in setting the hearing; and (3) the $ 98 was forfeitable because it was found in proximity to the instrumentality of an offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which ordered money in the possession of the drug dealer forfeited in a civil rem action brought by the city.

 

873 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Oyakawa v. Gillett


No. 1 CA-CV 91-0160


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


175 Ariz. 226; 854 P.2d 1212; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 111; 140 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 29



June 10, 1993 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County. Cause No. CI 30894. The Honorable Leonard C. Langford, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff domesticated an amended California defamation judgment against the community property of defendant husband and under the Revised Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann, § 12-1701 et seq. (1982). The Superior Court of Mojave County (Arizona) granted the husband and wife's motion to stay enforcement of the Arizona judgment and to vacate the portion of the judgment against the wife. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife argued that the California judgment against the their marital community was not valid in Arizona, contending that Arizona courts must apply Arizona law, which required the claimant to have proceeded against both spouses for the judgment to be valid against the community. Thus, the husband and wife argued that the judgment was effective only against the husband and could not be enforced against the community because the wife was not joined in the original California defamation action. The claimant argued that applying Arizona law would deny the judgment the full faith and credit to which it was entitled under U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1. The court held that the husband and wife's marital community was not deprived of due process by the earlier judgment in the action in which the wife was neither named nor served. Thus, original judgment was not tainted and because the judgment was effective against the community, there was no violation of due process in amending the judgment to reflect community liability. Consequently, both the original and amended judgments were entitled to full faith and credit in Arizona courts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order staying enforcement of the claimant's California judgment and vacating the judgment as to the wife and the husband and wife's community.

 

874 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crisp


No. 1 CA-CR 92-1069


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


175 Ariz. 281; 855 P.2d 795; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 128; 143 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



June 10, 1993 


NOTICE:   [***1] Originally filed June 10, 1993 as Memorandum Decision.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Redesignated as Opinion and Publication Ordered July 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 92-00137. The Honorable John H. Seidel, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which upheld the constitutionality of Phoenix, Ariz., Ordinance § 23-52(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating § 23-52(a)(2), which provided in part: "A person is guilty of a misdemeanor who solicits or hires another person to commit an act of prostitution." Defendant appealed to the superior court, claiming the jury instruction was improper and that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The superior court upheld the constitutionality of the ordinance, and defendant appealed. Defendant argued that the ordinance lacked an intent or mens rea requirement and was unconstitutional. The court explained that where a penal statute failed to expressly state the necessary element of scienter, the court was permitted to infer the scienter requirement from the words of the statute plus legislative intent. Here, the court inferred from the words "solicit" or "hire" the intent of defendant to thereby promote or facilitate the crime of prostitution. In addition, the ordinance did not sweep within its reach speech protected by the First Amendment. The ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague. Finally, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3214 made it clear that the legislature did not intend to preempt the field of regulation of prostitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court, which upheld the constitutionality of the ordinance.

Platt v. State


2 CA-CV 93-0089


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 107; 140 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



May 11, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Redesignated as Opinion June 2, 1993. Petition for Review Denied December 16, 1993. The Court of Appeals' Opinion shall not be published, pursuant to Rule 111(g), Arizona rules of the Supreme Court.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF APACHE COUNTY. Cause No. 9210. Honorable Michael C. Nelson, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state lands lessees sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Apache County, which granted summary judgment to appellees, State of Arizona and Arizona State Land Department Commissioner (collectively, the state) on certain of the lessee's claims. The state sought review of that part of the judgment that granted summary judgment to lessee.


OVERVIEW: The lessees refused to execute new grazing leases at the expiration of their old lease, claiming that certain provisions of the lease were unconstitutional, unlawful, and onerous. The trial court granted summary judgment for lessees as to certain provisions and granted summary judgment to the state on the remaining issues. Both sides appealed. The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the state and reversed the summary judgment in favor of lessees. The court found that the grazing lands were held by the state in trust for the support of schools and other institutions, and held that in dealing with trust lands, all doubts were to be resolved in favor of the trust. The court rejected the lessee's challenge to the provisions for acquiring prospective water rights, finding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 37-102, 132, and 132(A) authorized the state to set the terms of the leases, and that the lease provisions objected to were within the state's power to require. The court also found that a lessee did not have a right to compensation in the event of condemnation, and held that the state had authority to include a termination upon condemnation clause in the leases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the judgment in favor of the state in the action instituted by the lessees who claimed that certain of the state's grazing lease provisions were unconstitutional, unlawful, and onerous. The court reversed the part of the judgment holding in favor of the lessees.

State v. Hone


1 CA-CR 91-1143


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


177 Ariz. 213; 866 P.2d 881; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 82; 138 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



May 11, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on February 1, 1994 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-93-0295-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County. Cause No. CR 14917. The Honorable James B. Sult, Judge



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which dismissed the charges against defendant for hauling horses without requisite documentation in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 24-267.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appeared in city court for hauling horses without the requisite documentation and contested the constitutionality of the statute. The city court referred the matter to the state trial court because it did not have jurisdiction. The trial court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 24-261(C) was unconstitutional because it gave unfettered discretion to the livestock officers. On review, the court affirmed and found that § 24-261(C) was unconstitutional. The statute empowered Arizona Livestock Officers to conduct random, roving patrol stops of any vehicle capable of carrying hides or livestock without a reasonable suspicion or probable cause based on articulable facts to believe that Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 24-274, 24-267 had been violated. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 24-261 was in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. IV and the Arizona Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the charges against defendant based on the unconstitutionality of the statute.

 

877 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. GARCIA


No. 1 CA-CR 91-0105


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


176 Ariz. 231; 860 P.2d 498; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 50; 136 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



April 6, 1993 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied November 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-90-07978. The Honorable Robert L. Gottsfield, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; RESTITUTION ORDER MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of aggravated assault. The defendant contended that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on facilitation as a lesser included offense, in imposing a mandatory prison sentence, and in ordering restitution to victims with respect to dismissed counts.


OVERVIEW: The defendant drove a car past the home of a member of a rival gang while his companion fired shots injuring a victim in the knee. The defendant was arrested and convicted of aggravated assault and was sentenced to prison for five years. The defendant contended that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on facilitation as a lesser included offense of aggravated assault; in using a single factor, use of a deadly weapon, to define the offense and enhance his sentence; and in ordering restitution to victims with respect to dismissed endangerment counts. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision in part and reversed it in part. The court held that: (1) the defendant was not entitled to an instruction on facilitation where the indictment did not set out facts that described aggravated assault in a way that also defined another offense; (2) the state's allegation of dangerousness did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers because it was within the executive branch's power to enhance punishment; and (3) the trial court could not impose restitution on the charges for which the defendant was not found guilty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of the defendant for aggravated assault and the trial court's imposition of a sentence enhanced for dangerousness. The court vacated the trial court's order directing restitution relating to the dismissed charges of endangerment.
