State v. Delgadillo


No. 1 CA-CR 92-0840


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


174 Ariz. 428; 850 P.2d 141; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 47; 135 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 44



March 30, 1993 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review not filed.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Coconino County. Cause No. CR-16406. The Honorable Charles D. Adams, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Coconino County (Arizona), which, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 3-3405(D), fined him $ 68,088, three times the value of 56.74 pounds of marijuana, the possession of which gave rise to his conviction for possession of more than eight pounds of marijuana not for sale.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two codefendants were indicted on one count of possession for sale and one count of transportation for sale of more than eight pounds of marijuana. Defendant pled guilty to amended charges of possession of more than eight pounds of marijuana not for sale and possession of drug paraphernalia. The trial court sentenced defendant to terms of imprisonment. In addition, the court imposed a fine against him pursuant to § 13-3405(D). Defendant appealed contending that the fine imposed violated the Eighth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Ariz. Const. art. XV, § 12 because he was disproportionately punished by a fine based on the entire quantity of drugs that he jointly possessed with his codefendants. Defendant argued that the fine should have been split equally among the three codefendants and that he should have been assessed only a one-third share. Affirming the fine, the court held that the fine required under § 13-3405(D) was not restitution, subject to reduction by codefendants' contributions, but punishment for the indivisible culpability of defendant himself. The participation of codefendants did not lessen defendant's culpability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Church


No. 1 CA-CR 91-1257


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


175 Ariz. 104; 854 P.2d 137; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 79; 138 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



March 18, 1993 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Redesignated as Opinion and Publication Ordered May 11, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-91-90736. The Honorable Steven D. Sheldon, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of aggravated driving with a suspended license while under the influence of intoxicating liquor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of aggravated driving with a suspended license while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court found that the prosecutor's comments in closing argument regarding defendant's right to remain silent were not prejudicial because they simply affirmed defendant's right not to testify and did not urge the jury to draw an unfavorable inference or to impose a penalty on defendant for the exercise of his right to remain silent. The court determined that the inferred fact of receipt of notice of revocation or suspension of a driver's license was more likely than not to flow from the proved fact of mailing of the notice, and, therefore, the inference did not violate due process. The court further found that defendant did not assert lack of receipt at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Boldrey


Nos. 2 CA-CR 90-0403, 2 CA-CR 92-0411-PR


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


176 Ariz. 378; 861 P.2d 663; 1993 Ariz. App. LEXIS 15; 131 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 40



January 29, 1993 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 19, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-28407. Honorable John F. Kelly, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; PETITION FOR REVIEW DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) for four counts of sexual abuse and molestation involving his then 11-year-old daughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant engaged in repeated sexual acts with his daughter. A jury convicted defendant of four counts of sexual abuse and molestation. The trial court sentenced him to consecutive prison terms. Defendant appealed and filed a petition for post-conviction relief under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 32. The appeal and Rule 32 petition were consolidated. The court affirmed defendant's convictions for sexual abuse and molestation and the sentences imposed. The court held that evidence that an uncle had previously molested the daughter would not have changed the verdict because the evidence against defendant based on the daughter's testimony and defendant's admission to police officers was overwhelming. The court also found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in rejecting defendant's claim that the sentencing procedure was unfair. The court concluded that that the imposition of consecutive sentences did not violate Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-116, which prohibited double punishment for one act. The court explained that although defendant's crimes were committed as part of one sexual episode, each factually distinct act of forcible sexual contact exposed the daughter to a separate harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for sexual abuse and molestation and the sentences imposed.

Inch v. McPherson


No. 2 CA-CV 91-0217


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


176 Ariz. 132; 859 P.2d 755; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 330; 129 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 59



December 31, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 10, 1993. Reconsideration Denied February 11, 1993. Review Denied October 5, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 262037. Honorable Richard Nichols, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee neighboring property owners brought an action for trespass and appellant property owners cross claimed for quiet title over a piece of land that adjoined the two properties. The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) awarded a prescriptive easement through adverse possession to the neighboring property owners and allowed them to build a block wall on the easement.


OVERVIEW: A dispute arose between two property owners when the neighboring property owners used a gravel driveway beside their house that they had constructed and the property owners put up a fence that interfered with the neighboring property owners' driveway. The court held that the prescriptive easement granted to the neighboring property owners was proper because it was possible for the trial court to have concluded that the neighboring property owners used the disputed land to gain a prescriptive easement by laying gravel and parking on it. The court determined that the gravel areas used by the neighboring property owners could have given notice to the whole world they had taken the area their driveway was on for their own use. The court reasoned that the neighboring property owners were not allowed to build the wall on the easement because that would exceed the uses through which they had acquired the easement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of a prescriptive easement in favor of the neighboring property owners and vacated the order that allowed them to build a wall on the easement.

Tucson Mechanical Contracting v. Arizona Dep't of Revenue


No. 1 CA-TX 91-0039


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


175 Ariz. 176; 854 P.2d 1162; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 324; 129 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 44



December 29, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 7, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause No. TX 90-00003. The Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractors sought review of the judgment of the Tax Court (Arizona), which held that the transaction privilege tax assessed under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-1310.16.G as applied to the contractors did not violate the United States' constitutional immunity from state taxation and concluded that appellees, Arizona Department of Revenue (Department) and its director, did not unconstitutionally discriminate against the contractors.


OVERVIEW: The Department assessed unpaid transaction privilege taxes against the contractors on their gross income from federal contracts under § 42-1310.16.G. The tax court held that the tax was no unconstitutional as applied to contracting income from federal government projects, and on appeal, the court affirmed because the tax did not fall directly on the federal government and the statutory scheme did not compel the contractors to shift the legal incidence of the tax to its purchaser. The tax court also held that the Department had not discriminatorily enforced the tax, and on appeal, the court affirmed because nothing demonstrated any significant quantifiable disparity actually existed between the proportion of out-of-state contractors who did federal contracting work in Arizona and were audited by the Department and the proportion of in-state contractors who do such work and were audited. The court held that the tax court expressly found no systematic policy of discrimination and no evidence showing the Department's manner of selecting taxpayers for audit relied upon inherently invidious standards.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the tax court, which held that the transaction privilege as applied to the contractors' did not violate the United States' constitutional immunity from state taxation and concluded that the Department did not unconstitutionally discriminate against the contractors.

State v. Stevens


No. 1 CA-CR 92-0762


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department E


173 Ariz. 494; 844 P.2d 661; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 326; 129 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 31



December 24, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 91-08458. The Honorable Robert A. Hertzberg, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of her sentence after a guilty plea in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) on a charge of engaging in fraudulent schemes, with one prior felony.


OVERVIEW: The trial court orally sentenced defendant to a prison term and ordered to pay restitution after she pleaded guilty to one count of fraudulent schemes and a prior felony. On appeal, defendant challenged her sentence on the ground that she should have received credit for 214 days of presentence incarceration, instead of the 200 days the trial court credited; the State contested the court's jurisdiction under amendments to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4033(B) (1992) and Ariz. R. Crim. P. 17.1(e). The court modified the sentence to grant defendant credit for 214 days of presentence incarceration and to correct a minute entry to reflect the prior conviction admitted in the plea agreement and at the plea hearing. The court held that (1) the statutory amendments had only prospective application because a right to appeal was substantive, not procedural, and there was no waiver of defendant's right to appeal under Ariz. Const. art. II, § 24; and (2) under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-709(B) (1989), defendant was entitled to full credit for all time spent in custody pursuant to her offense, and the court was free to reconcile a discrepancy between the trial court's oral pronouncement and a minute entry.


OUTCOME: The court modified defendant's sentence to grant defendant credit for the full term of her presentence incarceration and to correct a minute entry to reflect the prior conviction admitted by defendant in the plea agreement and at the plea hearing.

Smith v. City of Phoenix


No. 1 CA-CV 91-0215


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department E


175 Ariz. 509; 858 P.2d 654; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 318; 115 N.M. 509; 129 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



December 17, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 4, 1993. Review Denied October 5, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 89-34283. The Honorable Marilyn A. Riddel, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge challenged an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which entered summary judgment for appellee city on the judge's claims for declaratory relief and contract damages related to the amendment of Phoenix, Ariz., City Code art. III, § 2-83.1, governing salaries paid to municipal court judges.


OVERVIEW: The judge brought an action against the city challenging changes made in the way municipal judges were paid. The city denied the judge's claim for additional compensation. He brought an action for declaratory relief and contract damages. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted summary judgment for the city. On appeal, the court affirmed. Section 2-83.1 did not violate Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 2, § 17. The constitutional provision was inapplicable in a case concerning the practice of differently valuing and compensating distinct varieties of judicial duties rather than an across-the-board salary increase or decrease for members of a court with staggered terms of office. A legislative increase in superior court judges' salaries, the condition precedent to the vesting of the judge's right to receive increased salary payments calculated under the pre-amendment version of Phoenix, Ariz., City Code art. III, § 2-83.1, never occurred while that version remained in effect. Because the judge had no vested contractual right in the pre-amendment § 2-83.1 salary calculation method, the prospective alteration of that method did not reduce his compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of the city in the judge's action for declaratory relief and contract damages.

 

886 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin


No. 1 CA-CR 91-1229


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


174 Ariz. 118; 847 P.2d 619; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 316; 127 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 22



December 10, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. LC-91-00172. The Honorable Norman D. Hall, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which remanded the matter to municipal court for further proceedings after affirming the municipal court judgment. A jury convicted defendant in municipal court of driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(A)(1), (A)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(A)(1), (A)(2) were unconstitutionally vague and that § 28-692(A)(2) was unconstitutionally overbroad. The court found that both § 28-692(A)(1), (A)(2) provided a person of normal intelligence a reasonable opportunity to know what was prohibited and established an objective standard of enforcement. The court concluded that neither was unconstitutionally vague. The court found that defendant had no standing to raise, on behalf of others, an overbreadth challenge to § 28-692(A)(2), because he did not allege that the statute substantially infringed upon protected First Amendment freedoms or that he was a member of a class of "innocent defendants." The court found that the essential element of § 28-692(A)(2) was having a blood alcohol concentration of 0.10 percent within two hours after driving. The court found that § 28-692(B) neither established that element nor placed the burden of disproving it on defendant. The court affirmed and concluded that the state still had to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant's blood alcohol concentration was 0.10 or more within two hours of driving to convict him of a violation of § 28-692(A)(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order remanding the case to the municipal court for disposition.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 90-01669. The Honorable Robert L. Gottsfield, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) that convicted and sentenced him, based upon his guilty plea, to the crime of escape in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: The evidence indicated that after defendant missed his court appearance for the offense of driving under the influence, he went to court and submitted himself to the judge to explain his prior failure to appear. An arraignment took place, and the judge informed defendant that he would have to post bond before he could leave. Defendant ignored the court order placing him custody and walked out of the courtroom. Defendant admitted that he knew that he was not free to leave the courtroom. Defendant thereafter entered a plea of guilty to the charge of escape in the third degree. On appeal, defendant alleged that the factual basis for the offense was insufficient because he was never physically restrained and therefore, there was no arrest. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that defendant left the courtroom in defiance of the judge's order not to leave, knowing that the judge has placed him in custody. The court stated that the facts of the case clearly established that the judge placed defendant in custody and under arrest by use of "constructive restraint."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted and sentenced defendant for escape in the third degree.

Church v. Rawson Drug & Sundry Co.


No. 1 CA-CV 90-0357


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


173 Ariz. 342; 842 P.2d 1355; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 276; 122 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 98



October 1, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 88-16726. The Honorable Philip W. Marquardt, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this negligence action brought by plaintiff claimant against defendant manufacturer, the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) reduced the amount of the claimant's recovery to reflect the abolition of the doctrine of joint and several liability by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2506. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was injured when containers delivered from the manufacturer fell on top of her as she unloaded them at her place of employment. She instituted an action for damages against the manufacturer but could not recover against her employer due to the workers' compensation laws. The trial court found that the manufacturer was one-third liable for the claimant's injuries, and it awarded her judgment against the manufacturer for one-third of her total damages. The claimant argued that § 12-2506, which abolished joint and several liability, was unconstitutional and should not have been applied to reduce the judgment against the manufacturer. The court held that § 12-2506 was constitutional. It concluded that the statute neither abrogated the right to bring an action for damages nor impermissibly limited the amount of recovery for an injury. It also ruled that the statute did not deny the claimant either the equal protection of the laws or due process of law, and it held that the statute did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the reduction in the claimant's negligence recovery against the manufacturer.

Estate of Bohn v. Waddell


No. 1 CA-TX 91-008


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department T


174 Ariz. 239; 848 P.2d 324; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 273; 16 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2877; 122 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 90



September 29, 1992

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause No. TX 89-00050. The Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge. Opinions of the Arizona Tax Court. 164 Ariz. 74, 790 P.2d 772 (Tax Ct. 1990) and 167 Ariz. 344, 807 P.2d 1 (Tax Ct. 1991). VACATED



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of the judgment from the Arizona Tax Court that denied injunctive relief but ordered appellee, the Department of Revenue of the State of Arizona (Department), to refund the taxpayers for the difference between the tax federal pensioners paid on their pensions and what they would have paid had state taxpayers been similarly taxed.


OVERVIEW: During the tax years 1984 through 1988, Arizona's income tax laws exempted from income taxation 100 percent of state and local retirement benefits paid to retired employees of those political entities, while exempting only the first $ 2,500 of federal retirement benefits paid to retired federal employees. The court held that the lower court did not abuse its discretion in declining to issue injunctive relief to the taxpayers under 42 U.S.C. S. § 1983. The court also held, however, that the taxpayers' failure to exhaust their Arizona administrative remedies either in their individual or representative capacities prevented the lower court from ruling on their claims for Arizona income tax refunds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part and affirmed in part the judgment from the lower court and vacated the lower court's opinions. The court remanded the action for further proceedings.

Berenter v. Gallinger


No. 1 CA-CV 90-0539


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


173 Ariz. 75; 839 P.2d 1120; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 258; 122 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 42



September 22, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 89-10951. The Honorable Gloria G. Ybarra, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Arizona Director of Insurance (director) suspended plaintiff insurance adjuster's license and assessed a civil penalty against him for violating Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 20-316(A)(4) and (7). The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) affirmed the director's order. The adjuster appealed. The primary issues on appeal were whether there was substantial evidence to support the order and whether the adjuster violated the statute.


OVERVIEW: The adjuster withheld an insurer's check made out to him and to a restoration company that performed services for the insureds after a fire damaged their home. The restoration company had refused to allow the adjuster to obtain his fee out of the check proceeds. The Department of Insurance noticed a hearing alleging that the adjuster had illegally withheld monies received in the course of his activities as a licensed insurance adjuster. The hearing officer rejected the adjuster's claim that he withheld the check based on his clients' instructions, and found that he withheld the check because he wanted a portion of the proceeds. The hearing officer concluded that the adjuster intentionally violated §§ 20-316(A)(4) and (7). The court upheld the superior court's judgment. First, neither the superior court nor the appellate court weighs the evidence, but determines only whether there was substantial evidence to support the administrative decision. Here, substantial evidence supported the decision. Second, § 20-316(A)(7) was not unconstitutionally vague. Finally, the adjuster was not entitled to a peremptory challenge of the hearing officer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court and denied the adjuster's request for attorney fees.

Fernandez v. State Personnel Bd.


No. 2 CA-CV 92-0007


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


175 Ariz. 39; 852 P.2d 1223; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 262; 122 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 123



September 22, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied October 21, 1992. Review Denied June 15, 1993. *


*  Feldman, C.J., and Zlaket, J., of the Supreme Court, voted to grant review.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY. Cause No. CIV-38872. Honorable Jay Abbey, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the State Personnel Board, Arizona Department of Corrections (DOC), and the director, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona), which entered judgment in favor of appellee employee. The DOC had dismissed the employee and had appealed unsuccessfully to the Board. The employee sought judicial review in the superior court, which ordered that the employee be reinstated.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a correctional officer, was dismissed from his employment with the DOC when its director became aware of the employee's mayoral position. The employee's dismissal was based solely on the prohibition under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-772, not his job performance. The superior court held § 41-772 to be unconstitutional in its applicability to small towns and rural communities. On appeal, the court vacated the judgment and affirmed the employee's dismissal by the DOC. The court held that the challenged portion of § 41-772 did not violate the employee's constitutional rights under the First or Fourteenth Amendments. Many governmental interests were served by that portion of § 41-772 under consideration. The court held that the prohibition against state employees holding paid public office enhanced a government work force of efficient, apolitical employees; avoided the appearance of impartiality; and assured employee advancement based on merit. Although § 41-772 did not define the phrase "paid public office," the employee's mayoral position unquestionably fell within its common, ordinary definition.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the superior court's order that reinstated the employee and affirmed the employee's dismissal by the DOC.

 

893 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Fry's Food Stores v. Indus. Comm'n


No. 1 CA-IC 91-059


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


173 Ariz. 578; 845 P.2d 504; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 240; 121 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 45



September 10, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted February 17, 1993. *


*  Corcoran, J., of the Supreme Court, recused himself and did not participate in the determination of this matter.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action--Industrial Commission. ICA CLAIM NO. 507-28-3909. CARRIER NO. 05DIL86C2464. Administrative Law Judge Donald H. Bayles



DISPOSITION: AWARD SET ASIDE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer appealed the order of the administrative law judge (ALJ) (Arizona) affirming the decision of respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona awarding respondent claimant permanent total disability without apportionment. The employer asserted that the ALJ misinterpreted Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23-901.05. Petitioner carrier was an additional party to the special action to review the award.


OVERVIEW: The claimant had a respiratory impairment due to both heavy smoking and "baker's lung" from exposure to flour at work. The employer initiated a special action review of the commission's award to the claimant for a permanent total disability without apportionment under the occupational disease or the industrial injury apportionment statutes, Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 23-901.05, -1044(E). The ALJ concluded that apportionment required a preexisting earning capacity disability, and that, although the claimant had a preexisting impairment, it was not earning capacity disabling before his industrial "injury." On appeal, the court set aside the award denying apportionment under the occupational disease apportionment statute because the ALJ misinterpreted Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23-901.05 to require a preexisting earning capacity disability. At issue was the meaning of "disability or death from any other cause not itself compensable." Applying the words' common meaning, the court interpreted them to mean any other cause, including a previous disability, a previous impairment, or even a latent condition that was a cause in fact of a disability or death, and not earning capacity disability.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the award denying apportionment for the claimant's permanent total disability under the occupational disease apportionment statute in the employer's special action review of the commission's award.

State v. Moreno


No. 2 CA-CR 91-0735


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


173 Ariz. 471; 844 P.2d 638; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 241; 121 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 56



September 8, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 2, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-33784. Honorable Leslie B. Miller, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from two aspects of his class 5 felony convictions for aggravated driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor on a suspended license and aggravated driving with an alcohol concentration .10 or more on a suspended license, and from one aspect of his sentencing to concurrent, presumptive three-year terms by the Superior of Pima County (Arizona).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was given three breathalyzer tests and only the last one was preserved. Defendant claimed that the admission of the third test result was error, based on Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692.03(A), which established certain non-exclusive foundational requirements for the admission of breath test results. Defendant contended that subsection three always requires duplicate tests because a range comparison was obviously inapplicable when there was but one test. The court held that a single test preserved the reliability of its result by a 20-minute pre-test observation period, the purpose of which was to prevent an artificially high test result due to recent alcohol consumption. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692.03(A)(3) did not require duplicate tests for a test result that was preceded by a 20 minute observation period and, therefore, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress the third test result. Defendant also could not complain of jury instructions that he had tendered or the trial court's refusal to sentence him concurrently on an unimposed federal sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences for aggravated driving while intoxicated were affirmed.

 

895 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re Maricopa County


No. 1 CA-CV 90-648


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


173 Ariz. 177; 840 P.2d 1042; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 235; 121 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 15



September 3, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. MH-90-00566. The Honorable Patricia A. Pelfrey, Commissioner



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Patient appealed an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) committing him to a state hospital for inpatient treatment and subsequent supervised outpatient treatment on the grounds of mental illness, challenging the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. 36-501(29).


OVERVIEW: The patient, a paranoid schizophrenic, appealed from an order committing him to inpatient treatment at a state hospital and subsequent supervised outpatient treatment on the grounds of mental illness. The patient asserted that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-501(29) was unconstitutional. The court disagreed and affirmed the order of commitment. The court held that the establishment of "persistently or acutely disabled" as a category for the involuntary commitment of the mentally ill, was not unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. Under the parens patriae power, the state had the authority to provide care for those citizens who, due to emotional or mental disorders, were unable to care for themselves. Additionally, the court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the conclusion that the patient was persistently and acutely disabled. These factors included hearing voices, hallucinations, and paranoia.


OUTCOME: The court held that the statute, which established "persistently and acutely disabled" as a category for the involuntary commitment of the mentally ill, was constitutional. Further, the court affirmed the order of involuntary treatment.

 

896 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Helffrich


No. 1 CA-CR 90-013


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


174 Ariz. 1; 846 P.2d 151; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 225; 120 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



August 27, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Granted, Opinion Amended November 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-89-04380. The Honorable Mark W. Armstrong, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which ruled that defendant was not entitled to an unconditional release because he was still suffering from a mental disease or defect and that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3994 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was acquitted of aggravated assault because he was not responsible by reason of insanity and was committed to the custody of the hospital. At the conditional release hearing, the trial court ruled that defendant was not entitled to an unconditional release, and on appeal, the court remanded because the trial court did not determine whether defendant was a danger to himself or others and reversed the refusal of unconditional release. However, the court affirmed the trial court's finding that § 13-3994 was constitutional because (1) due process was not violated by conditionally releasing an acquittee for an indefinite period of time because the nature and duration of conditionally releasing a person was reasonably related to the purpose of the release; and, (2) there was a rational basis for permitting acquittees to be conditionally released for an indefinite period of time while persons civilly committed were conditionally released for specific time periods. Also, § 13-3994(B) did not require that a 50-day release hearing be held absent a request by the acquittee, and the 120-day mandatory commitment period of § 13-3994(D) satisfied due process.


OUTCOME: The court remanded defendant's cause because the trial court did not determine whether defendant was a danger to himself or others and reversed the refusal of unconditional release. However, the court affirmed the trial court's finding that the conditional release statute was constitutional.

 

897 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


McClead v. Pima County


No. 1 CA-CV 90-477


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


174 Ariz. 348; 849 P.2d 1378; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 227; 120 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



August 27, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 89-17702. The Honorable John Foreman, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pensioners challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied their complaint against appellees, state and county pension funds and their officials, brought under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 35-212 and -213. The pensioners argued that post-retirement benefit increases violated the state constitution's extra compensation and gift clauses and the contract clause of both the state and federal constitution.


OVERVIEW: The pensioners brought an action against the state and county retirement funds and their officials claiming that post-retirement increase of benefits violated the state extra-compensation clause, Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 2, § 17, the state gift clause, Ariz. Const. art IX, § 7, and the impairment of contract clause of both the state, Ariz. Const. art. II, § 25, and federal, U.S. Const. art I, § 10, constitutions. The court held that the extra-compensation clause was not violated because the increased benefits did not come from state funds. Instead, the various respondent pension plans were funded by individual and employer contribution or by investment earnings. Nor was the gift clause violated because pension benefits were not gifts; they were deferred compensation for services rendered by the pensioners during their employment. Finally, the court applied a three factor test derived from federal cases, and concluded that the increased benefits were for the public good and did not impair any contractual relationship because all of the pension plans were fully funded and able to meet there contractual duties without jeopardizing the rights of vested beneficiaries.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed the pensioners' complaint against the state and county pension funds and their officials. The court held that proposed post-retirement increases in pension benefits did not violate the state constitution's extra compensation and gift clauses or the contract clause of either the state or federal constitutions.

 

898 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Carondelet Health Servs. v. Indus. Comm'n


No. 2 CA-IC 92-0020


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


173 Ariz. 575; 845 P.2d 501; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 218; 118 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



August 6, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: SPECIAL ACTION - INDUSTRIAL COMMISSION. ICA Claim No. 91119-049477. Carrier Claim No. G1HCC90C0207. Bill Enriquez, Administrative Law Judge.



DISPOSITION: AWARD SET ASIDE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought special action review of the order of respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona, which awarded workers' compensation death benefits under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1046 to respondent natural mother of respondent employee after the employee's death. An administrative law judge found that the natural mother was a dependent under the provisions of § 23-1046.


OVERVIEW: The employee was adopted by the mother and stepfather of her natural mother. The employee was raised as her natural mother's sister. When the employee turned 18, she went to live with and care for her natural mother. After the employee was injured while working for the employer, she filed a claim for workers' compensation benefits. She underwent surgery and subsequently died as a result of complications from the surgery. In the natural mother's action for death benefits, the employer conceded that she was partially dependent on the employee. The administrative law judge awarded death benefits to the natural mother, but the court set aside the award. The court held that death benefits awarded under § 23-1046 were limited to the class of dependents specified in § 23-1046(A). The court found that § 23-1046(A) specified dependents as surviving spouses, surviving children, parents, brothers, and sisters. Because the natural mother's parental rights were terminated at the time of the employee's adoption, she was not considered a parent. In addition, § 23-1046(B) did not broaden the class of dependents to include any individual who was in fact dependent upon the deceased employee.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the award.

El Paso Natural Gas Co. v. Ariz. Dep't of Revenue


No. 1 CA-TX 91-003


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department T


174 Ariz. 470; 851 P.2d 95; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 198; 117 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



July 16, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 28, 1992. Reconsideration Denied October 2, 1992. Review Denied May 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause Nos. TX 89-00145 and TX 89-00212 (Consolidated). The Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged a summary judgment from the Arizona Tax Court, which found in favor of appellee hospital district. The tax court ruled that the district had legal authority to impose a secondary property tax for the operation and maintenance of its hospital for the tax years 1988 and 1989, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 48-1907(6).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed actions challenging the district's 1988 and 1989 secondary property tax levies. The district moved to dismiss, or in the alternative, for summary judgment. The tax court granted partial summary judgment to the district. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that: (1) the district was not entitled to levy a secondary property tax for 1988 under § 48-1907(6) because the district was not operating the hospital at the relevant time; (2) the 1988 Ariz. Sess. Laws 141 was an unconstitutional special law within the prohibition of Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 2, § 19; and, therefore, did not authorize the district's 1988 secondary property tax levy; and (3) 1989 Ariz. Sess. Laws 254 § 2, which removed the requirement of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 48-1907(6) that a hospital district "operate" its hospital in order to levy a secondary property tax, was not effective until September 15, 1989, and therefore, did not authorize the district's 1989 secondary property tax levy on August 21, 1989.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the summary judgment in favor of the hospital district and against the taxpayers. The court held that the statutes did not authorize the district's 1988 and 1989 secondary property tax levy.

State v. Conlin


No. 1 CA-CR 90-1442


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


171 Ariz. 572; 832 P.2d 225; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 160; 114 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



June 4, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-90-07476. The Honorable Joseph D. Howe, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND VACATED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which ordered that defendant pay his fine and felony assessment to the State's general fund instead of the drug enforcement account as mandated by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-811(C)(1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to possession of heroin. The parties stipulated that defendant would pay a $ 2,000 fine and surcharge to the Arizona Drug Enforcement Fund. When the trial court accepted defendant's plea and entered judgment, it ordered defendant to pay the fine and assessment to the general fund instead of the drug enforcement account on the ground that payment to the latter violated defendant's right to due process and to a fair and impartial trial because the sentencing court was funded in part with monies from the drug enforcement fund. On appeal, the court held that where the trial court judge did not control expenditures from the drug enforcement account, his salary was fixed by statute and was not dependent upon fines levied in criminal cases, he did not have the discretion under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-811(C) or Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-2402 to assure or increase the funding of his paycheck, and he was not responsible for raising revenue, he did not have a direct, personal, substantial, pecuniary interest in assessing the fine and thus there was no due process violation.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's ruling that defendant pay his fine to the general fund. The court ordered defendant to pay the fine to the drug enforcement account.

State ex rel. Corbin v. Ariz. Corp. Comm'n


No. 2 CA-CV 92-0052


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


174 Ariz. 216; 848 P.2d 301; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 168; 114 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 36



May 29, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 3, 1992. Reconsideration Denied July 16, 1992. Review Denied April 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause Nos. CV 90-12939, CV 90-14317, CV 90-14419, CV 90-14420, CV 90-14421, CV 90-14606, CV 90-14609 (Consolidated). Honorable Sherry Hutt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Arizona Corporation Commission (commission) and its members appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which found that the commission's proposed ratemaking rules could not become effective until certified by the attorney general, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1041(A), and that the commission's rule to the contrary was unlawful.


OVERVIEW: The commission promulgated rules to regulate formation of holding companies by public service corporations, govern their ability to invest in business activities that might pose a risk to the utility's ratepayers, and regulate transactions between public service corporations and their affiliates. The order stated that the rules would become effective on filing with the secretary of state under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1032 or 90 days after submission to the attorney general, whichever was earlier. The state and several utilities argued this would allow the rules to take effect even if not approved by the attorney general as required by statute. The trial court held that the rules could not become effective until certified by the attorney general, who refused to certify them because he found that they were outside the commission's powers. The state supreme court ordered certification, but did not address submission to the attorney general. The court held that the commission did not have to submit the rules to the attorney general. Ariz. Const. art. 15, § 6, did not authorize giving the executive branch the authority to reject such rules. The judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court finding that the commission's proposed ratemaking rules could not become effective until certified by the attorney general was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court with directions to enter judgment in favor of the commission.

Aitken v. Indus. Comm'n


No. 2 CA-IC 91-0042


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


173 Ariz. 300; 842 P.2d 1313; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 151; 113 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 56



May 14, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted on Issues 1 and 2 January 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action - Industrial Commission. ICA Claim No. 374-78-9448. Carrier No. A065140. Administrative Law Judge Jerry C. Schmidt



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of three issues in this special action involving the workers' compensation claim against respondents, the State Industrial Commission (Arizona), the employer, and its carrier. The issues presented were whether the carrier's lien was limited to the amount of benefits paid, whether the lien provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1023 violated the Arizona Constitution, and whether the lien extended to a spouse's award.


OVERVIEW: The employee fell after stepping out of a doorway into an area where the sidewalk had been removed by a construction company. She filed a claim for workers' compensation benefits and received medical and compensation benefits from her employer's carrier. The employee and her husband asserted loss of consortium and filed a third-party negligence claim against the construction company. The jury awarded damages to them. The employee reimbursed the carrier for benefits paid, but objected to the carrier's claim of credit against future benefits. The administrative law judge found in favor of the carrier, holding that its lien could not be reduced by the employer's degree of fault and that it attached to the husband's award. On review, the court ruled that the carrier's lien was not limited to the amount of benefits paid, that the lien provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1023 did not violate the Arizona Constitution, and that the lien extended to the husband's award for loss of consortium. The court affirmed the award because the employee had the option to reject workers' compensation and pursue a third-party judgment free of an employer's lien, but chose not to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of workers' compensation to the employee, and affirmed the carrier's lien against the employee's third-party judgment.

State v. Miller


No. 1 CA-CR 90-1230


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


173 Ariz. 421; 844 P.2d 588; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 153; 112 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 58



May 14, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted on Issue No. 3 only and Denied on all other Issues February 2, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County Cause No. CR-90-01299. The Honorable Howard V. Peterson, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) convicted defendant of unlawful flight from a law enforcement vehicle and endangerment by conduct causing danger of imminent physical injury. Defendant appealed his convictions and the $ 150,000 fine accessed by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by the trial court as charged after the evidence showed that defendant, who had been drinking, led police on a high speed chase when police attempted to pull him over. This chase went to speeds over 100 miles per hour and defendant led the chase through residential neighborhoods. Defendant appealed his convictions and claimed the statutes at issue, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 28-622.01 and 28-624(C) were unconstitutionally vague. Defendant also claimed the fine accessed was excessive and violative of the Eighth Amendment. On appeal, the court affirmed and found defendant's claims meritless. The court found it was clear that it was felonious conduct to willfully flee or attempt to elude a pursuing police vehicle sounding an audible signal even if its colored light or lens were not visible from in front of the vehicle. Thus, the statutes were not unconstitutionally vague. Also, it could not be said that the fine imposed on defendant was either so shocking or so unreasonable as to be unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court convictions and the fine imposed.

Ariz. v. Aguilar


No. 1 CA-CR 90-1275


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


171 Ariz. 444; 831 P.2d 443; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 131; 112 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 48



May 12, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-90-07004. The Honorable Joseph D. Howe, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which entered a judgment of guilt when placing her on probation pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3601(G) under the Domestic Violence Diversion Program. Defendant pled guilty to endangerment pursuant to a plea agreement.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not believe that deferral of the entry of judgment of guilt was appropriate under the circumstances of the case and entered the judgment of guilt for a felony. The court found that under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3601(G), a trial court could not enter a judgment of guilt unless and until defendant had violated probation and consequently failed to complete the Domestic Violence Diversion Program. The court found that regardless of whether the Domestic Violence Diversion Program was mandatory or discretionary under the plea agreement stipulations, the trial court placed defendant on probation pursuant to § 13-3601(G). The court found that having done so, the trial court had no authority to enter the judgment of guilt. The court reversed and concluded that in essence, the trial court rejected a provision of the plea agreement and did not provide defendant with an opportunity to withdraw her plea as provided for by Ariz. R. Crim. P. 17.4(e).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with its decision.

 

905 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State of Arizona v. John Arthur Clough


No. 1 CA-CR 89-792


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


171 Ariz. 217; 829 P.2d 1263; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 112; 111 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 28



April 23, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County. Cause No. CR-10390. The Honorable Steven F. Conn, Judge

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Vacated Opinion of August 6, 1992, Reported at 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 178.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of third-degree burglary and theft of property in excess of $ 1,000. Defendant also challenged the enhancement of his sentence, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604(I) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was previously convicted of issuing bad checks in Montana. When defendant was convicted of crimes in Arizona, the trial court enhanced his sentence, based on a prior felony conviction in Montana. The state contended that defendant's conduct constituted a felony in Arizona. Originally, the court affirmed defendant's sentence and conviction. However, on reconsideration, the court vacated the sentence. The court held that there was not strict conformity between Mont. Code Ann. § 45-6-316 (1983) and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1801(B). Only § 13-1801(B) required an intent to deprive. Therefore, defendant could have committed the crime of issuing a bad check in Montana without engaging in conduct that would constitute a felony in Arizona. Moreover, defendant's conduct also did not constitute a violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2310. The court held that "intent to defraud" under § 13-2310 meant more than merely issuing a check knowing that there were insufficient funds to pay it. The trial court did not err in considering aggravating factors in sentencing. Finally, the court noted that the use of defendant's prior conviction for impeachment purposes was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for third-degree burglary and theft of property in excess of $ 1,000. The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded the case for resentencing.

Iphaar v. Indus. Comm'n of Ariz.


No. 1 CA-IC 90-136


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


171 Ariz. 423; 831 P.2d 422; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 113; 111 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 34



April 23, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 12, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action--Industrial Commission. ICA CLAIM NO. 0000P041709. CARRIER NO. 73X 004130. Administrative Law Judge William E. Smith



DISPOSITION: AWARD SET ASIDE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of a decision of an administrative law judge (Arizona) in favor of respondents, industrial commission, employer, and insurer, in an action seeking to reopen a workers' compensation claim.


OVERVIEW: The employee received an industrial eye injury. A workers' compensation claim was filed, accepted for benefits, and a permanent impairment was awarded. Thereafter, the employee requested that his claim be reopened because a physical examination revealed that he needed additional surgery. The insurer denied the claim. The employee then filed an untimely hearing request. The administrative law judge (ALJ) entered an award dismissing the hearing request for lack of jurisdiction. The ALJ found that the employee did not receive the notice from the insurer, but the insurer presented evidence that the notice was properly mailed. On appeal, the court found that under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-947, the legislature excused late filing if there was a clear and convincing showing that the employee did not receive the notice of claims status, but also provided that no excuse would be honored if it was shown that the claims status was properly mailed. The effect of that conflict was to deprive the employee of a hearing despite a clear and convincing showing that he never received the employer's notice of claims status. Thus, his due process right to notice and a hearing was violated.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the award of the administrative law judge in favor of the industrial commission, employer, and insurer, in an action in which the employee sought to reopen his workers' compensation claim and held that the employee's due process right to notice and a hearing was violated.

Calmat of Ariz. v. State


No. 1 CA-CV 89-602


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department E


172 Ariz. 300; 836 P.2d 1010; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 89; 110 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 97



April 14, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied and Cross-Petition for Review Granted as to issue No. 1 and Denied as to issue No. 2 and all other issues October 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause Nos. C-555355; CV 87-17569 (Consolidated). The Honorable E. G. Noyes, Judge

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Vacated Opinion of February 13, 1992, Reported at 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 28.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions in part, remanded for new trial in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation and cross-appellant state, sought reconsideration of two decisions from the court which had reversed and remanded decisions from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona). The trial court had awarded damages from the state to the corporation in condemnation proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had awarded damages for the property taken in one case and awarded severance damages in the other. In the action for severance damages, the trial court held that the corporation had failed to produce evidence to establish the proper measure of severance damages and entered a judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV) for the state. In the other case, the trial court granted the state a new trial. The corporation held the trial court erred in granting JNOV and a new trial to the state and the state held that even if the court reversed the trial court's findings, they were entitled to a new trial for the other case as well. On appeal, the court held that the proper date of valuation was the date that the corporation filed their inverse condemnation suit because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1123(A), which set the date of valuation at the date of the issue of the summons, applied to inverse condemnations as well. The court held that JNOV was improper because the jury had been properly instructed as to the issue of severance damages and had found for the corporation and just because it was less then the experts had said it was had not made the verdict erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court amended their prior opinion by issuing the supplement opinion and vacating the prior opinion and denied both parties' motions for reconsideration. The court reversed the JNOV finding for the state and remanded the case to the trial court to re-instate the jury verdict.

Hays v. Continental Ins. Co.


No. 1 CA-CV 90-600


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


172 Ariz. 573; 838 P.2d 1334; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 92; 110 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 93



April 14, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted November 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 90-90510. The Honorable David L. Grounds, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted defendant insurer's motion to dismiss, holding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23-930, gave the industrial commission exclusive jurisdiction over bad faith claims arising in workers' compensation actions.


OVERVIEW: The claimant alleged that the insurer knowingly breached its duty of good faith and fair dealing in her workers' compensation claim. The claimant challenged § 23-930, by contending that it unconstitutionally limited her damages for bad faith and deprived her of her right to a trial by jury. The trial court found that the claimant elected the workers' compensation law for her remedy and that the industrial commission was the forum for her claims, pursuant to § 23-930. On appeal, the court held that the cause of action for insurance bad faith did not exist at common law and was therefore not protected by Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6. Section 6 only protected actions recognized at common law at the time of its adoption. Further, the court held that the claimant did not have a right to a jury trial because Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 23, only guaranteed preservation of the right to a jury trial that existed at common law. The court found no error in the requirement of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23-941, that workers' compensation hearings be held before an administrative law judge rather than a jury. Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23-930, was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the claimant's complaint.

Robert Paul Norton v. Superior Court of Ariz.


No. 1 CA-SA 91-044


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


171 Ariz. 155; 829 P.2d 345; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 76; 109 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 64



March 31, 1992  
March 31, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CR 90-12511. The Honorable Robert L. Gottsfield, Judge



DISPOSITION: Jurisdiction accepted; Relief denied


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of respondent Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which denied his motion to dismiss a felony charge of failure to pay child support. Defendant's challenge also named the trial judge as a party respondent. The state attorney general was the real party in interest.


OVERVIEW: In the motion to dismiss, defendant argued that portions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-2458 (Supp. 1991) unconstitutionally shifted the burden of persuasion from the state to defendant. Although the trial court agreed, it denied defendant's motion to dismiss, finding that the unconstitutional portions were severable and that the remainder was not unconstitutionally vague. In the severability challenge, defendant argued that the severance of the two provisions was inappropriate. The court upheld the severance of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-2458(B), (C) (Supp. 1991) and denied relief to defendant. The court also declined to accept jurisdiction on the vagueness issue. The court held that it was sufficient to sever the unconstitutional portions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-2458 (Supp. 1991) from the remainder and that § 12-2458 was constitutional after the severance.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the trial court's severance of the unconstitutional portions of the criminal statute for failure to pay child support. The denial of defendant's motion to dismiss was affirmed.

State of Arizona v. Vickey Jean Ramsey


No. 1 CA-CR 90-1488


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


171 Ariz. 409; 831 P.2d 408; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 46; 108 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 6



March 3, 1992  
March 3, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-90-00024. The Honorable Robert L. Gottsfield, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of custodial interference in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-1302 (1989) and then deferred entry of defendant's judgment of guilt and placed defendant on three years probation pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-3601(H) after imposing sentence under the domestic violence statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-3601.


OVERVIEW: The action arose after defendant removed her children from their adoptive parents' home without consent after she had consented to the adoption of her children by her aunt and uncle. The state contended the prosecutor did not concur with the sentence that was required under the statute and since defendant's parental rights had been severed, she was no longer related to the children within the requisite degree and was not entitled to have been classified as a domestic offender under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-3601(A). The court found there were certain crimes designated as family offenses in which a court may have treated defendant more leniently and required the offender and victims had to been related by blood to the second degree of consanguinity. The court concluded the blood relationship between defendant and her children was not extinguished by the adoption as they were still related in the first degree of consanguinity. The court held the requirement of prosecutorial concurrence with the sentence violated the separation of powers under Ariz. Const. art. 3. The court held the prosecutorial concurrence could have been severed from the statute and affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the deferred entry of defendant's judgment of guilt for her conviction of custodial interference.

913 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Beltran


No. 1 CA-CR 91-292


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department E


170 Ariz. 406; 825 P.2d 27; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 26; 105 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



February 4, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 91-00449. The Honorable Gregory H. Martin, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which upon defendant's conviction imposed a fine plus a 40 percent surcharge under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-2403. Defendant argued that the trial court improperly applied the 40 percent surcharge under the amended statute as an ex post facto law, rather than the 37 percent surcharge the statute required at the time of the offense.


OVERVIEW: Between the time of defendant's offense and his sentencing, the amended Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-2403 went into effect and changed the mandatory surcharge from 37 percent to 40 percent. When the trial court imposed the 40 percent surcharge, defendant argued that the trial court applied the law unconstitutionally ex post facto. On review, the court held that whether the law was applied ex post facto depended on whether it was considered a substantive law or a procedural one; procedural laws could be applied retroactively but substantive laws could not. The court concluded that by law, the surcharge was considered a criminal penalty, and therefore, the additional or increased penalty provided for the crime after the crime was committed was impermissibly ex post facto within the constitutional prohibition. The trial court should have imposed the 37 percent surcharge.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to impose the 37 percent surcharge rather than the 40 percent surcharge, and as so modified affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State of Arizona v. Randy Joseph Wedding

Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A

915 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Dale Michael Landi v. Bernard Arkules


Nos. 1 CA-CV 89-361, 1 CA-CV 89-505


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


172 Ariz. 126; 835 P.2d 458; 1992 Ariz. App. LEXIS 1; 103 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 54



January 9, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 3, 1992. Petition and Cross-Petition for Review Denied September 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 88-10541. The Honorable E. G. Noyes, Jr., Judge. (Motion for Reconsideration Granted)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, lawyer and his wife, investigator and his wife, business, business owner and her husband, challenged the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied their motion for a new trial. Appellee heir filed suit to rescind an heir locator agreement he executed with the business and have it declared void and unenforceable, or for reformation of the agreement for a fair fee. He was granted summary judgement.


OVERVIEW: The business was an Illinois business entity engaged in the location of heirs. The business owner's brother discovered an unprobated estate in Arizona. He located some heirs, and the lawyer was hired to represent them. The lawyer received information that the heir had a superior claim to the estate than the others. The heir executed an agreement with the business and agreed to a fee of 40 percent of the estate. The lawyer was hired to represent him. The heir later hired his own attorney and filed suit to have the contract declared unenforceable. The trial court granted summary judgement to the heir and denied the motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court held that Arizona law was the proper law to be applied, and under Arizona law the heir locator contract was unenforceable as contrary to public policy. The investigator and the business owner were not licensed as private investigators. The lack of the required licenses voided the contract. The court found that the contract was unenforceable because the fee exceeded the statutory maximum of 30 percent of the value of the recovered property. It held that the claim of relief under unjust enrichment was not properly pled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgement and its denial of the motion for a new trial. The heir locator agreement between the heir and the business was unenforceable under Arizona law because neither the investigator nor the business owner were licensed by the state as private investigators, and a contract for the services of an unlicensed private investigator violated public policy and was void.

 

916 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Superior Court


1 CA-SA 91-210


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


171 Ariz. 511; 831 P.2d 1279; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 342; 103 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 33



December 31, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Leave to File Amicus Curiae Brief on Behalf of Evelyn Touchette, Granted July 7, 1992. Petition for Review Granted. The case will be set for oral argument. As Corrected July 10, 1992.
Petition for Review Granted July 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Special Action from the Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CV 90-18731. The Honorable Robert D. Myers, Judge



DISPOSITION: RELIEF GRANTED, REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff survivors brought an action against defendants, physician and his wife, for medical malpractice. The Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) ruled that the periodic payment statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-581 through 12-591, was unconstitutional. The physician and his wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The survivors brought an action against the physician and his wife for medical malpractice resulting in the death of the survivors' family member. The trial court found that the periodic payment statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-581 through 12-591, was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court disagreed and found that the statute, which allowed for the periodic payment of any judgment for loss of future economic benefits in medical malpractice cases, was constitutional. The statute did not unconstitutionally limit the survivors' recovery of damages. It was true that one or more of the survivors might die prematurely and thus not receive the full amount of damages or be able to will the damages to an heir. The survivors' right to transmit property on death, however, was not a fundamental right. It was also true that the physician and his wife might go bankrupt and be unable to pay the judgment, but Ariz. Const. art. II, § 31, and art. XVIII, § 6, were not designed to protect the survivors from an uncollectable judgment. The periodic payment statute did not deny the survivors the equal protection of the laws. Nor was it a special law in violation of Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 2, § 19.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the action to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with its opinion that the periodic payment statute was constitutional in medical malpractice actions.

 

917 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Lou Grubb Chevrolet v. Indus. Comm'n of Ariz.


No. 1 CA-IC 90-126


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


171 Ariz. 183; 829 P.2d 1229; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 343; 103 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



December 31, 1991  
December 31, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action--Industrial Commission. ICA CLAIM NO. 89293-137206. CARRIER NO. 73X 018943. Administrative Law Judge Anthony F. Halas



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, employer and carrier, sought review of a decision of the Industrial Commission (Arizona), which granted respondent employee's workers' compensation claim. The employee requested sanctions for a frivolous appeal.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured when she leaned back into her chair and turned her head. The carrier denied compensability. The court affirmed the commission's decision granting judgment for petitioners. The court determined that Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 8 did not exclusively define the types of risks that were to be covered by the state's workers' compensation laws and that an interpretation of Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 8 that permitted compensability for actual and positional risks did not result in an unconstitutional taking of property without due process of law. The employee's injury occurred by accident under Arizona law because pain was not an unexpected consequence of the movement that she made. The employee moved her head for a business reason rather than a personal one, therefore the injury occurred in the course of employment. The legislature had the inherent power to enact workers' compensation coverage and that power was not expressly denied to the legislature because its exercise was not contrary to an express power. Liability without fault was commonplace and did not subject the workers' compensation legislation to strict scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's decision granting the employee's workers' compensation claim and denied the employee's request for sanctions.

 

918 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


GOTLAND v. TOWN OF CAVE CREEK


1 CA-CV 89-562


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


837 P.2d 1132; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 324; 101 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 52



December 10, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 88-22657. The Honorable Paul A. Katz, Judge and The Honorable Daniel E. Nastro, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied its request for injunctive relief against appellee property owners. Appellant had declared a road to be a public highway, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1861(B), and had sought to prevent appellees from erecting a barricade which blocked access to an unpaved portion of that road.


OVERVIEW: Appellee property owners filed an action for inverse condemnation against appellant town, based upon appellant's declaration that a road passing over appellees' property was a public highway. Appellees also contended that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1861(B) was unconstitutional. The trial court granted partial summary judgment, holding that the statute permitted an unconstitutional taking without just compensation. Appellant sought an injunction against any present or future barricade over the road. The trial court denied the request, holding that appellant had an adequate remedy at law. Appellant sought review, and the court reversed and remanded, holding that § 28-1861(B) was constitutional. The court held that there could be no unconstitutional taking where appellees had lost their property rights by failing to preserve them from public use. The court noted that once appellees' rights were lost, there was no right to compensation and that appellant had a right to the property. Accordingly, the statute was constitutional. The matter was remanded for an evaluation as to appellant's request for an injunction, as there was no adequate remedy at law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision, holding that a statute which authorized appellant town to take property for a public highway after a period of time of use by the public was constitutional. The court held that where property rights of appellee property owners had been lost to the public, there could be no taking and therefore no right to compensation. The matter was remanded for a determination as to the injunction request.
