Estate of Hernandez by Hernandez-Wheeler v. Ariz. Bd. of Regents


Nos. 2 CA-CV 90-0191, 2 CA-CV 90-0219, 2 CA-CV 90-0252, 2 CA-CV 90-0257


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


172 Ariz. 522; 838 P.2d 1283; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 317; 101 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 87



November 29, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted on Issues 1, 2, 5, and 6, and Denied on all other Issues November 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 255362. Honorable Lina S. Rodriguez, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for negligence, appellant administratrix sought review of a summary judgment granted by the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) for appellees, national fraternity, local chapter, fraternity members, and state board of regents, claiming that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-312(B), which purportedly gave immunity to appellees, did not apply to the matter and, alternatively, that it was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In an action for negligence, appellant administratrix charged that appellees, national fraternity, local chapter, fraternity members, and state board of regents, were liable for her decedent's injuries and death that resulted from a collision with an underage, intoxicated fraternity member who had recently driven away from a fraternity party. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees. On review, appellant claimed that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-312(B), which purportedly gave immunity to appellees, did not apply and that it was unconstitutional. In affirming the summary judgment for appellees, the court reconciled § 4-312(B) with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-301, which provided immunity to a social host only if the person furnished alcohol was over 21. The court concluded that § 4-312(B) implicitly repealed § 4-301 by rendering it essentially redundant. The court also held § 4-312(B) was constitutional. Although § 4-312(B) provided immunity to appellees for appellant's loss, thereby abrogating a cause of action, appellant recovered damages from the intoxicated driver, so that § 4-312(B) did not violate the constitutional provisions against the abrogation of a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment below for appellees, national fraternity, local chapter, fraternity members, and state board of regents, in the action by appellant administratrix for negligence because a social host was immune from liability in damages for injuries or death caused by someone to whom it served liquor, regardless of that person's age, and the statute that provided the immunity was constitutional.

Dunn v. Indus. Comm'n of Ariz.


No. 2 CA-IC 91-0019


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


171 Ariz. 463; 831 P.2d 839; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 318; 101 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 95



November 29, 1991  
November 29, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 4, 1991. Review Granted June 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: SPECIAL ACTION - INDUSTRIAL COMMISSION. ICA Claim No. 137-26-0263. Bill H. Enriquez, Administrative Law Judge



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an employee's widow, child, and stepchildren, sought special action review of the award of respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona that dismissed petitioners' claim for death benefits under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1046 for lack of jurisdiction. An administrative law judge (ALJ) found that petitioners were not dependents under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1064 at the time of the employee's injury. Respondent carrier was also a party.


OVERVIEW: The employee sustained an industrial injury and received workers' compensation benefits. At the time of the injury, the employee was married to his former wife. After a divorce, the employee married the widow. The employee and the widow had one child together, and the widow had two children from a prior marriage. The employee died from a complication from the injury. Petitioners' death benefit claim was denied. At a hearing, the ALJ dismissed the case. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court read Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1046 in conjunction with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1064 and held that the widow was not a dependent. Although § 23-1064(A)(1) stated that a wife was conclusively presumed dependent upon a husband whom she had not voluntarily abandoned at the time of the injury, the crucial time for the presumption to be effective was at the time of injury. The widow was not married to the employee at the time of injury. The employee's child and stepchildren were not entitled to death benefits because they were neither born nor dependent upon the employee at the time of the injury. Because the employee elected to receive benefits, petitioners could not bring a wrongful death action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal.

Findlay v. Lewis


No. 1 CA-HC 90-004


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


171 Ariz. 454; 831 P.2d 830; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 300; 99 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



November 7, 1991  
November 7, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted June 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CV-90-23593; The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) that dismissed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus against respondent prison officials for his transfer from a Utah prison to an Arizona prison based upon the Western Interstate Correctional Compact (compact), codified as Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 31-471 to -475.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner alleged that he was unconstitutionally confined and that the prison officials had denied his constitutional right of access to the courts. The court found that the trial court denied the petitioner's motion for an extension of time to file a response to the prison officials' motion to dismiss but that the record showed no opposition to the motion for more time. The petitioner averred that the prison officials had not provided him with any access to Utah law so that he could challenge his transfer to the Arizona prison. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court reasoned that the right of access to the courts clearly extended to the inmates' challenges to the legality of their confinement or the conditions of their confinement. The state had an affirmative obligation when the inmate was an indigent prisoner. The state was not always bound to provide a lawyer to the inmate but it must provide some form of legal assistance adequate for a meaningful opportunity to be heard in court. Here, the state was required to furnish the inmate with adequate legal materials to ensure his access to the courts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of the inmate's request for a writ of habeas corpus based on his interstate transfer of prisons.

State v. Tober


Nos. 1 CA-CR 88-1458, 1 CA-CR 88-1459


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


170 Ariz. 573; 826 P.2d 1199; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 254; 96 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 91



September 26, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted April 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CR-88-01976; The Honorable Barry G. Silverman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendants appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) that convicted defendants after a jury trial under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1841 and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1842 when defendants sold unregistered securities and sold securities by unregistered salesman.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendants were convicted after a jury trial for the sale of unregistered securities and the sale of securities by an unregistered salesman. After determining whether the notes were securities by a seven-factor test, if the jury found the notes not to be securities, it was instructed that defendants had no duty to register the notes as securities or themselves as securities dealers. The defendants contended that because no one could have known in advance under Arizona's statutory scheme whether the notes at issue here crossed that line from commercial transaction (non-security) to investment transaction (security), the statutes failed to specifically define the crime. The court determined that defining security to mean any note under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1841 and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1842 was vague and that a limiting instruction would not cure the constitutional taint of vagueness. The court reversed the convictions and sentences of defendants.


OUTCOME: Defendants' sentences and convictions for the sale of unregistered securities and sale of securities by an unregistered salesman were reversed because the statutory definition of security as any note was vague and a limiting instruction would not cure the vagueness.

Nation v. Colla


No. 1 CA-CV 89-501


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


173 Ariz. 245; 841 P.2d 1370; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 265; 96 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 75



September 26, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied and Opinion Modified July 20, 1992. * Petition and Cross-Petition for Review Withdrawn December 29, 1992.


*  Jacobson, J., would grant the Motion to Reconsider the entire result.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. C-609931; The Honorable Harold A. Frederick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant caseworker appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which awarded plaintiff decedent's parents damages on their claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for the wrongful removal of decedent and his subsequent death. Plaintiffs cross-appealed from the dismissal of their state tort claims.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff decedent's parents brought an action against defendant caseworker under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and state tort law for the wrongful removal of decedent, a two-month old boy, and his subsequent death. The trial court determined that defendant was only entitled to qualified immunity for her conduct and actions, dismissed plaintiffs' state tort law claims because they were barred by limitations, and upheld a jury verdict of damages for plaintiffs on the § 1983 claim. The court reversed the trial court and held that defendant was entitled to absolute immunity for her actions relating to the dependency proceedings and, thus, the § 1983 claim based on those activities was barred. The court found that defendant's conduct in her investigation was entitled to qualified immunity and that her conduct did not violate a clearly established statutory or constitutional right and, thus, the plaintiff's claim was barred. The court reversed the trial court's decision to dismiss the state tort law claims because there was sufficient evidence to create a jury question of whether there was excusable neglect that defeated the limitations period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision and found that as a matter of law defendant caseworker's conduct and activities were subject to an unbroken chain of absolute and qualified immunity and, thus, the court dismissed the federal claim. The court reversed the lower court's dismissal of the state law tort claims and remanded the matter to a jury.

 

926 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Five Thousand Five Hundred & 00/100 Dollars


No. 1 CA-CV 89-588


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


169 Ariz. 156; 817 P.2d 960; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 241; 96 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



September 19, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CV 89-91040; The Honorable David L. Roberts, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which entered an order of forfeiture and clear title to appellee state against currency and a revolver seized during an arrest of the owner for an illegal drug offense.


OVERVIEW: The owner was served with a notice of seizure for forfeiture. Instead of filing a claim asserting his interest in the property, the owner filed a motion to dismiss the complaint alleging that it failed to state a claim. The state responded, urging the trial court to deny the motion because the owner's failure to file a claim left him without standing to file the motion to dismiss. On appeal from the judgment in favor of the state, the court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4311(D) required the owner to file a claim within 30 days of the notice of forfeiture and that the deadline was not extended by his filing a motion. Ariz. R. Civ. P. 12(a)(1) extended the time for filing a responsive pleading, but not a claim. The court found that in an in rem forfeiture proceeding, the property rather than the owner was the party. To contest the forfeiture, the owner was required to become a "claimant" by filing a claim. Affirming the judgment, the court held that the owner failed to demonstrate his standing by filing a timely claim setting forth his interest in the property at issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which ordered the owner's property forfeited and provided clear title to the state.

 

927 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Woods v. Filler


No. 1 CA-SA 91-104


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department E


169 Ariz. 224; 818 P.2d 209; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 236; 95 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 67



September 12, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action; Maricopa County Superior Court Cause No. CV 91-05857; The Honorable Charles A. Filler, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state requested a stay of proceedings in the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), where the respondents, business owners, objected to hearsay testimony in an order to show cause hearing pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4310(B), and asserted that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4310(E)(2) was unconstitutional because it invaded the supreme court's rule making authority.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a notice of seizure and pending forfeiture of personal property belonging to owners. At show cause hearing, the state offered hearsay testimony to establish probable cause. The owners objected to the hearsay testimony, asserting that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4310(E)(2), which permitted hearsay testimony to establish probable cause, was unconstitutional. The trial court sustained the objection. On appeal, the court held § 13-4310(E)(2), as applied to order to show cause hearings, was constitutional and that the trial court had erred in excluding the hearsay testimony. Recognizing that Ariz. Const. art. 6, § 5(5) gave the supreme court the power to promulgate the rules of evidence and hearsay testimony was admissible to prove probable cause in other hearings wherein only preliminary determinations were made, the court held that the exception to the hearsay rule provided in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4310(E)(2) was consistent with the purpose of the hearsay exceptions in Ariz. R. Evid. 803 and 804. The court rejected the owners' assertion that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4310(E)(2) was not reasonable and workable because it treated the parties to a forfeiture action differently.


OUTCOME: The court held that the statute permitting hearsay evidence in show cause hearings was constitutional and a reasonable and workable supplement to other rulings promulgated by the court. The court determined that the trial court erred in excluding hearsay testimony in the order to show cause hearing and lifted the stay. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Byers v. Wik


No. 1 CA-CV 89-576


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department E


169 Ariz. 215; 818 P.2d 200; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 228; 95 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 32



September 10, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CV 89-11794; The Honorable Robert D. Myers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trustee sought review of the decision by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed his action to quiet title in property that was sold at public sale to buyers without notice to trustee.


OVERVIEW: A former spouse of the owner of certain real property obtained a judgment against him which was published in the county recorder's office. The owner then put this piece of property in a trust, naming himself as trustee. After this, the former spouse issued a writ of general execution in aid of her judgment and the sheriff posted notice of the sale of the property on her behalf. No actual notice was given to the trustee. The sale was held where buyers purchased the property. The trustee then filed an action to quiet title but the trial court granted judgment for the purchasers after finding that the notice by the sheriff was adequate. The trustee appealed, and the court reversed the lower court. The court found that the notice was inadequate because the owner's information was readily accessible. The court held that when such information was available, actual notice should have been given.


OUTCOME: The court found that the trustee had not been given adequate notice before the sale of the property and therefore reversed and remanded the action.

Ariz. Ctr. for Law in Pub. Interest v. Hassell


No. 1 CA-CV 89-134


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


172 Ariz. 356; 837 P.2d 158; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 231; 23 ELR 20348; 95 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



September 10, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Dismissed on October 6, 1992 by Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-92-0076-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CV 87-20506; The Honorable Cheryl K. Hendrix, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public interest groups filed suit against appellee state officials, claiming that Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 37-1101 to 37-1108, 12-510, and 12-529 were unconstitutional. The Superior Court of Maricopa County ruled in favor of the state officials and the public interest groups appealed.


OVERVIEW: The public interest groups claimed that the statute violated the gift clause of Ariz. Const., art. IX, § 7, the special law clause of Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 2, §§ 19(6), 19(13), and 19(18), and the state's sovereign duty to protect the public trust. The public interest groups sought a declaratory judgment invalidating certain portions of the act, a declaratory judgment invalidating quitclaim deeds already issued pursuant to the act, and an injunction against issuance of further quitclaim deeds. The court held that when a court reviewed a dispensation of the public trust property, public purpose and fair consideration must be shown, and the statute violated the public trust doctrine and gift clause because the statute failed to provide a mechanism for particularized assessment of (1) the validity of the equal footing claims that it relinquished; (2) the continuing value of land subject to such claims for purposes consistent with the public trust; (3) equitable and reasonable consideration for claims that could be relinquished without impairing the public trust; and (4) conditions that could be necessary to any transfer to assure that public trust interests remain protected.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

State of Arizona v. Floyd Orville Peterson

*  Corcoran and Martone, JJ., of the Supreme Court, voted to grant review.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Coconino County; Cause No. CR-13448-87; The Honorable H. Jeffrey Coker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Coconino County (Arizona) denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence on the ground that it was the fruit of an illegal arrest and subsequently convicted and sentenced defendant for theft of property having a value between $ 500 and $ 1,000. Defendant appealed the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: A home was burglarized and it was determined that various household items had been stolen. A detective identified defendant as a possible suspect and a computer check revealed that defendant was the subject of an outstanding arrest warrant. The existence of the warrant was confirmed with the originating agency. This information was incorporated into a search warrant affidavit, and a search warrant was issued and served. The items observed by the detective were seized and introduced as evidence at defendant's trial. At the hearing on defendant's motion to suppress, it was revealed that the arrest warrant had been quashed and erroneously re-entered into the computer system. The trial court denied defendant's motion based on the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule. Noting that defendant's conviction was based on items that were seized as a result of his illegal arrest, the appellate court reversed the conviction and remanded for the entry of an order granting defendant's motion to suppress and for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter to the trial court for (1) the entry of an order granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence, and (2) for a new trial.

Thomas M. Thomas v. City of Phoenix


No. 1 CA-CV 90-173


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C

August 27, 1991  
August 27, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 5, 1992. Reconsideration Denied October 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CV 89-08673; The Honorable Elizabeth Stover, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied their application for attorneys' fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 and which dismissed their action that sought a judgment reinstating a decision of the board of adjustment and that sought declarative and injunctive relief based on the alleged unconstitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-462.06(J).

Stat. § 9-462.06(J) became moot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment with respect to the denial of the homeowners' application for an award of attorneys' fees and remanded the case for a determination of the amount to be awarded. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court with respect to the dismissal of the remainder of the homeowners' action that sought reinstatement of the board of adjustment decision and declarative and injunctive relief.

Caldwell v. Pima County


No. 2 CA-CV 90-0273


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


172 Ariz. 352; 837 P.2d 154; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 193; 94 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 74



August 22, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County; Cause No. 258039; Honorable William L. Scholl, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vendor sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which found that appellee, a county board of supervisors (board) did not act illegally, arbitrarily, capriciously, or in abuse of its discretion in affirming a zoning enforcement hearing officer's finding that the vendor had violated appellee county's zoning code.


OVERVIEW: The vendor was cited for operating a mobile, open fruit-vegetable stand at an intersection, in violation of Pima County, Ariz., Code § 18.43.020(A). Section 18.43.020(A) required all business within a specified zone to be conducted in completely enclosed buildings unless otherwise specified. A zoning hearing officer (officer) found the vendor in violation of the ordinance and imposed a fine. The board affirmed the officer's decision. The vendor appealed pursuant to the Administrative Review Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-901 through 12-914, and the trial court affirmed the action of the board. On review, the court affirmed, holding that board did not act illegally, arbitrarily, capriciously, or in abuse of its discretion. The court found that the officer had jurisdiction to rule on the vendor's violation. The court noted that the zoning code did not arbitrarily prohibit the vendor from operating a legitimate business; it merely prohibited businesses in a specified zone from operating in other than completely enclosed buildings. Finally, the court found that the enclosed building zone requirement passed the rational basis test and thus, did not violate the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the board did not illegally, arbitrarily, capriciously, or in abuse of its discretion in affirming a zoning enforcement hearing officer's determination that the vendor had violated the county zoning code.

LAIDLAW WASTE SYS. v. CITY OF PHOENIX


No. 1 CA-CV 89-581


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


168 Ariz. 563; 815 P.2d 932; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 196; 93 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



August 20, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CV 88-14849; The Honorable E.G. Noyes, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sanitation and waste-handling companies appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) that dismissed their amended complaint alleging that defendant city had taken their property without providing just compensation.


OVERVIEW: The sanitation and waste-handling companies claimed that the city's extension of its sanitation regulations and services into the newly annexed area of the city constituted a compensible taking under the United States Constitution and the Arizona Constitution because it resulted in economic hardship to them. The trial court dismissed their amended complaint. On appeal, the court reviewed the motion to dismiss, taking as true the facts alleged by the non-moving parties. The court determined that there was no inverse condemnation and no unconstitutional taking of the sanitation and waste-handling companies' property without just compensation. The sanitation and waste-handling companies conceded that the city's sanitation regulations were proper and enforceable exercises of its governmental powers. The court ruled that the city's activities created lawful competition with the sanitation and waste-handling companies, but did not foreclose the sanitation and waste-handling companies from participation in providing services to the annexed area. The trial court's dismissal was affirmed.


OUTCOME: On appeal, the court held that the city's actions did not effect a taking. Accordingly, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed the sanitation and waste-handling companies' amended complaint.

Tempe v. Fleming


No. 1 CA-CV 89-226


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


168 Ariz. 454; 815 P.2d 1; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 161; 91 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 60



July 18, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. C-580764; The Honorable David L. Grounds, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted partial summary judgment in favor of appellee city in its action to condemn the owner's residential property for a necessary and public use. The owner contended that the city did not have the authority to abate a nuisance on his property by eminent domain pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1111(6).


OVERVIEW: The owner and the city had been involved in a long-standing dispute concerning the abandoned vehicles, weeds, trash, and other debris on the owner's property. The city council had declared that the eminent domain action was necessary to abate a nuisance and to restore the property to a habitable condition. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's order granting partial summary judgment in favor of the city. The court held that the owner on appeal did not waive the right to challenge the condemnation based on his failure to respond to the city's motion for partial summary judgment. On the merits of the appeal, the court held that the city did not have authority to abate the nuisance on the owner's property through the power of eminent domain. The court found that the condemnation did not relate to the taking of property for the purpose of constructing roads, streets, and alleys, as permitted by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1111(6). The court stated that the city had the specific statutory authority to remove the debris on the owner's property and to assess the cost of removal as a lien upon the property, thus, permitting judicial foreclosure if the owner did not pay the cost.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting partial summary judgment in favor of the city in the eminent domain action, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

935 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Beckerman


No. 1 CA-CR 90-207


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department E


168 Ariz. 451; 814 P.2d 1388; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 165; 91 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 67



July 18, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CR-89-04002; The Honorable Mark W. Armstrong, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) to two counts of sale of narcotic drugs, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408. Defendant's sentence included concurrent prison terms, a felony assessment of $ 200.00, a fine of $ 2,740.00 and an $ 8.00 time payment fee (TPF), which was imposed under Ariz. Rev. Stat. 12-116. On appeal, defendant claimed error in the imposition of the TPF.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-116, which authorized assessment of an $ 8.00 TPF on any person who paid a court penalty, fine, or sanction on a time basis was an ex post facto law and also that it violated equal protection. Addressing defendant's claim, the court noted that § 12-116 provided that a part of the TPF was required to be deposited into the judicial collection enhancement fund, some of which would be used for county public defender training, whereas another portion of it could be utilized by the court imposing the TPF in order to improve, maintain and enhance the court's ability to collect and manage monies. Because precedent had declared § 12-116 to be procedural in nature and that it did not impose any penalty upon a defendant, the court rejected defendant's claim that it violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws set forth in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. Because § 12-116 did not impact a fundamental right and it was rationally related to the legitimate state interest of facilitating the collection of fines, penalties, and sanction, it withstood defendant's equal protection attack.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, finding no error in the sentence imposed upon defendant.

Davis v. Cessna Aircraft Corp.


No. 1 CA-CV 89-306


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


168 Ariz. 301; 812 P.2d 1119; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 108; 86 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 47



May 16, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause Nos. CV 87-38359 and CV 87-38360 Consolidated; The Honorable Albert M. Goldberg, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED; CAUSE REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed their strict liability claim against defendant airplane manufacturer for alleged defects in the design, manufacture and labeling of an airplane that crashed, killing their children, one of whom was the pilot.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the airplane manufacturer's motion to dismiss the parents' strict liability claim, in which it argued that the claims were barred by Arizona's 12-year limitations period for product liability cases. The order of dismissal contained Ariz. R. Civ. P. 54(b) language, which allows a trial court to certify finality to a judgment that disposes of one or more, but not all, of multiple claims upon a determination that there is no just reason for delay and directs the entry of judgment. The parents objected to the language because they also asserted negligence claims against the airplane manufacturer, but the order was entered anyway. The parents filed a notice of appeal. The court dismissed the appeal, holding that it lacked jurisdiction in the case because the order of dismissal was not a final judgment despite the Rule 54(b) language in the order. The court found that the judgment was not final because it did not dispose of a separate claim of a multi-claim action, as required. The court stated that the strict liability claim was not separate from the negligence claim, but merely a separate, alternative theory of recovery.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the parents' appeal of their strict liability claim against the airplane manufacturer for alleged defects in an airplane.

State v. Everhart


No. 2 CA-CR 90-0029


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


169 Ariz. 404; 819 P.2d 990; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 103; 86 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 64



May 14, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion on Motion for Reconsideration June 27, 1991. Review Denied November 19, 1991. *


*  Cameron and Corcoran, JJ., of the Supreme Court, voted to grant review.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County; Cause No. CR-21174; Honorable Howard Hantman, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which accepted defendant's plea and imposed a maximum sentence of 15 years in prison to run consecutively to a federal sentence defendant was serving. The trial court also ordered that defendant be placed on lifetime probation upon his release from prison. Defendant pled guilty to one count of attempted child molestation, a dangerous crime against children.


OVERVIEW: Defendant met the victim as an umpire for the victim's baseball team in March 1987. Shortly thereafter, numerous sexual encounters occurred. Defendant took the victim camping on April 26, 1987, and then drove him to California. Defendant was convicted in federal court of kidnapping and transportation of a minor for sexual purposes. Defendant pled guilty in this case to attempted child molestation occurring on or about April 18, 1987. Counsel argued that the imposition of lifetime probation was unlawful and that the imposition of a consecutive sentence violated appellant's constitutional protection against double jeopardy. The court modified and affirmed as modified. The court held that: (1) where Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01 authorized probation in lieu of, and not in addition to, the imposition of sentence on one offense, the trial court erred in imposing lifetime probation in addition to the prison sentence; (2) the trial court did not err in imposing a consecutive sentence; and (3) the presentence report contained sufficient evidence from which the trial court could have concluded that the victim suffered severe emotional trauma as a result of defendant's repeated molestations.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's sentence to delete the order of probation. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the sentence as modified.

 

938 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Padilla


No. 1 CA-CR 89-759


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


169 Ariz. 70; 817 P.2d 15; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 98; 86 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 15



May 2, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County; Cause No. CR-13474; The Honorable Richard Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which convicted him of offering to sell a narcotic in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408 and sentenced him to a mandatory seven years in prison. Defendant argued that his conviction violated his right to free speech, that the statute was overbroad, and that his sentence was disproportionate to his crime.


OVERVIEW: After the state convicted him of offering to sell a narcotic in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408, defendant appealed on two grounds. First, he argued that the statute violated both the First Amendment of the United States Constitution and Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 6, because the statute punished speech and was overbroad. Second, he argued that because the statute punished an offer to sell narcotics with the same sentence as a completed sale, his sentence was disproportionate to the crime, in violation of the Eighth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 15. The court explained that statutes were entitled to a presumption of constitutionality. The legislature had the power to define crimes and to prohibit crimes in which speech was used to carry out the illegal act. Such speech was not protected by the state or federal constitutions. Similarly, the legislature had the power to penalize the offer to sell in the same manner as a completed sale. The "offer" was a completed crime, unlike attempt, which was generally considered less serious. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for offering to sell a narcotic.

 

939 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Takacs


Nos. 1 CA-CR 89-1238, 1 CA-CR 89-1239


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


169 Ariz. 392; 819 P.2d 978; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 78; 84 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



April 11, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied November 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CR-89-05032; The Honorable Kenneth L. Fields, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from the dismissal by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) of an indictment charging two defendants with multiple counts of promotion of gambling, a felony, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3303, based upon a trial court finding that § 13-3303 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court dismissed defendants' indictment for multiple counts of felony promotion of gambling, violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3303, as void for vagueness, the State challenged the trial court's conclusion that § 13-3303 was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court found that § 13-3303 was not unconstitutionally vague even though § 13-3301(1) did not define the phrase "control to any material degree" with respect to amusement gambling, and § 13-3301(6) did not define the phrases "conducted as a business" and "compete on equal terms" with respect to social gambling. The court determined that the phrases in question were to be given their ordinary meaning and therefore gave defendants fair notice of the conduct that was prohibited. The court concluded that a person of ordinary intelligence was capable of understanding the meaning of the phrases in question. Accordingly, the court vacated the dismissal of defendants' gambling indictment because § 13-3303 was not unconstitutionally vague. The matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.


OUTCOME: The court found that the felony gambling statute in question was not unconstitutionally vague. Accordingly, the court vacated the trial court's order that had dismissed the indictment of two defendants on its finding that the statute under which they were indicted was void for vagueness. The court remanded this matter to the trial court for proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Fraternal Order of Eagles Tucson Aerie #180 v. Tucson


No. 2 CA-CV 90-0237


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


168 Ariz. 598; 816 P.2d 255; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 84; 83 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 42



March 29, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied September 12, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County; Cause No. 262765; Honorable Lawrence H. Fleischman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff organization sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which affirmed defendant city's ruling requiring the organization to admit four women to membership and subjected it to a fine for violating the city ordinance against discrimination, Tucson, Ariz., City Code § 17-12.


OVERVIEW: Four women filed a complaint with the city after they were rejected for membership into the organization. After an administrative hearing, the city ordered the organization to admit the women and ruled that the women's rejection violated § 17-12. The trial court affirmed the city's ruling, and on appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that because the organization engaged in a mixture of public and private activities, it was subject to § 17-12. The court further held that because the organization donated its funds to charities, it was not exempt from § 17-12 pursuant to Tucson, Ariz., City Code § 17-13. Finally, the court held that because the city had a compelling interest in eradicating gender discrimination, Tucson, Ariz., City Code § 17-12 was a permissible infringement on the organization's right of freedom of expressive association.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court, which affirmed the city's ruling requiring the organization to admit four women to membership and subjected it to a fine for violating the city ordinance against discrimination.

 

941 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Cacavas v. Bowen


No. 2 CA-SA 91-0020


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


168 Ariz. 114; 811 P.2d 366; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 58; 82 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



March 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 21, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action Proceedings.



DISPOSITION: RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged orders of the City Court of Tucson, in the State of Arizona, County of Pima, which denied their motions to dismiss on the grounds that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(A)(2) (1990) was unconstitutional. Defendants were charged with violating § 28-692(A)(2), which prohibited a person from having a blood alcohol content (BAC) of 0.10 percent or more within two hours of driving or being in actual physical control of the vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that § 28-692 was unconstitutional because it reallocated the burden of proof on defendant by labeling as an affirmative defense, not having a BAC of 0.10 percent at the time of driving, an element of the crime that was in a previous statute. The court found that § 28-692 had created a new crime and was not unconstitutional simply because it did not contain the same elements of the statute it replaced. The court found that § 28-692 raised no impermissible presumption that one who had a BAC of 0.10 percent within two hours of operating a motor vehicle also had a blood alcohol content of 0.10 percent at the time he operated a motor vehicle. The court found that the statute was violated by having the requisite BAC not only at the time of operating the motor vehicle but also within two hours thereafter. The court also rejected the argument that the statute impermissibly shifted the burden of proof by requiring defendant to prove facts that were more easily demonstrated by the state. The court affirmed and concluded that § 28-692 was not overbroad because the state had a compelling interest in reducing the terrible toll of life and limb on the state's highways.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders denying defendants' motions to dismiss.

 

942 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re Pima County Mental Health


No. 2 CA MH 90-0004


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


169 Ariz. 141; 817 P.2d 945; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 55; 82 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 39



March 14, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 22, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County; Cause No. MH 2081-3-90; Honorable Laurel B. Sammons, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which ordered inpatient treatment at the Arizona State Hospital, based upon a finding by the trial court of clear and convincing evidence that he was persistently disabled. The patient contended that the treatment should have been dismissed because was no reasonable basis for the findings and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-501(29) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered the patient to have been committed to a state psychiatric hospital and the patient appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision and found that the trial court had clear and convincing evidence that the patient was acutely disabled and required inpatient treatment. The court found that the patient had not been denied due process because the petition for custodial evaluation alleged the patient was persistently or acutely disabled, as did the order for detention, the doctors' affidavits and the three physicians' evaluations. The court also found that § 36-501(29) was not unconstitutionally vague. Those who are mentally incompetent to make judgments did not need fair warning of the condition that required treatment and that § 36-501(29) required that commitments were made under judicial supervision after factual findings based on constitutionally appropriate standards. The court found that testimony supported the conclusion that the trial court had a reasonable basis to find by clear and convincing evidence that the patient was persistently or acutely disabled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court and found that the testimony supported the conclusion that the trial court had a reasonable basis to have found by clear and convincing evidence that the patient was persistently or acutely disabled.

 

943 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sheehan


No. 1 CA-CR 89-1330


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


167 Ariz. 370; 807 P.2d 538; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 50; 81 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 21



March 5, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CR-88-06094; The Honorable John Foreman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of a drug offense and was placed on probation for three years. One year later, defendant pleaded guilty to committing two civil traffic offenses, driving without proper registration and driving left of center. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) modified the conditions of defendant's probation to require three months' incarceration. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant alleged that the civil traffic offenses admitted by him did not violate the standard term of his probation that generally required him to "obey all laws." In reversing the trial court's judgment, the court ruled that the phrase "obey all laws," in the context of a probation document, was to be construed to exclude civil traffic offenses. The Arizona Legislature, by decriminalizing numerous traffic offenses, determined as a matter of public policy that those offenses were not as morally reprehensible as criminal acts. A civil traffic offense was different in substance and effect from a criminal offense. Thus, the trial court erred in finding a violation of defendant's probation terms.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's judgment and restored the original conditions of defendant's probation.

 

944 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Terrell


No. 2 CA-CR 90-0535


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


168 Ariz. 112; 811 P.2d 364; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 41; 81 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 42



February 28, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review by Supreme Court Denied June 11, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Cochise County; Cause No. JP90-00134; Honorable Richard A. Winkler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of Cochise County (Arizona) that affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for giving false information to a police officer in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2907.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that two police officers assaulted him but he was able to struggle loose and flee. Following an investigation, the police concluded that the two officers on duty that evening had not assaulted defendant, who was ultimately charged with filing a false report in violation of § 13-2907.01. Defendant was found guilty, and the superior court affirmed the conviction. On appeal, defendant argued that § 13-2907.01 was unconstitutionally vague and overly broad. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court found that § 13-2907.01 provided reasonable persons of average intelligence with notice of the specific conduct it proscribed. Moreover, the class of people who could have been prosecuted under the statute was narrowly drawn and not overly broad. Only those persons providing the kind of information set forth in the statute with the requisite knowledge or purpose could have been found in violation of the statute. The court concluded that the state had a legitimate interest in facilitating the law enforcement process by discouraging individuals from knowingly providing information that would confound the functioning of the justice system.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for giving false information to a police officer.

Quinton v. Superior Court


No. 1 CA-SA 90-224


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department E


168 Ariz. 545; 815 P.2d 914; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 31; 80 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



February 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied September 12, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County; Cause No. CR-11525; The Honorable Leonard C. Langford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss murder charges brought pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1105, on which defendant was indicted following defendant's conviction for kidnapping, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1304.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen in the company of a woman whose body was later found in a dump. Defendant was indicted and convicted of kidnapping, under § 13-1304. Before defendant's sentencing, defendant was indicted for murder, under § 13-1105. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the murder prosecution on the ground that his protection from double jeopardy, pursuant to the Fifth Amendment, prohibited the indictment. Defendant's motion was denied, and defendant appealed. On appeal, the court reversed and ordered the murder prosecution dismissed without prejudice. The court held that because the murder prosecution involved the identical conduct and facts as the kidnapping prosecution, defendant's double jeopardy protection had attached. The court further held that defendant's attorney's objection to the consolidation of the two charges did not amount to a waiver of the double jeopardy protection because defendant had not himself executed a waiver knowingly and in open court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's decision, which denied defendant's motion to dismiss the murder prosecution and ordered that the prosecution be dismissed without prejudice.

Bruce Church, Inc. v. United Farm Workers


No. 1 CA-CV 89-180


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


169 Ariz. 22; 816 P.2d 919; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 11; 78 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



January 15, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 8, 1991. *


*  Cameron, J., of the Supreme Court, voted to grant both the appellee's petition for review and defendant/appellant's cross petition for review.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yuma County; Cause No. 49877; The Honorable H. Stewart H. Stewart Bradshaw, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant labor union challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Yuma County (Arizona), which returned a general verdict in favor of plaintiff corporation for unfair labor practices in violation of the Arizona Agricultural Employment Relations Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 23-1381 to -1395.


OVERVIEW: A corporation brought an action against the labor union for unfair labor practices. The practices alleged included engaging in a secondary boycott directed at the corporation's customers in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1385(B)(6), imposing illegal economic sanctions against the corporation, and threatening to or engaging in libel and slander to prevent the sale of the corporation's lettuce. After the trial court awarded damages to the corporation, the labor union appealed, alleging that the trial court erred in directing a verdict regarding the secondary boycott issue because none of the secondary boycott activity occurred in Arizona. The court held that the trial court had erroneously directed the jury to base their verdict on evidence of boycott activities that occurred in other states. State laws were not enforceable beyond the jurisdiction of the state which enacted them and could have extraterritorial effect only by the comity of other states.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the corporation in an action alleging unfair labor practices by the labor union.

State v. McCuin


No. 1 CA-CR 89-431


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


167 Ariz. 447; 167 Ariz. 447; 808 P.2d 332; 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 1; 77 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 33



January 8, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted as to Issue No. 3 and Review Denied as to Issue Nos. 1, 2 and 4 April 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CR-88-09427; The Honorable Rebecca A. Albrecht, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which, following pleas of guilty to two counts of sexual conduct with a minor, both class two felonies, sentenced him to an aggravated term of 14 years imprisonment on one charge, suspended imposition of sentence and imposed a concurrent probationary term of seven years on the other charge, and required him to register as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant regularly engaged in sexual conduct with his minor daughter. As a result, defendant was indicted on one count of sexual molestation of a child and three counts of sexual conduct with a minor. Defendant entered an Alford plea on two of the sexual conduct charges and was sentenced on one charge to an aggravated term of 14 years imprisonment. On the other charge, the trial court suspended imposition of sentence and imposed a concurrent probationary term of seven years. As a term of probation, the trial court required defendant to register as a sex offender pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3821. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) the trial court properly convicted and sentenced defendant on two counts of sexual conduct with a minor, as evidence sufficiently established two separate acts by defendant; (2) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in the sentences imposed; (3) § 13-3821 was regulatory rather than penal in nature; and (4) the trial court did not have a responsibility to inform defendant of the registration requirement before accepting his plea, because it was not a condition of the sentence imposed but an independent statutory requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which sentenced defendant to an aggravated term of 14 years imprisonment on one charge of sexual conduct with a minor, suspended imposition of sentence and imposed a concurrent probationary term of seven years on another charge of sexual conduct with a minor, and required him to register as a sex offender.

 

948 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Circle K Corp. v. Mesa


No. 1 CA-CV 88-205


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


166 Ariz. 464; 803 P.2d 457; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 407; 76 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 34



December 18, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. C-612828-SE; The Honorable David Grounds, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged a summary judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) in favor of appellees, city, adjustment board, board members, and building inspector, claiming that the Mesa City, Az., Code § 4-4-12(D)(6) was void because it conflicted with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-462.02 and that the ordinance allowed an unconstitutional taking of private property without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: The property owner, operating a convenience store, had a legal nonconforming sign on the property and sought to erect an additional sign. Its request for a variance was denied. The adjustment board cited Mesa City, Az., Code § 4-4-12(D)(6), and ruled that the property owner had to remove the nonconforming sign before any new ones were added. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees and denied a motion for a new trial. The court affirmed the trial court judgment, holding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-462.02 was permissive and that appellees were not limited to using purchase or condemnation to remove nonconforming uses and structures. Because under the ordinance the city could consider a parcel of land as an integrated whole, any change to part of the property was considered a change to the existing property. The statute, however, protected only existing property which remained unchanged or received only reasonable repairs or alterations. The court also ruled that because there was a direct relationship between the purposes for regulating signs and the required removal of a nonconforming sign, the condition did not constitute a taking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment for appellees and against the property owner.

Earthworks Contractor v. Mendel-Allison Constr.


No. 1 CA-CV 89-025


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


167 Ariz. 102; 804 P.2d 831; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 400; 75 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 56



December 13, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CV 88-07921; The Honorable Marilyn A. Riddel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff subcontractor brought an action against defendants, general contractor and insurer, seeking breach of contract or unjust enrichment damages. The subcontractor also asserted a claim for tortious interference with contractual relationships. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) granted the general contractor and insurer's motion to dismiss pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 32-1153. The subcontractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The general contractor contracted with an unlicensed subcontractor to pave a parking lot on a commercial construction project. When the contract was entered, contractors working on a commercial project were not required to be licensed. While the subcontractor was still performing on the contract, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 32-1101 was amended and required all contractors to be licensed. The trial court held that the subcontractor was precluded by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 32-1153 from receiving any compensation for any work it had performed because it lacked a license. The appellate court concluded that the application of § 32-1153 to the subcontractor's cause of action was an unconstitutional application of the statute because it impaired the subcontractor's rights under a contract entered into when a license was not required. U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, para. 1; Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 25. The appellate court held that the trial court erred in dismissing the claim for breach of contractual relations because the general contractor failed to allege that it was unsuccessful in attempting to have the subcontractor's employees breach their employment contracts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the subcontractor's complaint and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Vanguard Eng'g v. Superior Court


No. 1 CA-SA 90-188


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


166 Ariz. 405; 803 P.2d 126; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 402; 75 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 65



December 13, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. DR-235484; The Honorable Michael O. Wilkinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED RELIEF GRANTED IN PART, DENIED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought a special action after the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) that held him in contempt of court and assessed a fine as a penalty for the employer's failure to obey the trial court's order of wage assignment for child support payments pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2454.01 that was served on the employer by respondent state (Attorney General).


OVERVIEW: The court found the claims of error without merit, but on its own motion, ordered the Attorney General's filing of a brief addressing the issue of whether the trial court had followed proper procedures in assessing the penalty for contempt of court. Upon filing the brief, the Attorney General confessed error. The court held that the trial judge erred in fining the owner as a penalty for failing to honor a wage assignment for the employee's child support payments. The court found that the trial court treated the owner's disobedience of the order as a criminal contempt of court without affording the owner the rights and safeguards provided for by the Arizona Rules of Criminal Procedure (Rules). The court ruled that insofar as the owner was fined without regard to the Rules, the employer was correct that the Valentine's Day Roundup conducted by the domestic relations divisions resulted in Constitutional violations. The court vacated the fine and ruled that the fine, in the nature of a criminal penalty, was also improper because the employer had not waived a trial by jury, which was required pursuant to Ariz. R. Crim. P. § 33.4(a) in order to have properly assessed such a fine.


OUTCOME: The court, accepting jurisdiction, granted relief in part by vacating the fine in favor of the employer, and denied in part by finding all other claims for relief meritless in favor of the state in the employer's special action after having been held in contempt of court.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sign owner brought an action against defendants, city and city board of adjustment (board), claiming that the board abused its discretion in finding that the sign owner's sign did not conform to a city ordinance. The Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona) set aside the board's decision requiring that the owner reconstruct the sign. All parties sought review.

953 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cooper


Nos. 1 CA-CR 88-1239-PR, 1 CA-CR 88-1240-PR, 1 CA-CR 88-1241-PR, 1 CA-CR 88-1242-PR


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


166 Ariz. 126; 800 P.2d 992; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 338; 72 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



October 25, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for Review from the Superior Court; of Maricopa County; (Rule 32.9(c), Arizona Rules of Criminal Procedure); Cause Nos. CR-153567, CR-156664, CR-159363, CR-158554; The Honorable Thomas W. O'Toole, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVIEW GRANTED; RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the denials by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) of his petitions for post-conviction relief in which the inmate claimed that his learning that he was infected with human immunodeficiency virus constituted newly discovered material fact for which his sentence could have been vacated or reduced if he had been given an evidentiary hearing on his claim.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had denied the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief without providing the inmate with an evidentiary hearing. The court remanded for an evidentiary hearing. Even though the inmate's sentence had been previously affirmed on appeal, he could attack the validity of the sentencing proceedings pursuant to Ariz. R. Crim. P. 32. The inmate met the requirements of Ariz. R. Crim. P. 32.1(e) that permitted securing relief upon newly-discovered material fact that if it existed at the time of sentencing could have affected that determination. The inmate's claim that he had human immunodeficiency virus constituted a colorable claim of newly discovered material fact because he was not diagnosed until after sentencing, he was diligent in bringing the evidence to the trial court's attention, that evidence was not cumulative or impeaching, and it was relevant because an inmate's health was a factor considered at sentencing. If the inmate had the virus at the time of sentencing, the trial court at the hearing could exercise its discretion to allow the state or the inmate to withdraw from the stipulated sentences in the plea agreements.


OUTCOME: The court remanded for an evidentiary hearing whether the inmate's colorable claim of newly discovered evidence, his having human immunodeficiency virus, existed at the time of sentencing.

In re Appeal in Santa Cruz County Juvenile Dependency Action Nos. JD-89-006 & JD-89-007


Nos. 2 CA-JV 90-0022, 2 CA-JV 90-0023


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


167 Ariz. 98; 804 P.2d 827; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 341; 72 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 83



October 25, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied February 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Santa Cruz County; Cause Nos. JD-89-006 and JD-89-007; Honorable Roberto C. Montiel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Cruz County (Arizona), adjudicating their two minor children dependent and placing them in the custody of the Department of Economic Security (DES). The parents contended on appeal that they were denied due process because there was no cross-examination of the children, and counsel was ineffective in failing to object to the court interviewing the children absent counsel.


OVERVIEW: The children were 14-year-old stepbrothers, one the father's son, and one the mother's son. When they were nine, the boys started a spree of doing property damage and running away, telling DES workers that they had been beaten. Finally, the parents asked not to have the children returned to them when a voluntary placement ended, and DES filed a dependency petition. The children did not testify in court but were interviewed by the trial judge in chambers. The trial court found that the parents were not able to care for the children at the time and that the children would just again run away again if returned and be subject to danger. The court affirmed, rejecting the parents' argument that they should have been allowed to cross-examine the children. Given that neither child was called as a witness by the parents, although the possibility was discussed by counsel, it was clear that any objection to the trial judge's in-chambers interviews was waived by both counsel and the parents. The right to cross-examine the children was never refused, and therefore no due process right was violated, because the opportunity to exercise that right was never requested.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.
