Arizona State Bd. of Dental Examiners v. Fleischman


No. 2 CA-SA 90-0134


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


167 Ariz. 311; 806 P.2d 900; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 320; 70 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 61



September 28, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 7, 1990. Review Denied March 19, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action Proceedings.



DISPOSITION: RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Arizona State Board of Dental Examiners, sought review of an order of a trial court (Arizona), in which respondent judge declared unconstitutional and severable that portion of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 32-1296 which required that applicants, the real parties in interest, have a diploma in denture technology from a Board-accredited school in order to take an examination to be certified to practice.


OVERVIEW: Section 32-1296 required that in order to take an examination to be certified to practice denture technology, applicants had to have a diploma in denture technology granted by a school accredited by the Board. The trial court declared that portion of the statute to be unconstitutional and severable. On appeal, the court vacated the trial court's order and remanded the action with directions to enter judgment for the Board. The court held that the legislature permitted a rationally defined class of persons to take the licensure examination upon successful completion of a curriculum which met the requirements of the statute and was accredited by the Board. The procedure was rationally related to a legitimate legislative purpose, specifically, permitting qualified persons to become licensed during the interim in which it was presumably anticipated that institutions offering programs in denture technology would become accredited by the Board. The fact that the anticipated condition did not subsequently materialize did not render the temporary licensing provision a form of special legislation.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order and remanded the action with directions to enter judgment for the Board.

 

957 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


White v. Lewis


No. 1 CA-CV 88-615


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


167 Ariz. 76; 804 P.2d 805; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 319; 69 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



September 27, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. C-88-04286; The Honorable Stephen Gerst, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment to appellee corrections department on a complaint filed by inmate claiming that he had been denied his constitutional rights of access to the courts, his family, and sanitary supplies.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court correctly granted corrections department's motion for summary judgment because inmate had failed to respond to the motion. Moreover, he never filed affidavits controverting corrections department's statement of the facts nor did he ever argue that the actual facts presented by corrections department were untrue. Therefore, the court found that inmate's response to the motion for summary judgment was both procedurally defective and substantively without merit. As to inmate's claim that he had been denied access to the courts, the court held that inmate had demonstrated that he was articulate and able to make appropriate use of legal authority and that he had had access to the prison law library even if he did not have the services of a legal assistant. Access to the law library was sufficient to defeat inmate's claim that he had been denied access to the courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

958 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dunn


No. 2 CA-CR 89-0646


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


166 Ariz. 506; 803 P.2d 917; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 296; 68 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 46



September 6, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 13 and September 28, 1990. Reconsideration Denied October 16, 1990. Review Denied February 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Cochise County; Cause No. CR89-00238; Honorable Richard A. Winkler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of Cochise County (Arizona), which convicted him of importation of cocaine in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408(A)(7).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408(A)(7) was unconstitutional because it impinged upon the federal government's exclusive domain of regulating foreign commerce. Viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the state, the evidence at trial established that defendant took cocaine into Mexico and then re-entered Arizona with the cocaine. Upon re-entry into the United States, he was detained at a border inspection station, where it was discovered that he possessed 1.8 grams of cocaine. Defendant argued that § 13-3408(A)(7) that prohibited the importation of cocaine violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3 because the federal government had exclusive and plenary power over foreign commerce and that any attempt by a state to regulate foreign commerce was unconstitutional. Defendant also claimed that the Arizona statute punished importation more severely than its federal counterpart. The court found that Arizona's importation statute was even-handed and prohibited any importation of illegal drugs. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the Arizona statute was directly related to the exercise of police power aimed at the smuggling of illegal drugs into Arizona.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of importation of cocaine.

 

959 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


No. 1 CA-CR 89-433


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


166 Ariz. 450; 803 P.2d 443; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 290; 68 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 33



September 4, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County; Cause No. CR-10401; The Honorable Leonard C. Langford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for possession of marijuana for sale and production of marijuana from the Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for possession of marijuana for sale and production of marijuana involving more than eight pounds, and the court affirmed. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3405(C) imposed stricter penalties on those convicted of offenses involving more than eight pounds of marijuana. At trial, the marijuana seized was very dry and weighed 6.93 pounds, and an expert testified that wet marijuana weighed one-third more than dry. The court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion for acquittal because there was sufficient evidence to show that at the time of its seizure, the marijuana found weighed more than eight pounds. The court further found that a rational basis existed for the legislature's classification based on the weight of marijuana at the time it was seized, so the law was not unconstitutional. The eight-pound quantity, be it wet or dry marijuana, was enough to support the legislative assumption that a defendant was not possessing the marijuana for personal use. Thus, § 13-3405(C) clearly and rationally served a legitimate state objective of preventing the distribution of an illegal drug.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

960 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Irving


No. 1 CA-CR 89-448


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


165 Ariz. 219; 797 P.2d 1237; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 293; 68 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 28



September 4, 1990 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed a judgment of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which reversed a trial court's conviction of the defendant for driving while her license was suspended. The appellate court's order held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-110(F), which provided for self-authentication of certain Arizona Department of Transportation records, was facially unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted of driving while her driver's license was suspended. The court held that the appellate court erred when it reversed the defendant's conviction. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-110(F) was valid because it supplemented the Arizona Rules of Evidence and did not conflict with Ariz. R. Evid. 901 or 902. The court held that Ariz. R. Evid. 902 provided that certain documents were self-authenticating where such authenticity was presumed by statute and that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-110(F) was an example of such a statute. The court held that the fact that the defendant's driving record was computer generated and contained a printed facsimile of the record custodian's signature did not render the record inadmissible because § 28-110(F) did not require human involvement and absent contrary evidence, the trial court was entitled to presume that the facsimile signature of a state officer was valid. The court held that the driving record at issue was an original and not a copy pursuant to Ariz. R. Evid. 1001(3).


OUTCOME: The judgment which reversed the defendant's conviction of driving while her license was suspended was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

961 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Isbell v. Miller


No. 1 CA-CV 89-233


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department E


165 Ariz. 199; 797 P.2d 738; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 289; 68 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 21



August 30, 1990 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged a judgment from the trial court (Arizona), which affirmed an administrative order suspending his driver's license for driving under the influence of an intoxicating beverage.


OVERVIEW: The driver's expert witness prepared a report indicating that if the driver had taken a Breath Intoxilyzer Test contemporaneously with his arrest, rather than one hour later, his blood alcohol level (BAC) would have been below both the .10 found by the police and the .096 found by the expert's independent testing. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment affirming the administrative order suspending the driver's license. The court held that the administrative hearing officer correctly disregarded the extrapolation evidence presented by the expert because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-694 required that a driver's BAC be .10 or more at the time of a test, not at the time he or she was driving. In addition, the court stated that it could not construe § 28-694 as unconstitutional based on hypothetical examples presented by the driver, which did not apply to the case. Lastly, the court also stated that the driver's argument, that Arizona should have required that the operator of a breath testing device perform control tests before and after the driver took the breath test, should have been addressed to the Arizona legislature and not to the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment affirming the administrative order suspending the driver's license for driving under the influence of an intoxicating beverage.

American Fed'n of State, County & Mun. Employees, Council 97 v. Lewis


No. 1 CA-CV 88-298


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


165 Ariz. 149; 797 P.2d 6; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 276; 67 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



August 21, 1990 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state appealed the decision of the trial court (Arizona), which held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1609.01, requiring legislative council approval prior to any privatization of state prisons, was unconstitutional as violation of Ariz. Const. art. III. Plaintiff labor union and taxpayers cross appealed the trial court's ruling that § 41-1609.01 did not constitute an unconstitutional delegation of state police powers.


OVERVIEW: The labor union and taxpayers filed suit against the state seeking a judicial declaration that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1609.01 was unconstitutional because it violated the Distribution of Powers clause of Ariz. Const. art. III and because it constituted an unconstitutional delegation of state police powers. The trial court decreed that § 41-1609.01 violated art. III, but held that it was not an unconstitutional delegation. In reversing the declaratory judgment in favor of the union and taxpayers, the court held that the taxpayers had standing to bring a declaratory judgment action when direct expenditures of tax funds were made, but that the issues raised for declaratory judgment did not constitute an actual controversy ripe for adjudication when the matter was filed and no present injury was alleged.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaratory judgment in favor of the labor union and taxpayers and the matter remanded to the trial court. The court affirmed the trial court's conclusion that the statute did not constitute an unconstitutional delegation of state police powers.

 

963 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Knapp v. Miller


No. 1 CA-CV 89-083


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


165 Ariz. 527; 799 P.2d 868; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 223; 62 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 55



June 14, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied November 14, 1990.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged an order of the trial court (Arizona) that affirmed an order of appellee Arizona Department of Transportation (department) that suspended his driver's license under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-694. The driver alleged that the statute violated substantive due process, procedural due process, and equal protection of the laws.


OVERVIEW: The driver was involved in an automobile accident and given field sobriety tests and a blood alcohol test. His blood alcohol was above the legal limits and he was required to surrender his driver's license. After an administrative hearing, the hearing officer sustained the order suspending his license. The trial court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-694 required that the blood alcohol content had to be above the legal limit at the time of the test without regard to the projected reading at the time of driving. The statute was reasonably related to the legislative end of removing people who drink and drive from the roads. The statute was also not void for vagueness because it clearly gave notice that a driver faced suspension of driving privileges when he drank enough alcohol while driving to exceed the legal blood alcohol limit. A driver's license did not give rise to a constitutionally protected property interest and the administrative hearing complied with due process requirements. The right to drive was not a fundamental right and the statute was rationally related to a legitimate state purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's suspension of the driving license of the driver.

 

964 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lucas


No. 1 CA-CR 89-954


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


164 Ariz. 540; 794 P.2d 1353; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 215; 62 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



June 7, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted September 14, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 351. Vacated by Order of the Court July 30, 1991. Reconsideration Dismissed July 30, 1991. Reported at 1991 Ariz. App. LEXIS 349.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. CR-158861; The Honorable Bernard J. Dougherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of three counts of first-degree, felony-murder and one count of burglary and sentenced him to life imprisonment on the murder counts and ten years imprisonment on the burglary charge, with all counts to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued, inter alia, that a felony-murder charge could not be predicated on an assault, that several of the state's witnesses violated a pretrial ruling prohibiting reference to his prior misconduct, and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. The court affirmed the trial court's judgments and sentences. The court reasoned that although an assault which resulted in a death would not itself warrant a felony-murder charge, remaining unlawfully in a residence with the intent to commit an assault constituted a burglary and might warrant a felony-murder charge. The court concluded that appellant was properly charged with the murders of two victims because their deaths clearly occurred either during the burglary or during immediate flight therefrom. The court reasoned that an isolated remark by a detective could not have had such a prejudicial effect that a mistrial was the only remedy to preserve appellant's right to a fair trial. The court concluded that counsels' conduct did not result in the failure to preserve favorable pretrial rulings and that their trial performance was consonant with Sixth Amendment standards pertaining to effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both the judgments of the trial court, which convicted appellant of three counts of felony-murder and one count of burglary, and the sentences that the trial court imposed.

Bruce v. Chas Roberts Air Conditioning

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) entered summary judgment in favor of appellee employer in the action of appellants, parents and children, for negligence arising from a vehicle collision. The parents and children appealed.


OVERVIEW: Parents were injured in a vehicle collision when an employee was driving home from his employer's social event. The employee was intoxicated when the accident occurred. The parents and their children filed an action against the employer. The trial court granted summary judgment to the employer. Additionally, the court held that the employer had no duty to exercise care to control the employee's conduct in any respect once he left the social event and headed for home. Therefore, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment, which entered summary judgment in favor of the employer, was affirmed.

State v. Maldonado

967 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Hibbs v. Calcot, Ltd.


No. 1 CA-CV 88-453


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department T


166 Ariz. 210; 801 P.2d 445; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 196; 61 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



May 22, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 9, 1990. Review Denied December 18, 1990. *


*  Cameron, J., of the Supreme Court, voted to grant review.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; Cause No. TA-799; The Honorable Norman D. Hall, Jr., Judge; The Honorable Jeffrey S. Cates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Arizona Department of Revenue (department) challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which classified appellee taxpayer's real and personal property to warehouse baled cotton as class four agricultural property and not as class three commercial or industrial property. The trial court granted summary judgment in the taxpayer's favor and denied the department's motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was an incorporated, non-profit cooperative association. The court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-176(F) overruled Yavapai County v. Wilkinson, 111 Ariz. 530, 534 P.2d 735 (1975), so the department was not collaterally estopped by its failure to appeal an earlier tax-year decision of the State Board of Tax Appeals, which found that the taxpayer had class four status. The court held that § 42-176(F) did not abrogate or limit the doctrine of collateral estoppel. The court found that the taxpayer's member-owners jointly devoted the property to their collective commercial use through the taxpayer instrumentality. The court concluded that the taxpayer, though organized as a non-profit entity, devoted its property to a commercial use, and this use determined the propriety of a class three commercial designation under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-162(A)(3). The court found that an affidavit and an attached table did not demonstrate that any properties used similarly to the taxpayer's had been designated as class four; therefore, the evidence failed to support its claim of discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court with directions to enter judgment for the department.

969 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burt


No. 2 CA-CR 90-0122-PR


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 191; 60 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 67



May 15, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. MOTIONS FOR RECONSIDERATION OR PETITIONS FOR REVIEW TO THE ARIZONA SUPREME COURT MAY BE PENDING. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE. As Corrected


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 15, 1990


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pinal County; Cause No. CR-11027; Honorable Edward L. Dawson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted and sentenced for escape. At trial, he had argued that his escape was justified because he was under duress of threats on his life. Petitioner sought post-conviction relief because the trial court gave a jury instruction on justification that was later declared unconstitutional. He appealed an order of the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona), which summarily dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The challenged jury instruction told the jury that it must find petitioner not guilty if the jury decided that his conduct was justified. After petitioner's conviction, the Arizona Supreme Court held that the giving of the instruction was fundamental error because the instruction could have been erroneously interpreted by the jury as shifting the burden of proof to a defendant. The trial court decided that the Arizona Supreme Court's holding did not require that petitioner be given a new trial, and the court agreed on appeal. The defense of duress was not specifically set forth in the statute defining escape, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2503, or in the section of the criminal code on justifications, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-401 et seq. Public policy considerations required a more stringent standard of duress when applied to the crime of escape. Petitioner had the burden to establish duress, an affirmative defense, by a preponderance of the evidence. The court found that the giving of the instruction was not fundamental error. Any objection to the instruction was waived by petitioner's failure to raise it on direct appeal. Further, any error related to the instruction was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court granted review of the trial court's order, which had dismissed the petition. The court, however, denied post-conviction relief.

State v. Leyva


No. 2 CA-CR 89-0572


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


165 Ariz. 269; 798 P.2d 407; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 165; 60 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 61



May 10, 1990

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of a trial court (Arizona),which convicted defendant, after a guilty plea, of possession for sale of marijuana in excess of eight pounds, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3405(A)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested in possession of 232 pounds of marijuana. Defendant was indicted on one count each of possession of marijuana, possession of marijuana for sale, and transportation of marijuana for sale. Pursuant to a plea agreement, defendant entered a plea of guilty to possession for sale of marijuana in excess of eight pounds. 971 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burt


No. 2 CA-CR 90-0122-PR


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 172; 60 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 48



May 8, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied January 15, 1990.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of judgment of the trial court (Arizona), which denied his post-conviction petition for relief.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, the inmate was convicted of escape from a correctional facility in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2503. He admitted two prior felony convictions and was sentenced to the presumptive term of five years' imprisonment, to be served consecutively with the sentences he was serving. The trial court denied his post-conviction petition or relief. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court declined to adopt as a constitutional imperative that the State had to disprove beyond a reasonable doubt every fact constituting affirmative defenses related to the culpability of the accused. Due process required the prosecution to prove beyond a reasonable doubt all of the elements included in the definition of the offense of which a defendant was charged. Proof of the nonexistence of all affirmative defenses was not constitutionally required. The defense of duress was, in actuality, an affirmative defense. It was not an element of the crime of escape as defined in § 13-2503. Because there was no fundamental error, any objection to the duress instruction was waived by the inmate's failure to raise it on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

972 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stidham


No. 1 CA-CR 88-1082


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


164 Ariz. 145; 791 P.2d 671; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 159; 59 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



May 1, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 9, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR 88-01978, The Honorable Rebecca A. Albrecht, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which found him guilty in a jury trial on a charge of driving under the influence (DUI) while his license was suspended, cancelled, revoked or refused and sentenced him to a term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was pulled over by a police officer who observed his poor driving. Defendant produced an identification-only card, admitted to having consumed one drink, and was arrested. Defendant was charged with DUI while his license was suspended, cancelled, revoked or refused, and he filed a motion for a directed verdict on the ground that there was no evidence that his license had been revoked. The trial court denied the motion, and the jury found defendant guilty. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant's license was revoked because a record of his moving violations that was introduced at trial showed a revocation, and there was no indication on the document that the license had been reissued. The court also pointed to the evidence that defendant was only able to produce an identification-only card when he was stopped by the police officer rather than a driver's license. A revocation was of indefinite duration, and because of that the court held that the jury could have reasonably inferred that the revocation remained in effect when the offense occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant on a charge of DUI while his license was suspended, cancelled, revoked or refused and denied his motion for a directed verdict.

Sunpower of Arizona v. Arizona State Registrar of Contractors


No. 2 CA-CV 89-0232


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


166 Ariz. 437; 803 P.2d 430; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 153; 59 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



April 26, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 13, 1990. Review Denied January 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. 257123, Honorable Michael J. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant seller sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) which affirmed an order by appellee state registrar of contractors that the seller remove from the residences of appellee purchasers solar equipment that the seller had installed and to return to the purchasers the money that they expended for the purchase and installation of the equipment.


OVERVIEW: The superior court upheld the state registrar of contractors' (registrar) order which required a licensed seller to remove from the purchasers' residences solar equipment that it had sold and installed, and to return the purchasers' money. The seller argued that the registrar's order exceeded its regulatory authority, that it was a violation of the separation of powers, that one purchaser's complaint was barred by the statute of limitations, and that review was barred because the transcript was incomplete. Upon affirming the order, the court held:(1) that the registrar's order was a restitutionary remedy that was contemplated by the legislature as part of its authority to take appropriate disciplinary action against those who violated licensing standards; (2) that the administrative award of damages was constitutional because the seller's due process procedural rights were protected, prohibited conduct was well defined by the governing statute, and judicial review was available; (3) that there was no abuse of discretion in permitting the purchaser's claim to go forward, and (4) that there was substantial evidence in the available transcript to enable a meaningful judicial review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order which upheld the order of the registrar that required a seller to return equipment installation and purchase money to the purchasers.

Rowe Int'l v. Arizona Dep't of Revenue


No. 1 CA-TX 89-002


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department T


165 Ariz. 122; 796 P.2d 924; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 133; 58 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 40



April 10, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 25, 1990. Review Denied September 25, 1990.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant revenue department sought review of a judgment from the tax department of the superior court (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee taxpayer with respect to the taxpayer's action for a refund of transaction privilege taxes calculated on its sales of video game machines.


OVERVIEW: The revenue department issued transaction privilege tax assessments to the taxpayer calculated on the taxpayer's sales of video games to video arcades and other businesses. The taxpayer paid the amount owed under protest and then brought an action for recovery of the amount paid pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-124(B)(2). The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted the taxpayer's motion for summary judgment and ordered a refund of the amount paid under protest. The trial court denied the revenue department's motion for summary judgment and its motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case. The court held that video game machines were "games" under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-1314(A)(1). The court determined that the taxpayer had therefore made "sales at retail" and was liable for the transaction privilege tax under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-1312(A). The court also found that the taxation of the proceeds from video game machines under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-1314(A)(1) did not constitute double taxation and did not violate Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 13 or U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had granted summary judgment in favor of the taxpayer with respect to its action for a refund of transaction privilege taxes. The court remanded the case for proceedings consistent with its opinion.

 

975 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Barlow v. Blackburn


No. 1 CA-CIV 88-529


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


165 Ariz. 351; 798 P.2d 1360; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 126; 57 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 70



April 3, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 31, 1990. *


*  Gordon, C.J., and Cameron, J., of the Supreme Court, recused themselves and did not participate in the determination of this matter; Fernandez, C.J., and Livermore, V.C.J., of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, sat in their stead.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state Law Enforcement Officer Advisory Council (council) challenged the judgment of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which enjoined it from conducting administrative proceedings to consider revoking or suspending the certified law enforcement officer status of appellee deputy town marshal (deputy).


OVERVIEW: Deputy was sworn to uphold the federal and state constitutions and was a member of the Fundamentalist Mormon Church and practiced polygamy. Council voted to consider revoking his status as a certified law enforcement officer and deputy filed a special action in the trial court, requesting that the court dismiss the administrative proceedings and award him his attorney's fees and costs. The trial court found that the council did not show a compelling state interest sufficient to outweigh deputy's first amendment right to religious freedom and ordered it to dismiss the administrative proceedings. Council appealed and the court reversed. The court held that council was permitted to proceed with the administrative hearing and that, by practicing polygamy, deputy chose to disregard the state's proscription of polygamy and his oath to uphold the constitution. The court held that deputy's conduct may have been sufficient for council to conclude that he did not meet the reasonable minimum qualifications required for peace officer certification. The court held that the state's interest in enforcing its certification requirements overrode deputy's interest in the practice of polygamy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and held that the council was permitted to proceed with the administrative hearing to consider revoking or suspending the certified law enforcement officer status of the deputy.

 

976 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dykes


No. 1 CA-CR 88-1248


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


163 Ariz. 581; 789 P.2d 1082; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 117; 57 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 62



March 29, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-88-03244, The Honorable Armando de Leon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) for possession of a dangerous drug, a class four felony or class one misdemeanor under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3407(B)(1) (1988). Defendant challenged that portion of § 13-3407(B)(1) that conditioned the redesignation of the offense as a misdemeanor on a "motion of the State," arguing violation of the separation of powers and of Ariz. Const. art. III.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was indicted, she pled not guilty and proceeded to jury trial. At trial, the State presented evidence that the police had discovered a syringe and a small plastic bag containing a white powdery substance in defendant's purse during an inventory search following her arrest. After conviction but prior to sentencing, defendant moved for a new trial on the grounds of newly discovered evidence. The trial court denied the motion, and the matter was set for a mitigation hearing. Defendant then filed a motion invoking § 13-3407(B) and asking the trial court to designate the conviction a misdemeanor. The State had not filed the statutorily required motion, but defendant contended that requiring the State's motion was unconstitutional, claiming that designation of the offense as a felony or misdemeanor was an exclusively judicial function. The trial court denied defendant's motion to redesignate and sentenced her as for a felony, but the court reversed. Because § 13-3407(B) limited the exclusively judicial function of sentencing, it was unconstitutional under Ariz. Const. art. III. Further, the offensive portion of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3407(B) (1988) was severable.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the conviction as a class four felony and the sentence imposed thereon. The matter was remanded for the trial court to consider whether the nature and circumstances of the offense warranted the entry of the judgment of conviction as a class one misdemeanor rather than as a class four felony.

 

977 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gendron


No. 1 CA-CR 88-1236


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


166 Ariz. 562; 804 P.2d 95; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 120; 57 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 65



March 29, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 10, 1990. Review Granted in Part and Denied in Part February 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-88-05704, The Honorable I. Sylvan Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for unlawful flight from a law enforcement vehicle, aggravated assault, and criminal damage arguing that the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) erred by not allowing defendant to present a justification defense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions of unlawful flight from a law enforcement vehicle, aggravated assault, and criminal damage. Defendant was observed committing a traffic violation and was asked to stop his motorcycle. After defendant stopped, after his initial flee, an officer told him that he would blow him away. Defendant argued that the court erred by not allowing defendant to present a justification defense to the jury for the aggravated assault and criminal damage charges arguing that he fled from the officer the second time because he feared for his life based on the officer's comment. When threatened by inappropriate deadly force by an officer a suspect like defendant could fear its use and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-404(B) created a limited right for members of the public to resist excessive police force. The instructions requested by defendant should have been given regarding defendant's right to take action to avoid excessive force; therefore, the aggravated assault and criminal damage convictions were reversed, however, the unlawful flight conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for aggravated assault and criminal damage were reversed and remanded because the court should have allowed defendant to give the requested justification instructions, however, defendant's conviction for unlawful flight was affirmed because defendant fled from the officer prior to the officer making the illegal comment about deadly force.

 

978 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lammie


No. 1 CA-CR 89-216


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


164 Ariz. 377; 793 P.2d 134; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 121; 57 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 58



March 29, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 3, 1990. *


*  Corcoran, J., of the Supreme Court, was not present and did not participate in the determination of this matter.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR 88-08357, The Honorable Michael O. Wilkinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which ordered him to register as a sex offender pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3821 after he had pled guilty to two counts of attempted sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: After defendant pled guilty to two counts of attempted sexual assault, the trial court ordered defendant to register as a sex offender pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3821. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found that § 13-3821 was intended to apply to attempted offenses because an attempt to commit an offense was more than preparatory, it was a punishable segment of the crime intended. The court noted defendant was not convicted of committing an attempt, but rather he was convicted of attempting to commit the substantive offense of sexual assault. The court held that § 13-3821 was not vague where both statutory and case law recognized that an attempt to commit an offense is a lesser-included offense within the completed offense. The court concluded the sentence requiring defendant for his lifetime to register as a sex offender was not excessive punishment where the crimes committed were egregious, the sentence was not disproportionate to other sentences imposed, and other jurisdictions had similar sex offender statutes. The court noted defendant had sexually assaulted a mother and her 17-year-old daughter in their own home after he gained entry by using a knife.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that ordered defendant to register as a sex offender.

Dano v. Collins


No. 1 CA-CV 88-420


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


166 Ariz. 322; 802 P.2d 1021; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 102; 57 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



March 27, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 9, 1990. Review Granted January 15, 1991. Review Denied April 16, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CV 87-26850, The Honorable Daniel E. Nastro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment to appellees county attorney and county sheriff and denied the individuals' request for a declaratory judgment. The individuals contended that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(A)(1), (2), the state's concealed weapons ban, was void because it violated the state constitution.


OVERVIEW: Two individuals filed suit against a county attorney and county sheriff seeking a declaratory judgment holding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(A)(1), (2), which prohibited the carrying of concealed weapons, were unconstitutional as violative of Ariz. Const. art. II, § 26. When the lower court granted summary judgment, the individuals sought review. The court affirmed and found that (1) the Arizona constitutional provision did not grant an absolute right to bear arms in all situations, (2) the requirement that arms be borne openly did not impair the right to self-defense and in fact had a reasonable purpose of protecting the public by preventing persons from having deadly weapons on hand of which the public was unaware, (3) the right to keep and bear arms and the police power to regulate in order to protect the health, safety, and welfare of citizens had to be balanced, and (4) § 13-3012(A)(1), (2) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's grant of summary judgment to the county attorney and county sheriff in the individuals' declaratory judgment action challenging the state's concealed weapons ban on constitutional grounds.

 

980 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re 1632 N. Santa Rita


No. 2 CA-CV 89-0202


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


166 Ariz. 197; 801 P.2d 432; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 89; 56 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 43



March 13, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 19, 1990. Review Denied December 18, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. 255930, honorable Robert B. Buchanan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner challenged the order of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which awarded judgment to appellee state, in the state's forfeiture action under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314 that arose following the homeowner's agreement to plead guilty to unlawful possession of marijuana, and declared that the homestead exemption filed by the homeowner under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-1101(A) was null and void.


OVERVIEW: Following the execution of a search warrant, the homeowner was arrested for growing marijuana in his home, charged with unlawful possession of marijuana, unlawful possession of marijuana for sale, and unlawful production of marijuana, and pled guilty to unlawful possession of marijuana. The state brought a forfeiture action under § 13-2314 and stipulated with the mortgage holder to protect the mortgage holder's interest. After a hearing, the superior court declared the homeowner's homestead exemption null and void, and ordered the forfeiture. The homeowner appealed. The court affirmed. The court rejected the double punishment argument of the homeowner because the forfeiture provision of § 13-2314 served the purpose of removing from the homeowner the means to commit further offenses and helped the state defray expenses of investigation and prosecution, which made the provision remedial. The state's forfeiture complaint was not required to allege any injury from the predicate offense or to prove any injury. The state had shown that the residence was used to facilitate the unlawful possession of marijuana, which was all § 13-2314 required for the forfeiture of the entire property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the superior court, which awarded judgment to the state in the forfeiture action and held the homeowner's exemption was null and void.

 

981 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harrison


No. 1 CA-CR 89-007


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


164 Ariz. 316; 792 P.2d 779; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 58; 55 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 44



March 1, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 28, 1990. Review Denied June 26, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. LCA-88-01138, The Honorable Barry G. Silverman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which affirmed defendant's convictions in a municipal court for running a red light, failing to provide proof of insurance, and driving a motor vehicle in violation of a license restriction requiring him to wear eye glasses. Defendant argued that he was unconstitutionally deprived of a trial by jury and that the sentences imposed were cruel and unusual.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with traffic violations. The charges were consolidated and tried before a municipal court judge. Defendant was found guilty and fined, and his license was suspended. The convictions were affirmed on appeal to the superior court, and defendant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that defendant's constitutional rights were not violated. Defendant failed to meet any criteria creating a right to a jury. Defendant's fines totalled less than $ 500, and the license suspension was insufficient added punishment to make the crimes serious. Driving was a privilege, and the loss of the privilege was not as serious as the loss of a right. License suspension was a civil sanction, not a criminal sanction, and defendant's maximum exposure to a prison sentence was insufficient to trigger a jury. Traffic violations in themselves did not brand a person as depraved and inherently base or reflect on personal values. None of defendant's crimes existed at common law, and defendant did not timely request a jury trial. Requiring defendant to prove financial responsibility was not cruel and unusual punishment, and the sentences imposed were well within the prescribed legal limits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

983 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Whitaker


Nos. 1 CA-CR 88-941, 1 CA-CR 88-942


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


164 Ariz. 359; 793 P.2d 116; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 32; 54 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



February 15, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 10, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause Nos. CR-88-03571 and CR-87-08574, The Honorable Jeffrey S. Cates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, (Arizona), which held that acts of public sexual indecency could not be committed in a home and dismissed the charges brought against defendant.


OVERVIEW: The state appealed the trial court's ruling that an act of public sexual indecency could not be committed in a home and its dismissal of the charges brought against defendant. On review, the court disagreed. The legislature referred to the crime as public sexual indecency. Yet, the statute tracked the indecent exposure language of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1402, in that another person must be present and that defendant must be reckless about whether such person, as a reasonable person, would be offended or alarmed by the act. It was therefore clear that public sexual indecency under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1403 could be committed in one's own home. It was a question of fact whether an actor by his conduct knowingly exposed his activity to another and was reckless about whether such other would reasonably be offended or alarmed by such activity. Any constitutional considerations concerning the right to privacy and consensual acts in the home were guarded by the standard of reasonableness and the requirement that the actor must be reckless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that dismissed the charges and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Coats


No. 1 CA-CR 88-834


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


165 Ariz. 154; 797 P.2d 693; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 35; 54 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



February 15, 1990 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of a trial court (Arizona), which convicted him of possession of marijuana for sale, with one prior felony conviction, and which sentenced him to imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: A woman accompanied her husband to defendant's trailer, where the husband purchased marijuana. The woman subsequently informed the police, and an officer submitted an affidavit for a search warrant based on the information provided by the woman. A search warrant was issued and executed, and marijuana, firearms, and other items were seized. The trial court found that the warrant was based upon stale information. However, the trial court applied Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3925, the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule, and denied defendant's motion to suppress. On appeal, the court held that § 13-3925 did not violate the rule-making authority of the Arizona Supreme Court or the constitutional principles of separation of powers. The court further held that the trial did not abuse its discretion in finding that the officers relied on the warrant in good faith. Defendant failed to specify why the officer's affidavit was insufficient under the totality of the circumstances. Moreover, citizen informants were presumed to be reliable. Although the affidavit mistakenly identified the name of the trailer park where defendant lived, it was sufficient to identify the place to be searched.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Sherrill v. Arizona DOT


No. 1 CA-CV 88-591


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


164 Ariz. 442; 793 P.2d 1109; 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 25; 53 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



February 8, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted July 10, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CV 88-15498, The Honorable Daniel E. Nastro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who pleaded guilty to a charge of driving while intoxicated, appealed the suspension of her driver's license by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) on the grounds that she did not refuse to submit to a breathalyzer test.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving while intoxicated and agreed to submit to a breathalyzer test. On two tries the machine indicated that it received a deficient sample due to defendant's failure to blow hard enough; the second sample, however, yielded a blood alcohol content (BAC) above the legal limit. A Motor Vehicle Division hearing officer suspended defendant's driver's license pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-691, and the superior court affirmed. On appeal, defendant contended that her license should not have been suspended because the purpose of § 28-691 was satisfied both by her second test result and by her admission before taking the test that she was drunk and further that the law required that her refusal be willful. The court affirmed the suspension. It held that the hearing officer did not abuse his discretion in finding that defendant's failure to successfully complete the breathalyzer test constituted refusal. The court reasoned that compliance with § 28-691 was necessary even though the test provided prosecutors with a BAC reading high enough to demonstrate her intoxication and further that refusal to take the test did not need to be evidenced by a willful act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the suspension of defendant's driver's license.

Admin. Code § R4-19-403(1) (1986) through using or permitting the use of blank forms as standing orders.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that no nursing statutes or regulations void for vagueness, no unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority, no bias or selective enforcement, and no double jeopardy, appellant nurses lacked standing to complain of illegal search or seizure or to invoke the doctor-patient privilege, the exclusionary rule did not per se apply to administrative hearings, and appellee Arizona State Board of Nursing did not violate the open meeting statute. The finding of a failure to properly supervise tank room attendants was vacated and all other findings were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and vacated in part. The court vacated the finding that one appellant nurse failed to properly supervise tank room attendants and affirmed all other findings against appellant nurses. Appellee Arizona State Board of Nursing's decisions were not arbitrary or capricious, and there was no abuse of discretion or due process violations.

State v. Waits


No. 2 CA-CR 89-0510


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


163 Ariz. 216; 786 P.2d 1067; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 385; 52 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



December 12, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Redesignated as Opinion and Publication Ordered January 24, 1990. Review Denied March 6, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY, Cause No. CR 88-11162, Honorable Kenneth L. Fields, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of the sale of a narcotic drug, a class 2 felony, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3408, with two prior felony convictions and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence of life imprisonment. On review, the court affirmed and held that that the trial court did not err in refusing to admit a departmental report of the crime in question. The report was irrelevant and defendant was not able to demonstrate how he was prejudiced by the court's refusal to admit it. Moreover, defendant's sentence did not violate the Eighth Amendment of the United States Constitution and Ariz. Const. art 2, § 15. The harshness of the penalty, life imprisonment, could not be considered solely in relation to the sale of a $ 20 rock of cocaine. Recognition was given to the fact that defendant was a recidivist and that defendant committed the offense while on probation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the sale of a narcotic drug and his life imprisonment sentence.

 

993 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Prescott v. Chino Valley


No. 1 CA-CIV 9754


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


163 Ariz. 608; 790 P.2d 263; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 304; 47 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 63



November 14, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 8, 1990. Cross-Petition for Review Granted in Part and Denied in Part May 8, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County, Cause No. C-46161, The Honorable Allen G. Minker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant and appellee, both municipalities, challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which, in a decision determining the validity of appellee's use tax, upheld the imposition of appellant's tax upon appellee, sustained appellee's claim that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-1452 required reference of the case to the Board of Tax Appeals for resolution, and denied appellant's claim for attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellee adopted a one percent sales tax and directed the town's attorney to prepare an ordinance. Appellant refused to pay the tax and sought a declaratory judgment invalidating the tax. Although the court found that at least one of the executive sessions was improper, it affirmed in part and reversed in part rejecting appellant's claim that the tax should be voided for open meeting law violations.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellee's request for attorneys' fees, and upheld the validity of appellant's transaction privilege tax.

 

994 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lichon


No. 1 CA-CR 88-158


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


163 Ariz. 186; 786 P.2d 1037; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 293; 46 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



November 2, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 2, November 3 and November 20, 1989. Review Denied March 6, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-162979, The Honorable Peter T. D'Angelo, Judge, The Honorable John Foreman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of one count of renting an obscene item in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3502 (Supp.1988).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of renting an obscene item, and on appeal the court affirmed because (1) though the prosecutor was presumptuous in telling the jury they could determine the statewide standard from what they knew of their own community when the judge had refused his instruction to that effect, it was not a misstatement of the law because a juror could consider the views of the average person in the juror's community in arriving at an assessment of the statewide standard; (2) the expert witness's testimony regarding the harm caused by pornography was directed at the effect of pornography on children in general and did not violate the order in limine; (3) the judge's statement that if he were the trier of fact he would not find the movies obscene was merely a personal observation of no legal significance; (4) in view of the fact that the jury had an absolute right to review the videotapes at will, it was not unduly suggestive to allow a television monitor and VCR be placed in the jury room during deliberations; and, (5) the mere existence of a fine provision was not an unconstitutional prior restraint..


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of one count of renting an obscene item.

 

995 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Cochise County v. Borowiec


No. 2 CA-SA 89-0113


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


162 Ariz. 192; 781 P.2d 1379; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 281; 46 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



October 24, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] SPECIAL ACTION PROCEEDINGS, RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county sought special action relief from an order of respondent judge for the Superior Court of the County of Cochise (Arizona) (judge), which granted a motion for change of venue filed by real parties in interest, state agency and its director, in the county's action brought pursuant to the Administrative Review Act for judicial review of an administrative decision.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the judge erroneously concluded that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-822(B) applied because the county's action was not an action against the state as contemplated by the provision. The court held that a reasonable construction of § 12-822(B) showed that it was not intended to include actions seeking judicial review of administrative rulings, especially in light of a separate article that dealt specifically with such proceedings. The court found that the judge also erred in considering Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-401(16), which required that actions against public officers be brought in the county in which they held office. Although the director was a public officer, an administrative appeal was not an action against a public officer just as it was not an action against the state. Additionally, the more specific provision of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-905 was controlling and the action was properly brought under its requirements. The court vacated the order that granted the venue change because the judge exceeded his legal authority.


OUTCOME: The court granted special action relief sought by the county by vacating the judge's order that granted a change of venue.

 

996 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Benjamin v. Arizona Dep't of Revenue


No. 2 CA-CV 89-0103


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


163 Ariz. 182; 786 P.2d 1033; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 276; 45 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 44



October 19, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 26, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY, Cause No. C-586227, Honorable William P. Sargeant III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff disabled veterans appealed an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which held that statutory tax exemptions for veterans were invalid because the residency qualifications of Ariz. Const. art. IX, §§ 2(2), (3) were not severable and the residency requirements violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: The disabled veterans were denied a veterans' tax exemption because they were not residents of Arizona before September 1, 1945, or for a total of four years prior to their induction or enlistment in the United States Armed Forces. They filed suit to determine if the residence requirements were severable. The trial court found that the requirements were not severable and that the tax exemptions were invalid because the residency requirements violated the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The veterans appealed, contending that the residency requirements were severable. The court disagreed, holding that the requirements could not be severed from the remaining provisions for veterans' exemption because the remaining provisions would no longer reflect the intent of the voters who approved the constitutional amendment by referendum. It was apparent that the voters would not have voted in favor of the veterans' tax exemptions without the restrictive residency requirements contained in each amendment. In determining that question, the court considered the context, the language, the subject matter, the background, the effects and consequences, and the purpose of the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which had held that statutory tax exemptions for veterans based on residency were invalid.

 

997 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Zeigler v. Kirschner


No. 1 CA-CV 88-231


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


162 Ariz. 77; 781 P.2d 54; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 266; 44 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



October 5, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CV-87-27361, The Honorable Robert W. Pickrell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff medical benefit applicants brought an action against defendant director of state health care system, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief and restitution pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and state law. The director sought dismissal of the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and failure to state a claim. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) granted the director's motion. The applicants challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issues were whether the director was protected by immunity and whether the applicants' failure to exhaust state administrative remedies barred their claims. The court held that: (1) the defense of qualified immunity based on the director's objectively reasonable reliance on clearly established law was a personal one that was unavailable to him because the applicants had proceeded against the director in his official capacity; (2) the applicants were not required to exhaust state administrative remedies before bringing their 42 U.S.C.S. 1983 claims in federal court; (3) the applicants' § 1983 claims were not subject to dismissal by virtue of the absolute or qualified executive immunity created by Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-820.01, 12-820.02; (4) the immunity provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820 et seq. and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1802 did not apply to the applicants' claims for injunctive and declaratory relief; (5) the applicants' state law claims for monetary relief were barred by the applicants' failure to exhaust their state administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal to the extent that the applicants' state law claims against the director sought monetary relief. In all other aspects, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

998 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


JV-111701 v. Superior Court


No. 1 CA-SA 88-259


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


163 Ariz. 147; 786 P.2d 998; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 264; 44 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



October 5, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 15, 1989. Review Denied February 26, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action Review in the Matter of Maricopa County Juvenile Action JV-111701, The Honorable Thomas Jacobs, Judge, JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED IN PARTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juvenile filed a special action against defendant state challenging the constitutionality of Ariz. R. P. Juv. Ct. 3 (Rule 3) after he was detained pending the adjudication of a juvenile proceeding in the Maricopa County Juvenile Court (Arizona).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was arrested for delinquent behavior. He was detained for five days before the trial court advised him of the charges against him and held an initial hearing. At the hearing, the trial court found that there was reasonable cause to continue the juvenile's detention pending adjudication. The juvenile filed a special action challenging the constitutionality of Rule 3. On review, the court determined that Rule 3 required the state to take the juvenile before a magistrate within 24 hours of arrest, but that Rule 3(d) excluded Saturdays, Sundays, and holidays from the 24-hour period. The court held that Rule 3(d) was unconstitutional on equal protection grounds because it treated juvenile offenders differently than adult offenders, and there was no rational basis for the disparate treatment. The court ruled that the "reasonable cause" standard of proof imposed by Rule 3(b) to determine whether a juvenile should be detained pending adjudication was not a violation of the juvenile's due process rights because "reasonable cause" meant "probable cause." The court held that the trial court was not constitutionally required to make specific findings of fact pursuant to Rule 3(b).


OUTCOME: The court held that the subsection of the juvenile rule excluding Saturdays, Sundays and holidays from the 24-hour period that juveniles could be detained without being taken before a magistrate was unconstitutional. The court held that the remainder of the rule was constitutional. The court denied relief to the juvenile because the matter had become moot.

 

999 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Emond


No. 1 CA-CR 88-389


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


163 Ariz. 138; 786 P.2d 989; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 254; 44 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



September 26, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended October 4, 1989. Review Denied March 6, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-87-11101, The Honorable Joel Erik Thompson, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), that dismissed the indictment against defendant for sexual exploitation of a minor and dangerous crimes against children in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3553, class two felonies, for possessing child pornography.


OVERVIEW: A consensual search of defendant's home resulted in his indictment for possession of child pornography pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3553. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the case with prejudice alleging that the portion of the statute prohibiting the mere possession of visual or print medium in which minors were engaged in sexual conduct was unconstitutional under the First and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss. On appeal by the state, the court reversed and remanded for trial because it found that the statute was constitutional. The court weighed defendant's First Amendment rights, but concluded that the state's interest in protecting its minor citizens overrode defendant's First Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that dismissed the indictment against defendant for possession of child pornography, and remanded the case with directions to reinstate the indictment.

 

1000 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Cota-Robles v. Tucson


No. 2 CA-CV 89-0059


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


163 Ariz. 143; 786 P.2d 994; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 258; 44 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 37



September 26, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 26, 1990. *


*  Feldman, V.C.J., of the Supreme Court, recused himself and did not participate in the determination of this matter.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. 253047, Honorable Allen G. Minker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, voters and concerned citizens (citizens), sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which granted summary judgments against the citizens in their action seeking to compel appellees, the mayor, city council, and city, to call a referendum election on the alignment of a proposed parkway.


OVERVIEW: The citizens filed a complaint against the mayor, city council, and city, seeking an order requiring the city council to hold a referendum election on the proposed alignment of the parkway pursuant to the Neighborhood Protection Amendment to Tucson, Ariz., Charter, ch. XXV, § 13. The state and a group of individual voters intervened. The trial court granted appellees' motions for summary judgment. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that Arizona law preempted the city from legislating on the matter because: (1) the alignment and construction of the parkway was a subject of statewide concern where the parkway lay both inside and outside a city, the parkway was to be funded by state highway revenue user funds, and the state transportation board established the parkway as a state route and approved the alignment before the Neighborhood Protection Amendment became effective; (2) state legislation appropriated the subject under the provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 28-104, -1801(9), -106(B); and (3) once the parkway was established as a state route, the city lost authority to legislate on the matter and the city voters lost authority to seek a referendum election on it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgments against the citizens in their action seeking to compel appellees to call a referendum election on the alignment of the proposed parkway.
